Ubuntu Fundamentals Package Management Learning Objectives By the end of this lesson, you will be able to: Access the repository Apply the apt/apt-get command Install PPA Repository The repository list can be found in the /etc/apt/sources.list directory of Ubuntu OS. A repository can be defined as a central storage area for all software packages. Types of Repositories • Main • Restricted • Universe • Multiverse The four types of repositories to download software from are: This is a community-supported open-source software. Canonical will not support this in terms of providing updates for this release software. Types of Repositories Main Restricted Universe Multiverse This is the default repository and all the packages in this are free. This is a closed-source software supported by Canonical for a price till the end of the life cycle of the release. This includes closed-source software, such as adobe flash. It also includes open-source software with some restrictions. Repository Access To access a repository, the system should be connected to the internet. • Select the required repository from the Ubuntu software center console along with the source location. Repository Access • In the next tab, add repository URL into the file /etc/apt/sources.list. • To check for updates and new releases, use the command $ sudo apt-get update. Software with .deb Extension • In case the software packages are released in a .deb file format, there is no need to use the repository commands such as apt or apt-get. • Use the command $ sudo dpkg -i <package name> to directly install the software, and if there are any dependency failures, use the command $ sudo apt-get install -f. Introduction to apt/apt-get Command • The apt command is a CLI command used to download, install, and remove the software packages. • The earlier version of apt command was called apt-get command. • All new releases of Ubuntu have the apt command. Introduction to apt/apt-get Command • Install packages with the syntax: $ sudo apt install <app-package1> <app-package2> • Uninstall packages with the syntax: $ sudo apt <app-package1> • Remove orphaned application packages automatically. o While installing the packages, apt resolves the dependencies automatically. o Similarly, while uninstalling, it removes the critical dependencies of the application automatically. It is done by the command $ sudo apt autoremove. • Search packages with the syntax: $ sudo apt search <keyword>. Some of the frequently used apt commands are to: Update vs. Upgrade Update will check the availability of new versions of a given package, whereas upgrade will update the packages to a new version. Introduction to PPA • Personal Package Archives (PPA) are software packages that are released by the developer without any testing for publishing in the repository. • These are published separately and can be installed from the software center. Key Takeaways Repository can be defined as a central storage area for all software packages. $ sudo apt-get update command is used to check for updates to the software on the system. The apt command is a command-line interface command used to download, install, and remove the software packages. PPA or Personal Package Archives are software packages released by the developer without testing. Knowledge Check Knowledge Check A. B. C. Lesson 1-10 Network Services and Applications Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ● Describe a network controller ● Explain the use of a VPN and the three types of VPN ● Describe the IPsec, GRE, SSL VPN, and PTP/PPTP VPN protocols ● Discuss the difference between TACACS and RADIUS authentication protocols ● Explain Remote Access Services ● Describe the networking challenges of unified voice services After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • The interface between a device and a network is called a Network Controller. • In a computer this is often referred to as the Network Interface Card or NIC. • Common wired NICs use the Ethernet standard and support 10Mbps, 100Mbps, or 1000Mbps (1Gbps) connections. • The interface between a device and a wireless network is sometimes referred to as a Wireless Network Interface Controller or WNIC. Network Controllers Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. VPN • A Virtual Private Network (VPN) establishes a secure, private connection between two devices or two networks, through a public, unsecured network. • Example: An employee who needs access to sensitive company information while traveling may use a VPN to securely connect their laptop to the company network via the Internet. • VPNs may be used for: • Security • Avoiding censorship or filters by connecting to an outside host • Hiding one’s identity by connecting through proxy servers. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Three Types of VPNs • There are three types of VPNs-- • Host-to-Host: One device connects securely to another device • Host-to-Site: One device connects securely to another network, such as a traveling employee establishing a VPN back to their office network. • Site-to-Site: Two or more networks connected via VPN, functioning as if they are the same network. • Site-to-Site VPN connections are usually established by the routers or firewalls at each location. This is a popular solution for companies with more than one physical location, and need to share data as if they are on the same network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. VPN Protocols • VPNs use specific protocols to establish the connection and route traffic through the VPN. • Because VPN connections are referred to as “Tunnels” these are often referred to as “tunneling protocols”. • IPsec – Internet Protocol Security, authenticates and encrypts IP packets at the Network Layer of the OSI model • GRE – Generic Routing Encapsulation, encapsulates many network protocols into one tunnel. • SSL VPN – Secure Sockets Layer, a popular Internet encryption protocol, can be used to create a VPN • PTP/PPTP – Point-to-Point Tunneling Protocol is an older VPN method combining GRE with PPP (Point to Point Protocol, also called PTP) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Authentication Protocols • Security is paramount on any network, so services must be designated to handle user authentication, authorization, and accounting (AAA). Two popular authentication protocols are: • RADIUS – Remote Authentication Dial-In User Service, the most popular AAA protocol used by ISPs, servers, firewalls, etc. • TACACS – Terminal Access Controller Access-Control Systems, an old AAA developed in 1984 and generally superseded by RADIUS or by TACACS+, an enhanced version of TACACS created by Cisco. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Remote Access Service (RAS) • Remote Access Service (RAS) is a general term, referring to any combination of hardware and software which allows a user to remotely access a computer. • Originally used with Windows NT which had built-in remote access tools called RAS and allowed remote access via a telephone modem. • Today, RAS can refer to Windows’ built-in services such as Remote Desktop as well as 3rd party services, like: LogMeIn, TeamViewer, and DameWare. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Web Services • Web Services are communication channels over the Internet (or, less often, a company’s internal intranet). • Web services communicate using languages such as XML, REST, and SOAP • Secure connections to Web Services are often made using HTTPS (Hypertext Transfer Protocol Secure) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Unified Voice Services • Networks carry more than just data today – VoIP phone systems, video streaming, videoconferencing, and instant message systems represent a new challenge for network designers and troubleshooters. • Taken together these voice, video, and messaging systems are referred to as Unified Voice Services. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Challenges with Unified Voice Services, Part 1 • Two issues must be addressed to ensure a good user experience using Unified Voice Services: 1. Latency – latency refers to the delay in delivering packets between nodes. In data transfer occasional latency is not a problem, but in voice communication latency can distort or garble voice and video streams or prevent communication altogether. Implementing the QoS protocol as a method to prioritize packets can help to address latency issues. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Challenges with Unified Voice Services, Part 2 2. Bandwidth – video streaming and videoconferencing can use considerably more bandwidth than normal data transfer. Increasing network bandwidth capacity (by using faster switches and routers or upgrading to a faster WAN connection) can address bandwidth concerns. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The interface between a device and a network is called a _________. 1 port protocol network controller server Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Establishing a secure, private connection between two devices can be done with a ______. 2 router WAN network controller VPN Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. A VPN can establish a secure, private connection between two devices. d. router WAN network controller VPN 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary ● The interface between a device and a network is called a Network Controller. ● A Virtual Private Network (VPN) establishes a secure, private connection between two devices or two networks, through a public, unsecured network. ● Four popular VPN protocols are IPsec, GRE, SSL VPN, and PTP/PPTP. ● RADIUS, the Remote Authentication Dial-In User Service, is the most popular AAA (Authentication, Authorization, and Accounting) protocol used by ISPs, servers, and firewalls. ● The two major networking challenges with unified voice services are bandwidth and latency. All rights reserved. 1-11 DHCP and DNS Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ● Describe the difference between static and dynamic IP addressing. ● Explain the following DHCP attributes: reservations, scopes, leases, and suffixes ● Describe the benefit of Network Address Translation (NAT) ● Define port forwarding ● Explain these attributes of DNS records: A records, MX records, AAAA records, CNAME, and PTR. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • To communicate properly on a TCP/IP network, a computer needs four things: • A unique IP Address like 192.168.1.95 to identify it on the network. • A Subnet mask like 255.255.255.0. This defines the scope of the local network – requests that fall within the subnet will be handled by the computer itself, not by a gateway. • A Gateway like 192.168.1.1. The computer will send any non-local network requests to this device. • One or more DNS Servers, like 8.8.8.8. These are servers that translate names, such as wikipedia.com, into IP addresses. IP Basics Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Static Addressing • All that information – IP, Subnet mask, Gateway, and DNS – could be manually assigned to each computer. • This can be referred to as having a Static IP • The picture to the right shows manual IP settings in Windows 7 • Using a static IP requires the administrator to keep track of each computer’s settings and ensure no duplicate IP addresses are issued. • If the gateway, DNS servers, or subnet change, each computer or device must be updated manually. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Dynamic Addressing • Almost all devices support DHCP, Dynamic Host Control Protocol • DHCP allows the device to receive an assigned IP address, as well as predefined subnet, gateway, and DNS information, from a DHCP Server – this is referred to as Dynamic addressing or Dynamic IP • DHCP Servers are often a Router or Server • Some devices can choose which information is assigned by DHCP and which is set manually – the image to the right shows the IP, subnet, and gateway set via DHCP and the DNS set manually on a Windows 7 computer Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • The DHCP specification has two functions – an address allocation mechanism, and a communication mechanism for requesting and receiving addresses. • When a DHCP-enabled device first connects to the network, it has no IP and no network information – all it has is its MAC address. • The device sends a special broadcast request over UDP, looking for a DHCP Server. The request includes the device’s hardware address and may include a specific requested IP address. • If a DHCP Server exists on the local network, it will respond with appropriate IP configuration information. If a specific IP was requested, the Server may or may not provide that IP address. How DHCP Works Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The DHCP Command Sequence DHCP Discover DHCP Offer DHCP Request DHCP Ack IP address request IP address offer IP address selection IP address acknowledgment DHCP Client DHCP Server 1 2 3 4 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The DHCP Server and Relaying • The DHCP Server is generally a router or server on the local network. • When a device requests a DHCP-supplied address, it does so by broadcasting on the local network. • In larger networks where the DHCP server may not be on the local network, a DHCP/BOOTP Relay Agent can be setup to forward DHCP requests to another network and relay DHCP responses back to the local network. • Cisco routers use the term IP Helper to refer to Relay Agents BOOTP is the predecessor to DHCP – it worked similarly but could not dynamically assign addresses. Relaying work the same in both, which is why it’s called a DHCP/BOOTP Relay Agent. ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DHCP Server Configuration The DHCP Server runs as an application on a Windows Server or similar network server, or runs as a function on a Router. Settings for the DHCP Server include: • Scopes – the sequential range of IP addresses the server can give out, also called the Address Pool • Leases – how long the IP assignment is good. Shorter leases mean an IP address won’t be wasted on devices that are no longer on the network, longer leases are less work for the DHCP server. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DHCP Options The following may also be provided by the DHCP Server: • Subnet mask – details the scope of the local network • Gateway – the default gateway for the local network • DNS Server(s) – the default DNS servers for network devices to use • Default Suffix(es) – the default suffix to add when users search a servername (for example, the suffix “ourcompany.local” would find “ftp.ourcompany.local” if a network device looks for “ftp”) • Reservations – reservations allow specific IP addresses to be reserved for specific machines on the network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. APIPA What happens if there’s no static IP information set, AND no DHCP? • On Windows devices, Automatic Private IP Addressing (APIPA) auto-configures the IP settings. • Starts at 169.254.0.1, up to 169.254.255.254 (IPv4) • Uses ARP to verify if IP is assigned elsewhere. • Also called link-local addressing Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Subnet, Gateway, and DNS • The Subnet mask IP setting determines the scope of the local network. A network device can communicate directly with any other network device on the same local network. • The Gateway handles any traffic which is NOT on the local network. So if a network device needs to communicate with another device which is not on the local network, it sends its request to the Gateway. • The DNS server translates network names – representing either local or remote machines – into IP addresses. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Let’s look at how a Windows computer handles name resolution. If a user tries to go to the website “microsoft.com”, the computer follows these steps: 1. Am I microsoft.com? If so, handle the request directly; if not, go to step 2. 2. Is microsoft.com in my Hosts File? If so, use the Hosts File listing to find the IP address for microsoft.com; if not, go to step 3. 3. Query the DNS server(s) to find an address for microsoft.com. If an address is found, use it; if not, go to step 4. 4. Use NetBIOS name resolution to identify the name. NetBIOS name resolution is specific to Microsoft machines on the local network. 5. If none of these produces a result, return an error. Name Resolution Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Hosts File • A Hosts file takes precedence over DNS. • Hosts file is a manually created lists of domain names and their associated IP addresses. • On Windows computers the file is usually c:\windows\system32\drivers\etc\lmhosts.sam Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DNS Let’s look at how the Domain Name System (DNS) works on the Internet: • A domain name, such as donutfiesta.com, is registered with a domain name registrar. As part of the domain name registration, at least one (and usually 2 or 3) DNS servers are listed. • These DNS servers host the DNS settings for that domain – any inquiry for any address which ends with “donutfiesta.com” will be passed to these DNS servers for resolution. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DNS settings can include several types of records related to a domain: • “A Record” – this is the default IP address where any traffic for the domain is directed (IPv4) • “MX Record” – this is the Mail eXchange record, any email traffic for the domain is directed to these IP addresses • “AAAA Record” – similar to the A record, the AAAA record is the details of IPv6 address for traffic to the domain. • “CNAME” – also called an alias or Canonical Name record, the CNAME redirects a subdomain such as “ftp.donutfiesta.com” to another server name. • “PTR Record” – Pointer records map an IP address to a hostname, and are primarily used for reverse DNS. DNS Records Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DNS Propagation • Changes to DNS servers do not take effect immediately. • DNS Server information is cached by all DNS servers around the Internet, so a change to the DNS server setting itself can take up to 72 hours to be in effect for all the Internet hosts. • This delay is referred to as the DNS propagation delay. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Dynamic DNS • In some situations, the server referenced in a DNS record may not have a permanent, “static” IP address. • Dynamic DNS services can adjust DNS entries quickly to point to the current IP address of the target machine. • May include a software agent to monitor and report the current IP address to the DDNS server. • RFC 2136 provides a standard method of updating DDNS servers, but runs through DHCP. • Internet DDNS providers offer DDNS services for free or for a fee. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. NAT: Network Address Translation • NAT was created to solve the problem of limited public IP addresses with IPv4, though it has other uses as well. • Before NAT, each device connected to the Internet needed a public IP address. IPv4 uses 32 bits for IP addresses, yielding around 4.29 billion possible addresses. • NAT works like this: your border router has a public IP address, accessible on the Internet. But devices inside your network use private, local IP addresses such as 10.10.10.1 or 192.168.1.50. • NAT translates packets from your private, internal IP addresses at the router, then translates responses back. This allows potentially thousands of devices to share one public IP. Address Translation Certain IP subnets were designated for only private use – these include 10.x.x.x, 192.168.x.x, and 172.16.x.x through 172.31.x.x. These addresses are not used on the Internet and can be safely used on a local network. ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • SNAT: Static Network Address Translation. SNAT maps each private IP to a designated public IP. This does not help conserve public IP addresses but can be useful for migrating or merging networks. • DNAT: Dynamic Network Address Translation. DNAT maps each private IP to a public IP from a pool of available public IP addresses. • PAT (Port Address Translation) or Overloading: The most common form of NAT, Overloading is DNAT with just one public IP address shared by multiple private IP addresses. Each private IP address is assigned to a port, and outgoing packets from the router are designated for the port associated with the private IP which originated the request. Address Translation Options Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Ports • “Ports” can be visualized as separate connections on a router, but in reality the “Port” designator is specified in the TCP or UDP packet header. • Ports can identify specific services or, through PAT specific devices. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Port Forwarding • Port Forwarding is a function of a router or firewall which can forward packets designated for a specific port or a port range to a specific computer or device. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Proxy Servers • A proxy server makes network requests on behalf of another computer or device. • The proxy server is a “middleman” or intermediary. • Proxies can serve several functions: • Speeding up requests by caching common data at the proxy server • Bypassing content filters, especially geographic filters • Providing content-filtering services • Hiding the identity or attributes of the requesting device • Reverse proxy servers handle incoming requests on behalf of network servers Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. A DHCP server has run out of available addresses to allocate. The element to increase is the ___________. 1 lease subnet mask scope domain Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • DHCP can dynamically assign IP address, subnet, gateway, and DNS information to network devices. • Manually setting IP, subnet, gateway, and DNS information is referred to as having a static IP. • DHCP scope is the sequential range of IP addresses the server can give out, also called the Address Pool. • A DNS “A Record” is the default IP address where any IPv4 traffic for the domain is directed. • Network Address Translation (NAT) translates packets from your private, internal IP addresses into a shared public IP address at the router. Lesson 1-12: Addressing Schema Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Describe the structure of an IPv4 address. Explain the purpose of a subnet mask. Discuss how to create a subnet. Describe the difference between Classful and Classless addressing. Explain the role of private addresses in Network Address Translation (NAT). Identify the three components of an IPv6 address. Describe the difference between Stateful Configuration with DHCPv6 and Stateless Autoconfiguration (SLAAC). Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. IP Addressing Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. IPv4 • 32-bit number • Represented in four groups of 8 bits called octets • Expressed in four decimal numbers separated by dots (“dotted decimal”) 10.1.200.155 00001010 00000001 11001000 10011011 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Subnet and Subnet Mask • Subdividing a large network into a subnetwork is called subnetting. • The subnet mask determines the scope of the subnet. 10.1.200.155 00001010 00000001 11001000 10011011 255.255.0.0 11111111 11111111 00000000 00000000 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network and Host Address • The Network Address is the portion of the IP address shared by all devices on the subnet. • The Host Address is the portion of the IP address unique to the host. IP Address 10.1.200.155 00001010 00000001 11001000 10011011 Subnet 255.255.0.0 11111111 11111111 00000000 00000000 Network 10.1.0.0 00001010 00000001 00000000 00000000 Host 0.0.200.155 0000000 00000000 11001000 10011011 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network and Host Address (contd.) • The Network Address is the portion of the IP address shared by all devices on the subnet. • The Host Address is the portion of the IP address unique to the host. IP Address 10.1.200.155 00001010 00000001 11001000 10011011 Subnet 255.255.192.0 11111111 11111111 11000000 00000000 Network 10.1.192.0 00001010 00000001 11000000 00000000 Host 0.0.8.155 0000000 00000000 00001000 10011011 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Subnetworks • Network Address: 192.168.1.0 • Subnet Mask: 255.255.255.224 • 11111111.11111111.11111111.11100000 • Potential networks: 8 • Hosts per network: 30 • 32 minus the network/subnet address and broadcast address • Network address: first IP in each subnet • Broadcast Address: last IP in each subnet • First hosts: 192.168.1.1/33/65/97/129/161/193/225 • Example: First subnet is the range 192.168.1.0 through 192.168.1.31, with the network address of 192.168.1.0 and a broadcast address of 192.168.1.32 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Simple Subnetworks • Network Address: 192.168.1.0 • Subnet Mask: 255.255.255.0 • 11111111.11111111.11111111.00000000 • Potential networks: 1 • Hosts per network: 254 • Network address: 192.168.1.0 • Broadcast Address: 192.168.1.255 • Hosts: 192.168.1.1 – 192.168.1.254 • “Class C” Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Class 1st Octet Subnet # of networks Class A 1-126 255.0.0.0 126 Class B 128-191 255.255.0.0 16,382 Class C 192-223 255.255.255.0 2.097,150 Class D 224-239 n/a n/a Class E 240-254 n/a n/a Classes • Class D: multicast • Class E: experimental, research • “Classful” addressing uses a Class A, B, or C address (discontinued) • “Classless” addressing does not use a standard Class • Discontinued in 1993 in favor of CIDR Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. CIDR • Classless Inter-Domain Routing (CIDR) • Replaces Classful addressing for public IPs • More efficient: • Class A address (e.g. 100.x.x.x) reserves 16.5 million addresses. • No way to redistribute unused addresses to other networks. • CIDR provides more granular address distribution. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. CIDR Notation • A CIDR address looks like: • The subnet mask number indicates the number of bits in the subnet mask, in this case: • So 86.1.1.200/24 is a subnet ranging from 86.1.1.1 through 86.1.1.255 • More common: /33 subnet from an ISP, providing 8 public IP addresses 86.1.1.1/24 Network Address / Subnet Mask /24 = 11111111.11111111.11111111.00000000 = 255.255.255.0 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Private Addresses • CIDR helps to conserve the shrinking pool of public IPv4 addresses. • 4.3 billion IPv4 public IP addresses available • 7 billion people • IPv4 Address Exhaustion • Two Solutions: • IPv6 • NAT – Network Address Translation • The Plan: • Let companies use private addresses spaces inside their networks for any devices which need not be accessible from the Internet. • Map communication from those devices onto shared public addresses when communicating outside the network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. NAT and PAT Network Address Translation (NAT): • Uses designated Private Address Spaces including: • 10.x.x.x • 172.16.0.0-172.31.255.255 • 192.168.x.x • Non-routing • IP Packets are translated at the edge router • Static NAT maps each private IP to a designated IP • Dynamic NAT maps each private IP to one public IP in an available pool Port Address Translation (PAT) uses port designators to map all private IP addresses onto one shared public IP • Source & and destination port info is retained Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Next Generation – IPv6 Goals with IPv6: • More addresses (4.3bn -> 340k million million million million) • More efficient (less need for CIDN, easier routing, easier roaming) • More secure 340,282,366,920,938,463,463,374,607,431,768,211,456 – that’s the potential address space of IPv6! ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. IPv6 • 128-bit number (up from 32) • Represented in eight 16-bit blocks • Expressed in hexadecimal with colons between each group 2001:a01f:0021:d3d4:0000:0000:001a:002a Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. IPv6 Address Compression / Shortening • Drop leading zeroes 2001:a01f:0021:d3d4:0000:0000:001a:002a 2001:a01f:21:d3d4:0:0:1a:2a • Compress one set of all-zero blocks to a double-colon 2001:a01f:21:d3d4::1a:2a • Note: If there are more than one set of all-zeroes, only the first can be removed. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. IPv6 Address Structure 2001:a01f:0021:d3d4:0000:0000:001a:002a routing prefix (48) } } } subnet (16) interface identifier (64) • Used for Unicast and Anycast addressing • Routing prefix can be up to 64 bits, taking space from the subnet • For link-local addresses the routing + subnet consists of 1111111010 followed by 54 zeroes • The routing prefix + the subnet is called the Network Prefix Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Unicast, Multicast, Anycast, Broadcast • IPv4 supports three types of transmissions: • Unicast – packets sent from one host to another specific host • Multicast – packets sent from one host to a group of designated hosts • Broadcast – packets sent from one host to all other hosts within the broadcast domain • IPv6 does not have Broadcast, replacing those functions with Multicast. But IPv6 adds: • Anycast – packets are sent from one host to the nearest host in the designated anycast group. • IPv6 allows multiple addresses per interface Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. APIPA (IPv4) • What happens if there’s no static IP information set, AND no DHCP? • On Windows devices, Automatic Private IP Addressing (APIPA) auto-configures the IP settings. • Starts at 169.254.0.1, up to 169.254.255.254 (IPv4) • Uses ARP to verify IP is unassigned elsewhere. • Also called link-local addressing Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Auto-configuration (IPv6) • IPv6 interfaces can configure their own addresses, similar to link-local on IPv4. • Called Stateless Autoconfiguration (SLAAC) • Using Neighbor Discovery Protocol (similar to ARP) to retrieve the network prefix • Using modified EUI-64 to derive an interface ID from its own MAC address • Modified EUI-64: • Start with a MAC address (48 bits) • Add FF:FE in the middle (now 64 bits) • Invert the 7th bit (Universal/Local bit) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Auto-configuration (IPv6) (contd.) • Example: • MAC Address aa12:4dfc:4545 • Add FF:FE to get aa12:4dff:fefc:4545 • Invert the 7th bit: a812:4dff:fefc:4545 • Most common first 32 bits is “00”, which inverted is “02” Inverting the 7th bit: a (hex) = 1010 aa = 101010110 Inverted 10101000 10101000 = a8 (hex) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DHCPv6 • Does Autoconfiguration mean no more DHCP? • DHCPv6 provides: • DNS settings • Gateway settings • Optional: IP Address • “Stateful Configuration” – DHCPv6 provides the IP address • “Stateless Autoconfiguration” (SLAAC) – DHCP lets the device keep the IP from autoconfiguration Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Co-existing, IPv4 and IPv6 • IPv4 and IPv6 are NOT compatible (cannot talk to each other) • They *can* co-exist on the same network through: • Dual-stack: routers and other devices on the network use both IPv4 and IPv6 separately • Tunneling: IPv6 is encapsulated in IPv4 packets for transmission across an IPv4 LAN or WAN (6to4 tunneling) • 4to6 tunneling would carry IPv4 packets across an IPv6 network • Tunneling will break if NAT is involved. Teredo and Miredo are solutions to encapsulate IPv6 packet in UDP datagrams to traverse NAT segments • NAT-PT: Network Address Translation – Protocol Translation, translates IPv6 to IPv4 like NAT, but has issues Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which type of transmission is NOT part of IPv6? 3 unicast anycast broadcast multicast Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. IPv6 networking does not include broadcast transmissions, replacing those functions with multicast. c. unicast anycast broadcast multicast 3 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Subdividing a large network into a subnetwork is called subnetting. • The Host Address is the portion of the IP address unique to the host. • Class C addresses started with 192 through 223 in the first octet, with a subnet mask of 255.255.255.0. • CIDR stands for Classless Inter-Domain Routing which replaced Classful addressing for public IPs. • Port Address Translation (PAT) is a form of Network Address Translation (NAT) which uses port designators to map all private IP addresses onto one shared public IP. • Stateless Autoconfiguration (SLAAC) allows IPv6 hosts to configure its own IP address using Neighbor Discovery Protocol and a modified EUI-64 version of its MAC address. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 1: Network Theory and Architecture CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 1-13: Routing Concepts Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Explain the purpose of routing protocols. Describe the difference between distance vector, link state, and hybrid routing protocols. Discuss the use of routing tables with static and dynamic routes. Define routing metrics such as distance (hops), MTU, bandwidth, and costs. Explain administrative distance. Label RIPv2, BGP, OSPF, and IS-IS as distance vector, link state, or hybrid protocols. Define route aggregation and route redistribution. Discuss strategies to maintain high availability with regards to routing. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Routers • Small networks usually have just one router. • Larger networks may have many routers to: • Break up broadcast domains • Connect remote locations • Separate logical divisions/departments Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Routing Tables • Each Router creates and maintains a Routing Table to determine which interface will be used for each packet being routed. • At a minimum, each network identified is listed with an associated interface and one or more metrics. • If the same network is available through multiple interfaces, the interface with the best route (metrics) is used. • Routing Tables can be constructed manually (static) or automatically (dynamic). • If a Table contains both static and dynamic entries, the static entries are prioritized. • A default route can be programmed for networks not listed in the table. Routing Table 192.168.1.0 E0 0 192.168.2.0 S0 0 192.168.3.0 S0 1 192.168.4.0 S0 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Dynamic Routes • Calculating the best route dynamically requires work from the router. • Best routes can be calculated based on various routing metrics, including: • Hop count (how many routers away is it?) • MTU, bandwidth (packet size and speed) • Latency (how fast does the next router respond?) • Costs (set by administrator) • Administrative distance – a measurement of perceived quality of a route, based on the routing protocol and/or source of the routing table data, measured from 1 to 255. • SPB – Shortest Path Bridging, 802.1aq. SPB is a newer technology intended to simplify the configuration of networks while enabling multipath routing. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Routing Loop • Router A has a packet to send to Router C. • Its routing table tells that sending to Router B is the best route, so it does so. • Router B checks its routing table for the best route to Router C, and finds it’s through Router A; so it sends the packet back to A. • This is a Routing Loop • Most routing protocols work to avoid loops • Looping packets will generally be dropped when they’ve traversed more than 15 routers. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Interior vs. Exterior • Routing protocols can be classified as Interior or Exterior Gateway Routing Protocols (IGRP or EGRP) • Interior means within a given Autonomous System (AS) – a collection of networks and subnets under the same administrative control. • Exterior means outside a given AS, also outside of your designated network domain. • If an AS is registered with the Internet Assigned Numbers Authority to present its clearly defined routing policy to the Internet, it will have an Autonomous System Number (ASN). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Distance Vector Routing Protocols • Distance Vector protocols use distance – measured in hops – to calculate the best route. • Each router shares its routing table with neighboring routers, who merge it with theirs and share again. • The time it takes for all routers to finish merging their tables is called convergence. • Distance Vector Routing Protocols include: • RIP (Routing Information Protocol) • RIPv2 (recommended for small networks) • IGRP (Interior Gateway Routing Protocol) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Link State Routing Protocols • Link State Protocols (also called Path First Protocols) create three separate tables for direct neighbors, the network topology (including best path and backup path to each network), and a routing table. • Link State protocols include: • OSPF (Open Shortest Path First) • IS-IS (Intermediate System to Intermediate System) • Both divide networks into “Areas” for faster processing. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Hybrid Protocols • Hybrid protocols combine elements of Distance Vector and Link State routing protocols. • EIGRP (Enhanced IGRP) – includes the subnet mask along with the route updates, supports CIDR and IPv6. • BGP (Border Gateway Protocol) – the main routing protocol of the Internet, can also be used in local networks. Measures 10 attributes of all connected networks, including distance. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Route Redistribution – the translation that occurs when different parts of a network use different routing protocols. • Route Aggregation – minimizing routing tables by consolidating multiple routes into a single route advertisement. • Loopback Interface – a logical, virtual interface in a router, used by OSPF, BGP, and other protocols to maintain communication when physical interfaces are down. Other Terms Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. High Availability • Networks should be designed to resist any single point of failure – a feature known as High Availability. • A virtual IP and virtual MAC address is created for a redundant group of routers. • One router is designated “Master”, the others are designated “Backup”. Master assumes the virtual IP and MAC on a virtual interface. • Hosts on the network use the virtual IP/MAC for their Gateway. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. High Availability (contd.) • Master and Backups communicate every 30 seconds with a “hello” message – if the Master does not respond, a Backup assumes the virtual IP and MAC. • Protocols which use this arrangement include: • HSRP (Hot Standby Router Protocol) – proprietary to Cisco • VRRP (Virtual Router Redundancy Protocol) – open standard hello? Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Each Router uses a Routing Table to determine which interface will be used for each packet being routed. • Routing Tables can be constructed manually (static) or automatically (dynamic). • Routing tables include metrics for each network which can include distance (hops), MTU (packet size), bandwidth, latency, and costs. • An Autonomous System (AS) is a collection of networks and subnets under the same administrative control. • Hybrid routing protocols combine elements of Distance Vector and Link State routing protocols. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 1-14: Unified Communication Technologies Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Define Unified Communications as it relates to networking. • List technologies and devices that can be included in UC. • Discuss the challenges UC services can have on a network. • Explain the use of Quality of Service (QoS) to improve UC services. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Unified Communications (UC) is a marketing term, not a standard. • UC refers to the merger of voice, video, and other communication onto the data network. Unified Communications Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. UC Technologies • UC technologies may include: • Voice-over-IP (VoIP) phone services • Video conferencing and video streaming • Realtime services such as chat or instant messaging (IM) • Presence indication • Desktop sharing • Interactive whiteboards • eFax services Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. UC Components • UC Devices • VoIP Phones • Video cameras • Video Teleconference systems (VTC) • Audio and music devices • UC Servers – servers designed to support one or more unified communication technologies, such as VoIP phone servers, video conferencing servers, or media servers. • UC Gateways – networking gateways which support UC protocols such as QoS Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network Challenges • Delay – packets arriving too slowly • Dropped packets • Error – corrupted packets • Jitter – variation in packet delay • Out-of-order delivery • Multicast vs. Unicast – Multicast uses less bandwidth Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QoS – Quality of Service • TCP/IP is a “best effort” protocol, not designed with UC in mind. • Quality of Service (QoS) is a way to prioritize traffic on a network, so that sensitive UC packets are less likely to be delayed or dropped. • DSCP – Differentiated Services Code Point (DiffServ), a field in an IP packet which species IP Precedence and Type of Service. • Guaranteed Service – high quality with guaranteed minimum latency • Controlled load – high quality without guaranteed latency • Class of Service (COS) –adds a 3-bit field called Priority Code Point (PCP) to an Ethernet Frame, ranging from 0 (“best effort”) to 4 (“controlled load” / steaming media) to 7 (“layer 2 network control reserved”). • QoS services must be available and enabled on all appropriate switches, routers, and other devices. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Unified Communications is: 1 a standard a protocol a packet format a marketing term Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Unified Communications is: Unified Communication is a marketing term. d. a standard a protocol a packet format a marketing term 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of the following best describes Quality of Service (QoS)? 2 a measurement of dropped packets a way to prioritize packets on a network. an encryption protocol the distance between packets Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which of the following best describes Quality of Service (QoS)? Quality of Service (QoS) is a way to prioritize packets on a network. b. a measurement of dropped packets a way to prioritize packets on a network. an encryption protocol the distance between packets 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Unified Communications (UC) is a marketing term which refers to the merger of voice, video, and other communication onto the data network. • UC technologies may include VoIP phone services, video conferencing, chat and IM, and presence indication. • UC Servers are servers designed to support one or more unified communication technologies, such as VoIP phone servers. • Quality of Service (QoS) is a way to prioritize traffic on a network, so that sensitive UC packets are less likely to be delayed or dropped. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 1-15: Cloud and Virtualization Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Describe virtualization, including virtual servers, virtual switches, and virtual network interfaces. • Define software defined networking (SDN). • Explain the use of a Storage Area Network (SAN). • Define iSCSI, Fibre Channel, and Jumbo Frames. • Explain the use of and differences between Software-as-a-Service (SaaS), Platform-as-a-Service (PaaS), and Infrastructure-as-a-Service (IaaS) • Differentiate between public, private, hybrid, and community clouds. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • “The Cloud” is a term for the Internet and services hosted through the Internet. • Operating in “The Cloud” has created an entirely new type of environment. • Creating and maintaining “The Cloud” requires some special technologies. The Cloud Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Hardware and software can be the same thing. • Virtualization is the creation of virtual devices (computers, routers, switches) which are not directly tied to physical components. Virtualization Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Virtualization Components • Host – the machine on which the virtualization takes place • Guest – the virtualized machine or device • Hypervisor – the software which creates and supports the virtual environment Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Benefits of Virtualization • Portability– virtual machines can be moved from host to host as needed. • Scalability – virtual machines can be easily increased, decreased, and multiplied. • Failover and load balancing – virtual machines can be moved to a new host when one host fails or needs additional capacity. • Energy saving – multiple virtual machines can be combined on one physical host, saving energy and cooling costs. • Faster/easier provisioning – new virtual equipment can be created quickly and easily within a virtual environment. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Virtual Infrastructure • Virtual computers can connect virtually through virtual infrastructure, including: • Virtual Switches • Virtual Routers • Virtual Firewalls • Virtual NICs connect to physical NICs through bridging. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Virtual Network Interfaces • Some routers include virtual network interfaces in addition to their physical interfaces • Virtual network interfaces: • Have their own MAC address • Will be assigned IP addresses just like a physical interface • Connect to physical interfaces through bridging Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Software Defined Networking (SDN) • SDN is a method for abstracting the control decisions in a network device from the hardware and lower level functionality. • SDN can be more scalable, manageable, and cost-effective than traditional networking. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Storage Area Network • A Storage Area Network (SAN) is a network dedicated to storage. • SAN storage is accessible to network devices as if it were local storage. • SAN storage is block-level accessible, supporting any file system. • Network Attached Storage (NAS) refers to a file-level server sharing data on a network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. iSCSI and Fibre Channel • SCSI – Small Computer Systems Interface, a type of data connection to local hard drives or other storage • iSCSI – Internet Small Computer Systems Interface, an IP-based data standard to connect data storage facilities to network devices, often used in SANs. • Fibre Channel – a high speed data connection protocol, functionally similar to iSCSI but communicates through a direct connection (copper or fiber optic) between the storage and the host. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Jumbo Frame • A traditional ethernet frame is limited to 1500 bytes. • Jumbo frame is the term used for ethernet frames over 1500 bytes, up to 9000 bytes. • Jumbo frames can reduce network bandwidth, especially in storage networks, by reducing the administrative overhead of frame headers. • The risk with jumbo frames is the increased chance of CRC32 errors and having to retransmit large frames when they occur. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Cloud Computing • Cloud computing is a solution where a pool of computer resources is shared with users, generally on a subscription basis, from a centrally hosted solution. Cloud computing can be grouped into three general categories: • Software-as-a-Service (SaaS) – software applications, often web-based, in which software licensing and delivery is provided on a centrally-hosted subscription basis. • Platform-as-a-Service (PaaS) – a solution where clients can build and run their own web apps using a shared cloud-based platform. PaaS makes it easy to build applications without the need to build low level functionality and virtualization. • Infrastructure-as-a-Service (IaaS) – a cloud computing solution which provides hosted infrastructure components such as servers, storage, backup, and network connectivity. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Cloud Types • Public – cloud services which are shared with other unrelated users or organizations in a multi-tenant arrangement. • Private – cloud services which are entirely controlled by one organization, often inside a corporate firewall and controlled by the IT department. • Hybrid – a combination of public and private clouds, where some components are managed in-house (private) while others are provided by a third party (public). • Community – a special type of private cloud which is shared by several organizations but not generally available to the public. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Private Cloud Public Cloud Hybrid Cloud Community Cloud 3 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Virtualization is the creation of virtual devices (computers, routers, switches) which are not directly tied to physical components. • Virtual network interfaces have their own MAC address, are assigned IP addresses just like a physical interface, and connect to physical interfaces through bridging. • SDN is a method for abstracting the control decisions in a network device from the hardware and lower level functionality. • iSCSI – Internet Small Computer Systems Interface, an IP-based data standard to connect data storage facilities to network devices, often used in SANs. • A Public cloud is cloud services which are shared with other unrelated users or organizations in a multi-tenant arrangement. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 1-16: Implementing a Network Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Discuss the network planning process. • Explain how environmental limitations such as distance and EMI/RFI interference sources affect your network plan. • Describe types of equipment that might be segmented for compatibility purposes. • List three considerations of planning a wireless network. • Discuss reasons to include or not include 802.1x and posture assessment in the planned security for your network. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Implementing a Network • Let’s say you are tasked with creating a new network. • What data do you need to design the network appropriately? • How to get started? Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. List of Requirements • Start with a list of requirements for the network, provided by the stakeholders including senior management, IT directors, and key users. • If a list of requirements isn’t provided, request one. The list of requirements should include things like: • Software applications to be used • Network services such as VoIP, video conferencing, or database applications • Any special needs such as ICS/SCADA systems or medianets. • Any specific security concerns. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Device Types and Requirements • Consider the quantity and type of devices that will need to use your network. PCs, servers, printers, industrial equipment, tablets, smartphones, and any other devices should be considered. • As a rule of thumb, double the expected quantity of devices which will use the network. If the total is greater than 50 devices, consider segmenting the network into subnets to minimize broadcast traffic. • Will there be any devices with particular network requirements, such as videoconferencing or SCADA networks? Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Environmental Limitations • Keep in mind environmental limitations as you map out your network. In particular: • Copper wiring generally has a limitation of 100m – longer distances need to be broken up with switches or repeaters, or carried via fiber optic. • Wireless coverage should be mapped out with a site survey to look for dead spots. • Are there any unusual EMI or RFI sources which should be factored in? • Is there sufficient electrical power in the data room or network closet where key network infrastructure will be housed? • Consider redundant power sources or battery backups for critical network components. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Compatibility Requirements • Think about any potential compatibility issues within your planned network. • If you are implementing IPv6, does all your equipment support it? • Are there older legacy devices which require special connections or which should be segmented into their own network for security considerations? • If your network will include ICS or medianets, consider segmenting those for better performance and security. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wired and Wireless considerations • If there is existing wiring, is it of a sufficient grade to support your planned network speeds? (e.g. Cat5e or better if 1000Mbps) • As a general rule, wired connections are preferable whenever feasible for non-mobile devices. • If multiple wireless access points are needed, consider implementing a mesh network for reliable coverage and/or 802.1x for centralized authentication. • If guests may need access to Internet or network services while at your location, consider implementing a guest WLAN and/or guest VLAN to keep their access away from secure network areas. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Security Considerations • Attention to security should be part of every step in your network planning process. • There is no such thing as “too secure”, though security considerations must be balanced against your budget and your user experience. • Think about your most likely vulnerabilities (outside hackers, malware, rogue users) and focus on hardening the network against those attacks. • Functions such as Posture Assessment and 802.1x authentication are great but may not be feasible for smaller organizations due to lack of budget or other resources. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The coverage area of any wireless access points. Any sources of EMI/RFI Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. The coverage area of any wireless access points. Any sources of EMI/RFI 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of these is a valid reason to use IPv4 on your network? 2 Some network equipment does not support IPv6 The network is expected to have less than 100 users. IPv4 is faster than IPv6 You want to use jumbo frames Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which of these is a valid reason to use IPv4 on your network? If some existing network equipment does not support IPv6, this would be a valid reason to use IPv4 on your network. a. Some network equipment does not support IPv6 The network is expected to have less than 100 users. IPv4 is faster than IPv6 You want to use jumbo frames 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Designing a new network starts with a list of requirements for the network, provided by the stakeholders including senior management, IT directors, and key users. • As a rule of thumb, double the expected quantity of devices which will use the network and if the total is greater than 50 devices, consider segmenting the network into subnets to minimize broadcast traffic. • Copper wiring generally has a limitation of 100m – longer distances need to be broken up with switches or repeaters, or carried via fiber optic. • If using existing wiring, consider whether it is of a sufficient grade to support your planned network speeds? (e.g. Cat5e or better if 1000Mbps) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Ports and Protocols’. This concludes ‘Implementing a Network’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 1-17: Ports and Protocols Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Describe a TCP/IP port. • Define protocol as it relates to networking. • Discuss the default port for protocols such as HTTP, FTP, SMTP, SNMP, and SIP and their appropriate uses. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Ports • “Ports” can be visualized as separate connections on a router, but in reality the “Port” designator is specified in the TCP or UDP packet header. • Ports can identify specific services or, through PAT specific devices. • Port is a 16-bit number, representing a potential 65536 possible ports. • Approximately 1024 standard ports are designated, with the others generally considered available for any use. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Protocols • A Protocol is a standard for communication, with rules and conventions to facilitate communication between two devices. • Protocols exist at different layers of the OSI model – IP is a layer 3 protocol, TCP is a layer 4 protocol, HTTP is a layer 7 protocol. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. TCP and UDP • TCP, Transmission Control Protocol, is a connection-oriented protocol and part of the TCP/IP Suite. • UDP, User Datagram Protocol, is a connectionless protocol and part of the TCP/IP Suite. • The rest of the protocols we’ll look at are built on top of TCP or UDP, with standard default port designations Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. HTTP and HTTPS • Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) is a protocol based on structured text with hyperlinks. • Most websites are built with HTTP. • HTTPS is a more secure version of HTTP and uses TLS or SSL encryption to improve the privacy and security of the data transmitted and received. • HTTP defaults to port 80, HTTPS defaults to port 443. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. NetBIOS • NetBIOS or Network Basic Input/Output System is a networking API which runs on layer 4 (Session Layer) of the OSI model. • NetBIOS facilitates communication by assigning a NetBIOS name to a host and providing datagram and session services. • NetBIOS works on multiple underlying protocols, including its related protocol NetBeui, but today is most often run as NetBIOS over TCP/IP, using ports 137-139. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Internet Email • POP or Post-Office Protocol is used for the simplest form of Internet email delivery and defaults to port 110. • IMAP or Internet Message Access Protocol is a more advanced email protocol which allows a device to access email stored on a remote server. IMAP defaults to port 143. • SMTP or Simple Mail Transport Protocol is used to send email on the Internet, and defaults to port 25. Because port 25 is frequently blocked as a spam prevention measure, most SMTP servers also support alternate ports. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Audio/Video Protocols • SIP (Session Initiation Protocol), used for multimedia communication and VoIP phone systems, defaults to ports 5060 and 5061. • MGCP (Media Gateway Control Protocol) is used in some VoIP applications and uses ports 2427 and 2727. • RTP (Real-time Transport Protocol) is used for streaming media such as video conferencing, and uses ports 5004/5005. • H.323 is a standard and a protocol used in voice and videoconferencing applications, and uses port 1720. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. TCP/IP Application Protocols • FTP, File Transfer Protocol (Ports 20 or 21) is used for sending files over TCP/IP networks. • TFTP, Trivial (or Tiny) File Transfer Protocol is a simplified version of FTP designed for very simple transfers such as firmware updates or configuration settings, and uses port 69. • SNMP, Simple Network Management Protocol is used to query or set attributes on network devices and uses port 161 by default. • Telnet is a protocol to allow access to remote computers and uses port 23. • SSH or Secure Shell functions similar to Telnet but with encryption and uses port 22. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Microsoft Protocols • SMB (Server Message Block) is a protocol for network file sharing on a Microsoft Windows network, and uses port 445. (A similar protocol, AFP or Apple Filing Protocol is used on Apple OSX networks). • RDP (Remote Desktop Protocol) is designed to share a user’s desktop, including the graphical interface, keyboard, mouse, and (in later versions) audio and print redirection. RDP uses port 3389 by default. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DNS and DHCP • DNS (Domain Name System) uses a unique protocol called the DNS protocol to facilitate assigning and looking up domain names. • The DNS protocol uses port 53. • DHCP (Dynamic Host Control Protocol) dynamically assigns network IP addresses, and uses ports 67 and 68 by default. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of these is NOT a protocol? 1 HTTP SNMP Session H.323 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which of these is NOT a protocol? HTTP, SNMP, and H.323 are all examples of protocols. H.323 is also a standard. c. HTTP SNMP Session H.323 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which port does POP most commonly use? 2 80 81 110 5060 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which port does POP most commonly use? The Post Office Protocol (POP) uses port 110 by default. c. 80 81 110 5060 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Port is a 16-bit number, representing a potential 65536 possible ports. • A Protocol is a standard for communication, with rules and conventions to facilitate communication between two devices. • Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) is a protocol using port 80 which is based on structured text with hyperlinks. • SMTP or Simple Mail Transport Protocol is used to send email on the Internet, and defaults to port 25. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Monitoring Tools’. This concludes ‘Ports and Protocols’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 1: Network Theory and Architecture CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 1-1: Networking Theory Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ●Define a Network and Network Devices ●Describe the basic characteristics of a LAN, WAN, MAN, and WLAN ●Explain the uses of Bluetooth and NFC ●Describe the purpose of SCADA ●Explain the benefit of segmentation in Medianets After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • A Network is an interconnected group of computers or devices which can communicate with each other. • The connection may be wired or wireless. • Each device on the network is called a Node or Host. Network Theory and Types of Networks Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Computers • Servers & and Storage • Printers • Routers, Firewalls, Switches, and other Network Devices • VoIP Phones • IP Security Cameras • Game Consoles • Internet-Capable TVs or Music Devices • Home Appliances • Industrial or Medical Equipment • Smartphones and Tablets Network Theory and Types of Networks Devices on a network may include: Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. LAN (Local Area Network) • A network in a particular geographic location such as an office, floor, or building. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN (Wide Area Network) • A network spanning multiple geographic locations. • Broadband connections from Internet Service Providers are (usually) WANs. • A common misconception is that WAN means “Wireless Area Network”. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. MAN (Metropolitan Area Network) • A WAN that spans an entire city or metropolitan area. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WLAN (Wireless LAN) • A network comprised of wireless connections, or the portion of a LAN that uses wireless connections. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Mobile Hotspot • A Hotspot is a portable wireless access point, most often using cellular networks. • A Hotspot can be used to connect wireless devices to the Internet or to each other, in areas where there is no permanent network infrastructure (or where using the infrastructure is expensive). • A Hotspot may be a separate device, or can also be an app run from a smartphone, turning the phone into a Hotspot. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. PAN (Personal Area Network) • A network used among devices such as a computer, tablet, smartphone, or PDA, for a single user. • A PAN may use wired connections such as USB and FireWire, or wireless connections such as Bluetooth, IR/IrDA, or INSTEON. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bluetooth • Bluetooth: a low power wireless connection protocol designed to replace short cables to connect devices. • It is used by local devices such as keyboards, mice, speakers, headsets and headphones, intercoms, phones, tablets, and more. • Bluetooth uses the 2.4GHz radio spectrum, which is also used by Wi-Fi, cordless phones, and other unregulated wireless devices. • Up to 7 devices can connect to one Bluetooth host. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. NFC: Near Field Communication • Used for wireless communication in very close proximity (less than 10cm). • NFC is built into many smartphones as well as some tablets and computers. • Uses can include: • Mobile payment solutions such as Apple Pay or Google Wallet • Marketing, such as embedding NFC Info tags in movie posters to give NFC-enabled devices additional information • Identification – NFC Info tags can be embedded in packages and shipping containers for easy identification by NFC readers. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. IrDA / IR • IR: Infrared, also known as IrDA for the Infrared Data Association. • Infrared can be used for wireless communication between devices. • Infrared is a form of light, so IR works only when there is a clear line-of-sight between the receiver and transmitter. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ICS: Industrial Control System • ICS is a generic term for several types of control systems used in Industrial Production. • The most common type is Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition (SCADA) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. SCADA • SCADA works with: • Sensors (Analog or Digital) • Remote Terminal Units (RTUs), used for human interaction and display. • Programmable Logic Controllers (PLCs), used to gather data from Sensors • ICS Server: Acquires information from Sensors, PLCs, and RTUs about the status of equipment for display or recording purposes • The network connecting ICS devices is referred to as a Distributed Control System (DCS). • A best practice is for the DCS to be a Closed Network, not connected to outside networks or the Internet. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Medianets • Medianets refer to networks primarily devoted to audio and video communication. This can include: • Voice-over-IP (VoIP) Phone Systems • Unified Communications services such as Microsoft Lync or Skype • Media broadcast services, such as the network carrying audio and video feeds for a television station • Video Teleconferencing (VTC) solutions, which enable remote meetings and collaboration. • Older VTC Solutions use the H.320 standard over ISDN connections. • Modern VTC Solutions use Session Initiation Protocol (SIP) or the H.323 standard over IP Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Medianets and Segmentation • Medianets are often separated from the rest of the network, which is called Segmentation. • Segmentation lets VTC and other high-bandwidth applications run with high performance and low latency. • Segmentation also offers greater security since the media applications are separated from normal network use Medianets (contd.) Summary ● A Network is an interconnected group of computers or devices which can communicate with each other. ● A LAN is a network in a particular geographic location such as an office, floor, or building. ● A WAN is a network spanning multiple geographic locations. ● Bluetooth is a low power wireless connection protocol designed to replace short cables to connect devices. ● The most common type of Industrial Control System (ICS) is Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition (SCADA). Lesson 1-2: OSI Model Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ●Describe the OSI model ●List the seven layers of the OSI model ●Describe the basic characteristics of each layer ●Identify which layers handle Bits, Frames, Packets, and Segments ●Apply the OSI model to troubleshoot networks After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The OSI Model For a network connection to work, many things must take place. • The Open Systems Interconnection Reference Model (OSI Model) is a useful guide to understanding the seven layers of activity involved in a network connection. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The Seven Layers of the OSI Model 1- Physical 2- Data Link 3- Network 4- Transport 5- Session 6- Presentation 7- Application •Each layer builds on the level below it, but is (mostly) independent. •Layers represent a group of communication functions. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Reference Guide 1-Physical 2-Data Link 3-Network 4-Transport 5-Session 6-Presentation 7-Application The OSI model is a useful reference guide to understanding and troubleshooting networks. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The OSI Model Remembering the order of the layers is important – these acrostics may help: •Please Do Not Tell Sales People Anything •Please Do Not Throw Sausage Pizza Away •All People Seem To Need Data Processing 5 - Session 1 - Physical 2 - Data Link 3 - Network 4 - Transport 5 - Session 6 - Presentation 7 -Application Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. A Simple Analogy 1 - Physical 2 - Data Link 3 - Network 4 - Transport 5 - Session 6 - Presentation 7 -Application 1 - Chicken 2 – Chicken Lays Egg 3 – Egg Collected by Farmer 4 – Egg Sold at Market 5 – Egg Purchased by Restaurant 6 – Chef Cooks Egg 7 –Customer Gets Cooked Egg Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 1 – The Physical Layer Includes all physical elements involved in transmitting and receiving BITS: • Cables or radio spectrum • Physical ports, network cards, Wi-Fi transmitters The Physical Layer sends and receives BITS ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Provides basic error correction Includes two sub-layers: • MAC layer – handles physical addressing and topology (Media Access Control) • LLC Layer – coordinates and synchronizes with other devices on the network (Logical Link Control) Used by network switches 2 – The Data Link Layer 0 1 1 0 0 1 1 0 The Data link layer sends and receives FRAMES (a Sequence of 64 to 1518 bytes) ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Protocols such as IP, IPX, or AppleTalk exist in this layer and is used by Routers 3 – The Network Layer The Network layer sends and receives PACKETS (a chunk of data) ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Connects the low level communications “hardware” in levels 1 through 3 with higher level software in levels 5 through 7. • Common layer 4 protocols are: • TCP, or Transmission Control Protocol • UDP, or User Datagram Protocol 4 – The Transport Layer The Transport layer communicates with SEGMENTS ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. This layer constructs, supports, and deconstructs sessions as needed by services in the higher layers. 5 – The Session Layer Session: A set of related communications that should be treated separately from other communications, similar to a conversation. ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. This layer is where data formatting and encryption may take place. • Example: Converting ASCII-encoded text to EBCDIC or vice-versa Sometimes known as the syntax layer. It is often included as part of layer 7 6 – The Presentation Layer Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. This layer provides network services or applications to software running on the device. • Often confused with actual user applications such as email programs, Internet browsers, etc. • Includes HTTP, FTP, SMTP, SNMP, etc. 7 – The Application Layer Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. All rights reserved. Summary ● The Open Systems Interconnection Reference Model (OSI Model) is a useful guide to understanding the seven layers of activity involved in a network connection. ● The Physical Layer includes all physical elements involved in transmitting and receiving BITS. • The Data link layer sends and receives FRAMES (Sequences of 64 to 1518 bytes). ● Protocols such as IP exist in the Network layer, which sends and receives PACKETS. ● A Session is a set of related communications that should be treated separately from other communications, similar to a conversation. Lesson 1-3: Topologies Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ● Differentiate between Point-to-Point and Point-to-Multipoint networks ●Explain the difference between Client-Server and Peer-to-Peer networks ● Define Bus Topology ● Identify Ring Topology ● Discuss Star Topology ● Differentiate between Partial and Full Mesh Topology ●Identify Hybrid Topology After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. What is a Topology? • Topology is the interrelatedness and arrangement of constituent parts in a network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network Topologies Imagine you were inventing a new way to network. How would you connect the devices to each other? Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bus Topology • One unbroken cable, terminated on each end, connecting to each computer with a “T” connector. • Bus Topology was common with older 10base2 and 10base5 networks using a coaxial cable. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bus Topology – Pros and Cons • PROS: No central hardware (switches, hubs) needed. • CONS: Any disconnection anywhere in the cable stops all communication Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Ring Topology • This is similar to Bus Topology with one unbroken cable. • While Bus topology has two terminated cable ends, a Ring Topology is in a loop with no ends. • It has similar pros and cons compared to Bus: No central hardware is needed but any faults or disconnections bring down the entire network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Star Topology • Each computer connects directly to a central point, usually a Switch, Hub, or Router. • Disconnections only affect the one computer on that link. • Most LANs and WLANs, today, use Star Topology. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Mesh Topology • Full Mesh: Every device connects to every other device. • Partial Mesh: Some nodes are in a Full Mesh, other nodes may only connect to 1 or 2 other devices. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Mesh Topology−Pros and Cons • PROS: Highly fault tolerant – no single failure will disrupt communication • CONS: Requires each node to be intelligent enough to manage its own communication Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Mesh Wireless mesh is frequently found in large wireless networks such as, on a campus or public area. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Hybrid Topology A mix of 2 or more network topologies Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Point-to-Point Communication Point-to-point communication is one dedicated communication connection between two devices. A traditional phone call is an example of point-to-point communications. ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Point-to-Multipoint Communication Point-to-multipoint communication is one device or node that connects to multiple devices. Wireless access points create Point-to-Multipoint networks ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Client-Server vs Peer-To-Peer Client-Server • A network arrangement where user computers and devices (“Clients”) primarily communicate with one or more central Servers. Peer-To-Peer • A network arrangement without a central server, where the clients communicate with each other directly Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Cat5 Star Point-to-Point VPN 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Peer-to-peer refers to: 3 A network without a central server A bus topology network. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Topology is the interrelatedness and arrangement of constituent parts in a network. • Common topology types are Bus, Ring, Star, Mesh, and Hybrid. • A Star topology is when each node connects directly to a hub or switch. • Client-Server is a network arrangement where, user computers and devices (“Clients”) primarily communicate with one or more central Servers. • Peer-to-Peer is a network arrangement without a central server, where the clients communicate with each other directly.
