Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 1: Network Theory and Architecture CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 1-4: WAN Technologies Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ● Explain the characteristics and benefits of various WAN technologies, including Dialup, DSL, Broadband Cable, ISDN, T-Series, Metro-E, and Satellite. ● Discuss the differences between ADSL and SDSL. ● Explain the difference between Frequency Division Multiplexing and Time Division Multiplexing. ● Describe the basic characteristics of SONET, MPLS, ATM, Frame Relay, and Wireless WAN circuits. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN Technologies WAN: Wide Area Network is often the network your Internet Service Provider uses to connect your LAN to the Internet. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Fiber vs. Copper vs. Wireless A WAN can be delivered many ways, which may include traditional copper cabling, fiber optic cabling, wireless solutions, or a combination. The type of media used may be based on these factors: ● Signal Attenuation/Degradation: The longer the distance a signal travels, the weaker it becomes. The maximum range for a copper DSL circuit is 5.5km while a fiber SONET circuit can travel up to 15km. ● Cost: Generally fiber optic cabling is the most expensive and most difficult to install. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Multiplexing, Time or Frequency • Multiplexing is a procedure for transmitting many signals on the same connection. The combined signals are demultiplexed on the receiving side. • Frequency Division Multiplexing (FDM) sends each individual signal within a non-overlapping frequency sub-band on the communications medium. • Time Division Multiplexing (TDM) chops each individual signal into discrete chunks, which are transmitted over a synchronized connection. Each chunk uses the connection for a fraction of time. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN Technologies - Dialup ● Maximum speed 56Kbps ● Generally obsolete except in rural areas ● Uses a Modem and an analog phone line, often referred to as either: o PSTN—Public Switched Telephone Network o POTS―Plain Old Telephone Service Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN Technologies - ISDN ISDN • Consists of 2 or more Bearer channels (“B channels”) capable of carrying 64kbps each, plus one Data channel (“D channel”) at 16kbps. • PRI-ISDN consists of 30 B channels for a total bonded bandwidth of 1920kbps. • BRI-ISDN, most common in North America, uses 2 B channels for a total bonded bandwidth of 128kbps. • Often used for video conferencing systems and phone service, less often for Internet connections. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DSL • “Digital Subscriber Line” • DSL allows high speed data transmission over short distances using ordinary 2-wire telephone cabling. • Because DSL uses frequencies outside of those used for voice traffic, it does not interfere with normal phone calls on the same cable. • DSL circuits must connect to a Digital Subscriber Line Access Multiplexer (“DSLAM”) within approximately 18,000 feet (5.5 km). WAN Technologies - DSL Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • ADSL • ADSL or Asynchronous DSL has a faster download speed than its upload speed. • ADSL speeds are often written as Upload/Download. E.g. “768/128” indicates an ADSL connection with a 768kbps download speed and 128kbps upload speed. • SDSL • Synchronous DSL: upload speeds and download speeds are identical DSL Types Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Broadband Internet Service uses coaxial cable, generally the same cable used for TV service. • Compared with DSL, Broadband Cable is generally faster but can have higher Latency. • Broadband Cable users share bandwidth with all other users on their local loop. • (DSL users share bandwidth at the shared DSLAM). WAN Technologies – Broadband Cable Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN Technologies - Satellite Satellite • Satellite is an option for Internet (and other) connectivity in areas not served by other broadband options. • Satellite speeds have improved but satellite broadband is generally slower than DSL or Cable. • Satellite suffers from extremely high latency – not surprising since transmissions must go into space and back! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN Technologies – T-Series and E-Series T-Series and E-Series • T-1 is a type of “leased line” phone and data circuit provided by phone companies in North America. • Originally built for combining multiple voice lines on one circuit, T1s combine 24 64k channels (DS0). • Each channel can carry an analog voice call or be used for data. • 24 channels of 64kbps each *should* yield bandwidth of 1.536 Mbps, however a full T1 bandwidth is 1.544 Mbps due to one extra frame bit sent for synchronization after every 192-bit frame. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. T-Series and E-Series • T-2 and T-3 are larger versions of the T-1. • T-2 is very uncommon, but T-3 is the equivalent of 28 T-1s, with total bandwidth of 44.736 Mbps. • Together, T-1s and similar circuits are referred to as the T-Series. • In Europe a very similar standard is the E-Series. • E-1 connections use thirty-two 64k channels for a total bandwidth of 2.048 Mbps. • The E-3 connection can reach speeds of 34.368Mbps, the equivalent of 16 E-1s. WAN Technologies – T-Series and E-Series (contd.) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. T-Series and E-Series • Despite being slower and often much more expensive than ADSL or Cable connections, T-1 circuits are still very common in businesses for three reasons: • Reliability – T-1 circuits often have very strong Service Level Agreements (SLAs) from the provider, guaranteeing uptime, bandwidth, latency, and packet loss. • Speed – Despite being slower than most DSL or Cable circuits, T-1s are dedicated circuits, not shared with other customers on the local loop (cable) or at the DSLAM (DSL). • Suitability – While modern phone systems may work with IP-based telephone services, many legacy phone systems are designed to work with PRI interfaces (provisioned through a T-1 or ISDN) or single analog lines (PSTN). WAN Technologies – T-Series and E-Series (contd.) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Metro Ethernet (Metro-E) • A WAN technology using plain Ethernet. • Not widely available, but often faster and less expensive than comparable broadband offerings when available. • Often designed as Ethernet to MPLS then back to Ethernet on the remote side. WAN Technologies – Metro E Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN Technologies – SONET/SDH SONET/SDH • Synchronous Optical NETwork (US) or Synchronous Digital Hierarchy (International) • Standard for Synchronous data transmission over fiber optic cables • The SONET basic data rate is 51.84Mbps, called the Optical Carrier Level or OC. • Fiber optic speeds are measured in multiples of OC: • OC-3 = 155.52 Mbps • OC-12 = 622.08 Mbps Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wavelength Division Multiplexing (WDM) • WDM is a technique for multiplexing multiple OC signals on a single fiber by using separate wavelengths of light for each. • Individual signals are multiplexed onto the carrier fiber, then demultiplexed back into the original signals at the other end. • This allows network carriers to effectively add more optical “circuits” without the necessity of adding additional lines. • Dense Wavelength Division Multiplexing (DWDM) is highly efficient, with more than 8 active wavelengths per fiber. • Coarse Wavelength Division Mutiplexing (CWDM) is less efficient, with fewer than 8 active wavelengths per fiber, but is considerably less expensive compared to DWDM. WAN Technologies - WDM Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Frame Relay • A packet switched technology that allows different customers to use the same network at the same time using individual virtual circuits (Permanent or PVC) or (Switched or SVC). • A portion of the available bandwidth is guaranteed to each user, but additional bandwidth can be used if available. • Committed Information Rate (CIR): The maximum bandwidth guaranteed for a particular user. • Access Rate: The maximum speed the Frame Relay interface can transmit. WAN Technologies – Frame Relay Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. MPLS • Multiprotocol Label Switching (MPLS) is a mechanism to route packets through a large network based on short path labels rather than network addresses. • MPLS works with any protocol (TCP, UDP, etc.) • MPLS can work over most communication technologies, including DSL, T1, ATM, Frame Relay, and IP. • MPLS can improve network traffic by minimizing routing – nodes within the MPLS cloud transfer packets based on their short path label rather than having to perform a routing lookup. • Because MPLS serves some functions at OSI layer 2 and layer 3, it’s considered a “Layer 2.5” technology. WAN Technologies - MPLS Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN Technologies - PPP PPP (Point-to-Point Protocol) • PPP is a Data Link protocol used to establish a direct connection between two nodes. • PPP works over dialup, serial cables, ISDN & T1 circuits, or SONET. • PPP-over-Ethernet or PPPoE is often used with DSL connections. • Multilink PPP bonds the underlying physical connections into one virtual pipe, so that three T1 connections at the Physical Layer are seen as a single 4.5Mbps path to a Layer 3 router. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ATM • Asynchronous Transfer Mode (ATM): a communications standard designed in the 1980’s to accommodate both high throughput transmissions, such as file downloads, and real-time, low- latency content such as voice calls or video conferencing. • Uses elements of both Circuit Switching and Packet Switching: • Transmits small, fixed-size “cells” (similar to packets) using Time Division Multiplexing. • Establishes a virtual circuit which is either fully dedicated (permanent) or switched. • Being replaced by IP-only Networks WAN Technologies - ATM Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Circuit Switching vs Packet Switching • Circuit Switching: implementing a network connection via a dedicated communications channel. • For the duration of the communication session, the circuit is 100% dedicated to the network connection. • Traditional Analog phone calls are circuit-switched connections. • Packet Switching: transmitting multiple network connections over a single medium. • Each communications steam is broken into packets, with appropriate header information to be delivered properly on the other end of the medium. • The Internet is a packet-switched network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. WAN Technologies - Wireless Wireless WANs • Wireless WAN connections via mobile phone networks are becoming more affordable and popular • Cellular Generations: • Marketing based, no clear standards until 3G • 1G: First Generation, Voice-only • 2G: Second Generation, up to 1Mbps data rate (1x) • 3G: Third Generation, up to 28MBps in theory but closer to 2Mbps in actual use • 4G: Fourth Generation, up to 300Mbps, with future versions planned for up to 1Gbps Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless WANs • GSM: Global System for Mobile Communications – the default global standard for 2G and 3G Cellular Communications • EDGE: Enhanced Data Rates for GSM Evolution – an enhanced technology to improve data speeds on 2G and 3G GSM networks • HSPA+: High Speed Packet Access – often called “3.5G”, provides higher data rates on GSM networks • CDMA: Code Division Multiple Access, also called IS-95, is an alternate communications standard to GSM, used by North American mobile phone providers including Verizon and Sprint. • LTE: Long Term Evolution, also called 4G LTE. LTE has become the dominant standard for 4G mobile phone networks, supplanting one-time alternative WiMax. WAN Technologies – Wireless (contd.) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which protocol uses label switching to determine routing? 1 PPP MPLS Circuit Switching ATM Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which protocol uses label switching to determine routing? MPLS or Multiprotocol Label Switching routes packets through a WAN using short path labels. b. PPP MPLS Circuit Switching ATM 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. A packet switched technology that allows different customers to use the same network at the same time is ______. 2 ATM Circuit Switching Dial-Up Frame Relay Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. A packet switched technology that allows different customers to use the same network at the same time is ______. Frame Relay is a packet switched technology that allows different customers to use the same network at the same time using individual virtual circuits. d. ATM Circuit Switching Dial-Up Frame Relay 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of the following WAN technologies has the fastest bandwidth? 3 OC3 ISDN T-1 3G Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which of the following WAN technologies has the fastest bandwidth? OC3 connections have a bandwidth of 155.52Mbps compared with 1.544 for a T-1, 1920k for PRI-ISDN and a theoretical 28Mbps for 3G. a. OC3 ISDN T-1 3G 3 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary ● Frequency Division Multiplexing (FDM) sends each individual signal within a non-overlapping frequency sub-band on the communications medium. ● Time Division Multiplexing (TDM) chops each individual signal into discrete chunks which are transmitted over a synchronized connection. Each chunk uses the connection for a fraction of time. ● BRI-ISDN, most common in North America, uses 2 B channels for a total bonded bandwidth of 128kbps. ● DSL allows high speed data transmission over short distances using ordinary 2-wire telephone cabling. ● T-1 is a type of “leased line” phone and data circuit provided by phone companies in North America. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn, All rights reserved. This concludes ‘WAN Technologies’ The next lesson is ‘Network Devices’

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 1: Network Theory and Architecture CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 1-5: Network Devices Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ● Define and describe the appropriate use for Routers, Switches, Hubs and Access Points. ● Identify the benefit of a Multilayer Switch (MLS). ● Explain the purpose of Firewalls, IDS, IPS, HIDS, and Content Filtering devices. ● Describe the function of Packet Shapers, Load Balancers, VPN Concentrators, and Analog Modems. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Network Devices Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Routers and Bridges Routers connect separate networks. • MUST be distinct, addressing schemes (IP subnets or similar) on each network • Routers route packets between networks by using routing tables or routing policy, forwarding packets to the next connected router closest to the packet’s destination. Bridges connect similar networks. • MUST be identical, addressing schemes (IP subnets or similar) on both sides. • Establishes separate Collision Domains, minimizing traffic across the network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Hub • Hubs are obsolete, replaced by Switches. • Hubs connect multiple wired network devices as if all were on the same cable. • All traffic is rebroadcasted to all ports on the hub. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Switch A Switch is a “Hub with Brains” • A Switch is a “Layer 2” device – it reads the MAC address from the Frame. • If the MAC address is known to be connected to a specific port on the Switch, ONLY that port receives the traffic. • Each port on a Switch is therefore a unique collision domain. • If the Switch cannot identify which port includes the destination MAC Address, the frame is forwarded to all ports. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Switch (contd.) • Simple Switches are Unmanaged and not directly accessible. They work automatically with no configuration options. • More complex Switches are Managed, with their own accessible IP address and the ability to be configured and monitored via SNMP. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. A Multilayer Switch (MLS) is a typical Switch at OSI Layer 2, but also performs Routing or other functions at Layers 3 or higher. • Advanced functions in an MLS may include: • Packet Routing • Qos and VLAN Routing • Load Balancing • Content Filtering Multilayer Switch Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Firewall A Firewall protects your network by keeping unauthorized traffic off the network. • Can be a hardware device or software • Enforces traffic rules between the public side and the private side. • Can often designate one or more private side addresses as being in the “DMZ”, Demilitarized Zone, making them open to the public side without the firewall’s defenses. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Intrusion Detection Systems (IDS) and Intrusion Prevention Systems (IPS) • IDS monitor network or system activities, looking for signs of malicious activity or policy violations. • Incidents are reported and logged • IPS include IDS functions but also attempt to stop or block the suspicious activity. • Both are network devices (appliances), but can be implemented as software applications as well. IDS/IPS Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. HIDS HOST Intrusion Detection Systems (HIDS) • A HIDS is an application running on a host computer which monitors the host for suspicious activity via system logs and active applications. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Access Point • Wireless devices can connect to each other using Ad-Hoc Mode. • No central hardware is required, but ad-hoc networks generally perform poorly and cannot connect to outside networks. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Access Point (contd.) • An Access Point connects one or more wireless devices in Infrastructure Mode. • In Infrastructure Mode, the Access Point functions as a hub for the wireless devices. • An Access Point can also connect to a Wired network, creating a transparent bridge between the wireless and wired devices. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Content Filter • A Content Filter is an appliance or program which scans network traffic for content and filters out designated content or content types. • Content filtering may be based on a Blacklist, which includes specific sites, regions, or types of content that should be filtered out. • A Whitelist designates which content should be allowed, and all other content is filtered out. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Load Balancer A Load Balancer sends network traffic through one of two or more possible pathways, to minimize network congestion on either segment. Typical load balancing algorithms include: • Scheduled • Least-Load • Fault Tolerance • Fastest Response • Content-Aware Switching Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Analog Modem Modem stands for Modulator/De-Modulator An Analog Modem modulates an analog carrier signal to encode digital information. Analog Modems connect computers via traditional phone lines at up to 56kbps. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. A Packet Shaper or Traffic Shaper controls how Packets are transmitted on a network. • Packet Shaping provides several benefits: • Prioritizing critical applications, such as VoIP or Video • Containing disruptive traffic such as large file downloads Packet Shaper Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • A VPN Concentrator accepts multiple VPN connections. • Specifically built for handling the encryption and authentication needed for multiple VPN sessions. • Can offload VPN responsibilities from a router or server VPN Concentrator Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Summary ● A Router connects separate networks with distinct addressing schemes. ● A Switch connects wired computers, with each port becoming its own collision domain. ● An Access Point is necessary for a wireless network to operate in infrastructure mode and to connect to a wired network. ● An Intrusion Detection System (IDS) monitors network traffic looking for malicious activity. ● An Intrusion Prevention System (IPS) monitors for and attempts to block suspicious activity. Lesson 1-6: Network Concepts Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ● Describe the function of encapsulation and de-encapsulation. ● Discuss how segments, packets, frames, and bits work together. ● Describe multiplexing, demultiplexing, TDM, and FDM. ● Define baseband, broadband, bit rates, baud rates, and sampling size. ● Explain what collisions are and how CSMA/CD and CSMA/CA are used to mitigate collisions. ● Discuss the role of TCP, UDP, and ICMP. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Physical Layer: Bits • Data Link Layer: Frames • Network Layer: Packets or Datagrams • Transport Layer: Segments • How do these relate to each other? Recap: OSI Model 1 - Physical 2 - Data Link 3 - Network 4 - Transport 5 - Session 6 - Presentation 7 -Application Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Encapsulation (in networking) means designing communications in modular protocols, so that logically separate functions can be communicated by including or encapsulating information inside higher level objects. Encapsulation and De-Encapsulation THING THING Encapsulated THING De-Encapsulated Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Physical Layer (Layer 1) sends Bits (1s and 0s): • For convenience, these are grouped into 8-bits each, called Octets (or Bytes) Encapsulation and De-Encapsulation (contd.) 0 1 1 0 0 1 1 0 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Scenario: An application on a network device needs to send data to another device on a TCP/IP network. • At the Transport Layer, Layer 4, the data is Encapsulated in a TCP Segment: The Header Data includes important information about the size, destination port, urgency of the data, and a sequence number. • Combined TCP Header and Data form a TCP Segment, which is passed to layer 3 for continued processing. Creating a TCP Segment TCP Header Data Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The new TCP Segment: At Layer 3, the Network Layer, IP information must be added, so the segment(s) will reach their destination. Each segment is encapsulated into an IP Packet: TCP Header Segment to Packet Data IP Header Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. This IP Packet: Then arrives at the data link layer, Layer 2, to be encapsulated again as a Frame. Frames are often smaller than packets, meaning one packet must be broken into multiple frames. Packet to Frame IP Header Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Final Ethernet Frame: • This is transmitted as 1s and 0s by the Physical Layer, Layer 1. The Ethernet Frame Preamble, Frame Delimiter, MAC Destination, MAC Source, 802.1Q tag, Ethertype Payload (portion of the Packet): . Frame Check Sequence (CRC) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Encapsulation and De-Encapsulation Summary: Data Is Encapsulated into a Segment: TCP Header Data IP Header Which is Encapsulated into a Packet Which is Encapsulated into one or more Frames Preamble, Frame Delimiter, MAC Destination, MAC Source, 802.1Q tag, Ethertype Payload (portion of the Segment): . Frame Check Sequence (CRC) DATA (Layer 5+) SEGMENT (Layer 4) PACKET (Layer 3) FRAME (Layer 2) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • On the receiving device, the process is reversed (“De-Encapsulation”): De-Encapsulation Preamble, Frame Delimiter, MAC Destination, MAC Source, 802.1Q tag, Ethertype Payload (portion of the Packet): Frame Check Sequence (CRC) Data IP Header TCP Header Data Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. OSI / Encapsulation Summary • Layer 4, Transport, encapsulates data as Segments • Layer 3, Network, encapsulates Segments as Packets • Layer 2, Data Link, encapsulates and splits Packets into Frames • Layer 1, Physical, transmits Frames as Bits. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. TCP/IP Suite • IP (Internet Protocol): Deliver packets based on IP Addresses • TCP (Transmission Control Protocol): Connection- oriented protocol which provides reliable, ordered, error-checked Segments in conjunction with IP • UDP (User Datagram Protocol): Connectionless protocol, able to send Datagrams (similar to Segments) faster than TCP, but with no guarantee of delivery or sequence. • ICMP (Internet Control Message Protocol): Used by network devices to send error messages such as host unreachable or service unavailable. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. TCP/IP Suite (contd.) • Other Services: • DHCP • DNS • PPP • ARP • IP: Two versions, IPv4 and IPv6 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Modulation Techniques • Multiplexing: Combining multiple communication streams onto one physical media. • De-Multiplexing: Reconstituting mutiplexed communication streams from one physical media. • Multiplexing can be Analog or Digital Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Modulation Techniques ( contd.) • Time-Division Multiplexing (TDM): Transmitting multiple data signals via a synchronized physical link, so that each signal appears on the link for a fraction of time. • Frequency-Division Multiplexing (FDM): Transmitting multiple data signals over a physical link by allocating a specific frequency range to each signal. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Modulation Techniques (contd.) • Time-Division Multiplexing (TDM): •Frequency-Division Multiplexing (FDM) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Binary 0 0 1 0 1 1 1 0 128 64 32 16 8 4 2 1 Numbering Systems • Decimal: 0 through 9 • Binary: 0 or 1 • Hexadecimal: 0 through F • Octal: 0 through 7 • The charts to the right express the number “46” (decimal) in the different numbering systems Hexadecimal 0 0 0 2 E 65,536 4096 256 16 1 Octal 0 0 0 5 6 4096 512 64 8 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Baseband vs Broadband • Baseband: When all the bandwidth of a physical media is used by one signal. • Ethernet is a baseband technology, e.g. “100baseT” • Broadband: When the bandwidth of a physical media is shared by multiple signals. • Example: Cable or DSL-based internet service Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bitrate vs Baud rate • Baud Rate: In the 1970s and 1980s, the speed of telephone modems was expressed as Baud Rate • Named for French engineer Jean-Maurice-Emily Baudot • Measures electronic state changes per second: 1200 baud = 1200 voltage changes on a physical line in one second. • Originally Baud rate = Bitrate. • The term became unclear when modems began transmitting multiple bits per state change. • Bit Rate: The number of bits transmitted per second. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Sampling Size • When converting analog to digital or vice-versa, the Sampling Size determines the number of times the analog signal is measured at regular intervals. • Higher Sampling Size yields a more precise measurement and more accurate data. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wavelength • The Wavelength of a signal is the measurement of the spatial period of the wave – the distance between the repetitions of the wave. • Wavelength in networking most commonly applies to: • Fiber Optic cabling, where data is transmitted as wavelengths of light. • Wireless networks, where data is transmitted as wavelengths on a radio frequency. wavelength Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Collisions • Collision: When multiple devices share one physical medium, and two or more devices attempt to transmit at the same time. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Collisions (contd.) • Carrier Sense Multiple Access with Collision Detection (CSMA/CD) is the method which Ethernet and other wired technologies use to minimize Collisions and their associated problems. • Host checks for the presence of another signal before and during transmission • If another transmission is detected, Host broadcasts a jam signal to alert all devices to the collision. • Host waits for a randomly generated amount of time, then attempts retransmission. • Also referred to as CDMA/CD for “Carrier Detect Multiple Access”, though CDMA is also an unrelated WAN technology. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Collisions (contd.) • Carrier Sense Multiple Access with Collision Avoidance (CSMA/CA) is an alternative to CSMA/CD. • Superior to CSMA/CD on Wireless Networks because: • Wireless devices cannot easily detect signals while they are transmitting • Wireless devices may communicate with an Access Point but not be able to receive transmissions from other devices connected to the same Access Point (the “Hidden Node” problem). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Collisions (contd.) • In CSMA/CA: • A node listens to the shared medium to determine when the medium is not in use by other nodes. (Note – this may be inaccurate due to “Hidden Nodes”) • The node then sends an RTS, “Request To Send” signal to the Access Point (or receiver). • If clear, the Access Point will issue a CTS, “Clear To Send” signal back to the requesting node. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Collisions (contd.) • The node then sends an entire Frame, and waits for the Access Point to acknowledge correct receipt of the Frame. • If no acknowledgement is received, the node assumes a collision has occurred, waits for an exponentially- increasing backoff period, then tries again. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Lesson 1-7: Wired Connections Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ● Define and Describe the following types of wired network connections: After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Wired Connections • 10BaseT • 100BaseT • 1000BaseT • 1000BaseTX • 10GBaseT • 10Base2 • 100BaseFX • 10GBaseSR • 10GBaseER • 10GBaseSW • Discuss Ethernet over HDMI and Ethernet over power line. • List the wire colors of the EIA/TIA 568A and 568B wiring standards. • Describe DOCSIS. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Common Cable Types Category 1: Two twisted wire pairs, only suitable for voice. Category 3: Four twisted wire pairs, data speeds up to 10Mbps Category 5: Improved version of Cat 3, data speeds up to 100Mbps Category 5e: Improved version of Cat 5, data speeds up to 1Gbps Category 6: Improved version of Cat5e, data speeds up to 10Gbps Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Ethernet Cabling Ethernet cabling types use the naming convention “N<base/broad>X”, where: • N=Signaling rate in Mbps • X=Identifier for the cabling scheme • <base/broad> = Base for baseband or Broad for broadband • Example: 10baseT = 10Mbps, baseband, Twisted-pair Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Coax Cabling standards • 10base5 “thicknet”: Coaxial Ethernet standard used with heavy RG-8 or RG-6 coax cabling. • The “5” represents the maximum segment length of 500m. • 10base2 “thinnet”: Coaxial Ethernet standard used with RG-58 coax cabling. • The “2” represents a theoretical maximum segment length of 200m, though 185m is more likely. • Both use 50ohm impedance and are most commonly used in bus topology networks. • Mostly obsolete. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Twisted-pair Cabling Standards • 10baseT: 10Mbps, 4 pairs (2 used), up to 100m on Cat3+ • 100baseT:100Mbps, 4 pairs (2 used), up to 100m on Cat5+ • 1000baseT: 1Gbps, 4 pairs (all used), up to 100m on Cat5e+ • 10GbaseT: 10Gbps, 4 pairs (all used), up to 100m on Cat6a Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Twisted-Pair Cabling Why the twist? • Electromagnetic Interference (EMI) on untwisted wire pairs can create more noise on the wire closer to the EMI source. • With twisted-pair cabling, EMI interference is balanced across the pair, canceling out the interference. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. EIA/TIA 568A Wiring Standards EIA/TIA 568A and 568B EIA/TIA 568B Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Fiber Optic Cabling • 100BaseFX: 100Mbps on two strands of optical fiber, up to 2km • 10GbaseSR: “short reach”, 10Gbps on single-mode fiber, up to 400m • 10GbaseER: “extended reach”, 10Gbps on single- mode fiber, up to 40km • 10GbaseSW: 10Gbps on multi-mode fiber, up to 300m (designed for SONET equipment) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Other Ethernet Standards Ethernet over Power Line: • Allows Ethernet transmission over existing power lines • Can be used by power companies to provide broadband, or used within a home or office to supply wired Ethernet to areas where it is difficult to run new cabling. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Other Ethernet Standards (contd.) • Ethernet over HDMI • In theory, it combines Ethernet signaling with audio, video, and potentially other streams on a single HDMI cable. • In practice, very few devices support Ethernet over HDMI and practical uses seem limited. • Ethernet over Power Line and Ethernet over HDMI are part of the IEEE 1905.1-2013 standard. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. IEEE • The IEEE (Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers) is a global professional association which publishes standards in areas including Power, IT, and Telecommunications. • Wiring standards including 10baseT, 10GbaseSR, etc. are from the IEEE • IEEE 1905.1-2013 is a recent standard designed to provide a common interface for technologies including Ethernet over Powerline, Ethernet over HDMI, and 802.11x wireless standards. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DOCSIS Data Over Cable Interface Specification (DOCSIS) is a broadband standard for delivering high bandwidth data over cable TV (CATV) systems. • DOCSIS 1.x and 2.x can deliver one channel of 42.88Mbps bandwidth downstream and 10 to 30Mbps upstream. • DOCSIS 3.0 added support for IPv6 and multiple bonded channels. • DOCSIS 3.1 can deliver up to 10Gbps downstream and 1Gbps upstream by using available spectrum more efficiently. Summary ● Category 3 cables use four twisted wire pairs for data speeds up to 10Mbps. ● Category 5 cables are improved version of Cat 3, data speeds up to 100Mbps. ● 1000baseT is a 1GBps cabling standard which uses all 4 pairs of wires on a Category 5e+ cable for up to 100m. ● 100BaseFX is a fiber optic cabling standard which transmits at up to 100Mbps on two strands of optical fiber at a distance of up to 2km. ● The IEEE (Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers) is a global professional association which publishes standards in areas including Power, IT, and Telecommunications. ● Data Over Cable Interface Specification (DOCSIS) is a broadband standard for delivering high bandwidth data over cable TV (CATV) systems. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wired Connections • There are many types of wired connections, both copper and fiber-optic, which a networking professional should be familiar with. • Our goal in this module is to review the most common types and their benefits. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Some of the most common cable types are RJ-11, RJ12, RJ-14, RJ-45, and RJ-48 • RJ stands for “Registered Jack” and describes the physical construction, wiring, and signaling of the connection • Many RJ connectors look alike and may function similarly, due to similar construction RJ Connectors Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. RJ11, RJ12, and RJ14 RJ11, RJ12, and RJ14 use 6-pin connectors • RJ11 is traditional analog “phone cable” and uses only the center two wires on the 6-pin cable • Other pins may or may not be wired but will not be used in RJ11 signaling • May be labeled “6P4C” or similar • RJ12 uses all 6 wires • RJ14 uses 4 wires Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. RJ45 and RJ48C • RJ45 cables use 8-pin connectors and 4 wire pairs • Category 3, Category 5, Category 5e, and similar wiring standards use RJ45 cables and connectors • The signal is carried on pins 1,2,3, and 6 • RJ48C is a similar 8-pin, 4 wire pair cable used in ISDN / DS1 demarc connections, with the signal carried on pins 1,2,4, and 5 • In practice RJ45 and RJ48C often use the same cables Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. DB9 and DB25 Connector • DB25 Connector: 25 pin physical connection, used for RS/232 Serial Ports and Parallel Printer ports “D” refers to the shape of the connector, “B” is a size designator indicating 25 pins. ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • DB9 Connector: 9 pin physical connection, most often used with RS/232 Serial Ports on computers or routers • Technically it’s a “DE-25” connector, with D being the shape and E indicating a size of 9 pins, but DB9 is the popular designation DB9 and DB25 Connector Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. RG Cables and Connectors RG-59/U and RG- 6 are popular types of coaxial cables • Coaxial cables have two conductors: an inner wire and an outer tubular conducting shield • The coax design minimizes electromagnetic interference (EMI) from outside sources, and also minimizes the EMI generated by the cable itself Why “RG”? RG or “Radio Guide” classifications began in World War II. The numbers are sequential, meaning “RG-6” was the 6th type of cable, which was assigned an RG designation. ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. RG-59 vs. RG-6 RG-6 is the most commonly used coaxial cable type, used for cable television. RG-6, also called RG-6/U for “general utility use”, has these characteristics: • 75 ohm impedance • 18AWG center conductor RG-59 is a thinner, cheaper alternative to RG-6, sometimes used to connect devices such as DVD players to TVs. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • RG-58, also called Thinnet, or cheapernet, was a popular cable type to carry 10base2 Ethernet signals. • RG-8 (“Thicknet”) was used to carry 10base5 Ethernet signals and is also popular in amateur radio setups. RG-58 and RG-8 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. BNC Connectors • BNC connectors are used by older 10base2 networks, and by some video connections. • BNC stands for “Bayonet Neill-Concelman” Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Couplers • BNC couplers connect two BNC cables. • Similarly, UTP couplers connect two RJ cables. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. F Connectors • F Connectors attach to raw coax cable to create a threaded connection. The connector carries the outer “shield” signal while the center conductor of the coax cable is used as the male connector. • An F Coupler connects two coax cables with F connectors Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Blocks • 66 Block – a punch down block used to connect sets of wire in a building or office. Traditionally used for phone cabling, 66 blocks are unsuitable for data. • 110 Block – similar to the 66 block, the more modern 110 blocks are used for telephone and data cabling. Some 110 blocks are certified for up to Cat5 and Cat6 wiring. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Common Cable Types and Distances Category 3: 10Mbps, 100m Category 5: 100Mbps, 100m Category 5e: 1Gbps, up to 100m Category 6: 10Gbps, up to 55m Category 6a: 10Gbps, up to 100m Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Shielded vs. Unshielded Shielded Cable More expensive, adds EMI shielding to the cable. Unshielded Cable Most commonly used type Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Plenum Cable : More expensive than PVC, Plenum cable is fire retardant and thus suitable for the plenum spaces in buildings (where air circulates). • PVC Cable: Less expensive, more commonly used form of cabling. Sheathed in PolyVinyl-Chloride, it gives off deadly gases when burned and thus Plenum cable is sometimes required by fire codes. Plenum vs. PVC Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Straight-Through cable: wires are mapped to the same pins on both ends. (1-1, 2-2, 3-3, etc.) • Crossover cable (X designation): TX and RX lines are crossed along the cable. Crossover cables are sometimes required to connect two network devices, such as switches, to each other. • Rollover cable: wire order is exactly reversed on the opposite end. (1-8, 2-7, 3-6, etc.) Straight-Through vs. Crossover vs. Rollover Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Standard End EIA/TIA 568B Crossover Cable Crossover End Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copper vs. Fiber • Copper: • Cheap • Flexible • Subject to EMI and RFI • Limited distance (100m maximum, typically) • Fiber Optic: • Expensive • More difficult to install • Easier to damage • Immune to EMI/RFI interference • Transmits up to 40km, harder to troubleshoot • Requires more expensive tools and equipment to install and test. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Fiber Connectors– Full Size ST – “Straight Tip” SC –Subscriber, Square, or Standard Connector FC – Ferrule Connector or Fiber Channel Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Fiber Connectors–Small Form Factor MTRJ –Mechanical Transfer Registered Jack LC – Lucent, Little, or Local connector Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Fiber Optic Cables consist of: • A core of one or more glass or plastic strands • Clad in an outer sheath of glass or plastic which reflects light back into the core • An armor layer, usually made of Kevlar, to protect the core • An outer shell of PVC or Plenum Fiber Cables Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Single-Mode Fiber vs. Multimode Fiber Single-Mode One strand of glass fiber, one signal, very long distances. Yellow jacket. Multimode Larger core, multiple strands/signals, shorter distance, multiple propagation modes. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Fiber couplers are available to join fiber optic cables for each connector type Joining Fiber Optic Cables Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • UPC – Ultra-Polished Connector or Ultra Physical Contact • Core strands are cut perfectly straight, causing reflections back into the core, which produces a loss of signal called “return loss”. • UPC connectors are generally blue. • APC – Angle Polished Connector or Angled Physical Contact • Core strands are cut at a precise 8 degree angle, causing reflections to bounce into the side cladding, which minimizes return loss. • APC connectors are generally green. APC vs. UPC Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Media Converters convert fiber optic signals to other media. Common types include: • Single-Mode Fiber to Ethernet • Multimode Fiber to Ethernet • Fiber to Coax • Single mode to Multimode Media Converters Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Common cabling tools include: • Cable Crimpers – used to crimp connectors onto copper cables • Coaxial • Twisted Pair Cabling Tools Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Wire Strippers – used to strip the outer insulation from cables • Punch down tool – used to punch twisted pair cables onto 66 Blocks, patch panels, or outlets • Snips – used to cut cables Cabling Tools (contd.) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • OTDR – Optical Time-Domain Reflectometer – used to test and characterize fiber optic cables • Cable Certifier – used to perform advanced tests on twisted pair cables to confirm the performance as Category 6, Category 5, etc. Cabling Tools (contd.) Summary ● RJ11 is traditional analog “phone cable” and uses only the center two wires on the 6-pin cable ● RG-6 is the most commonly used coaxial cable type, with 75 ohm impedance and an 18AWG core conductor ● A 66 Block is a type of punch down block used to connect sets of wire in a building or office ● Category 5 cabling is certified for up to 100Mbps bandwidth and up to 100m distance ● Multimode fiber is different from single-mode in that it has a larger core, with multiple strands/signals, operates over a shorter distance, and can have multiple propagation modes Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. Lesson 1-9: Wireless Connections Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ● Define and describe the following types of wireless connections: • 802.11a • 802.11b • 802.11g • 802.11n • 802.11ac After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • In 1997, the IEEE (Institute of Electrical and Electronic Engineers) created the 802.11 specification for wireless computer communication. • In 1999 a trade association called the Wi-Fi Alliance formed to certify equipment to the 802.11 standards. • Equipment certified by the Wi-Fi Alliance uses this official logo, however non-certified equipment is also usually compatible. Wi-Fi Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Over 12 accepted 802.11 protocols exist, however the most common are: • 802.11a • 802.11b • 802.11g • 802.11n • 802.11ac • All use the 900MHz, 2.4GHz, and/or 5GHz frequency ranges, which are unregulated for public use in most countries. Wireless Connections Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Data signals are encoded into radio frequencies using modulation. • Common modulation techniques include: • DSSS: Direct Sequence Spread Spectrum, used by 802.11b and 802.11g • OFDM: Orthogonal Frequency Division Multiplexing, used by 802.11a, 802.11g, 802.11n, and 802.11ac Modulation Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 802.11a • 802.11a • Supports up to 54Mb/s • Uses the 5GHz band and OFDM multiplexing • Comparatively limited range due to signal absorption and interference Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • 802.11b • Supports up to 11Mb/s • Uses the 2.4GHz band and DSSS multiplexing • Longer range and lower cost compared to 802.11a • 802.11g • Supports up to 54Mb/s • Uses the 2.4GHz band and OFDM multiplexing • Backward compatible with 802.11b 802.11b and g Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Supports up to 600Mb/s • Uses the 2.4GHz OR 5GHz bands • Uses HT protection to coordinate signaling with legacy a, b, and g devices • Uses multiple-input multiple-output (MIMO) antennas to increase bandwidth 802.11n Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Supports up to 1.3Gb/s • Uses 2.4GHz and 5GHz bands • Similar to 802.11n with enhancements • 160MHz channel bandwidth (compared to 40MHz in 802.11n, 20MHz in older standards) 802.11ac Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which wireless protocol NEVER uses the 5GHz frequency? 1 802.11a 802.11b 802.11n 802.11ac Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which wireless protocol NEVER uses the 5GHz frequency? 802.11b only uses the 2.4GHz frequency, while 802.11a and ac always use the 5GHz frequency and 802.11n may use the 5GHz frequency. b. 802.11a 802.11b 802.11n 802.11ac 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which is the maximum throughpout of 802.11g? 2 54Mbps 11Mbps 600Mbps 10Gbps Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which is the maximum throughpout of 802.11g? The maximum throughput of an 802.11g connection is 54Mbps. a. 54Mbps 11Mbps 600Mbps 10Gbps 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary ● 802.11a supports up to 54Mbps using the 5GHz band. ● 802.11b supports up to 11Mbps using the 2.4GHz band. ● 802.11g supports up to 54Mbps using the 2.4GHz band. ● 802.11n supports up to 600Mbps using the 2.4GHz OR 5GHz band and MIMO. ● 802.11ac supports up to 1.3Gbps using the 2.4GHz and 5GHz bands, MIMO, and 160MHz channel bandwidth. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn, All rights reserved. This concludes ‘Wireless Connections’ The next lesson is ‘Network Services and Applications’

Introduction to Cybersecurity Cybersecurity Fundamentals Learning Objectives Explain the fundamentals of cybersecurity Identify threat actors, attacks, and mitigation Describe security policies, procedures, standards, and baseline By the end of lessons you will be able to: Elaborate the cybersecurity mitigation methods Fundamentals of Cybersecurity What Is Cybersecurity? A set of technologies used for protecting systems, networks, and programs from digital attacks, damage, and unauthorized access. Attack Damage Unauthorized Access Address Threats Why Cybersecurity? The world relies on technology more than ever before, and as a result digital data creation has surged. Increased rate of cyber crime Increased demand to protect data Presence of crime syndicates Presence of cyber armies Presence of financial frauds Information Security and Cybersecurity Refers to processes and tools designed to protect sensitive information Encompasses paper documents and digital and intellectual property Cybersecurity Is a set of techniques used to protect the integrity of networks, programs, and data Is a component of information security Information Security Cyber Crime Statistics 25+ million records exposed everyday in 2018 Cyber Crime to cost $6 trillion in 2021 Healthcare: Ransomware attacks will quadruple 300 billion passwords exist worldwide in 2020 24,000 malicious mobile apps blocked daily 60% of fraud originates from mobile devices Factors Affecting Cybersecurity Technology Business Plans Platforms and tools Risk tolerance Outsourcing service providers Industry trends Network connectivity Level of IT complexity New or emerging security tools Operational support for security 1 2 3 4 5 Nature of business Mergers and acquisitions and partnerships CIA Triad Authorized parties can access the information CIA Triad Information must be available on demand CIA Triad Authorized people can add, remove, or alter information Governance, Risk Management, and Compliance (GRC) Scope of GRC Governance, Risk Management, and Compliance of every organization is different and varies based on the type of organization. Mission Regulations Size It depends on organization mission, size, industry, culture, and legal regulations. Culture Industry Responsibility of GRC The ultimate responsibility of the GRC program is to protect their assets and operations IT, including their infrastructure and information. GRC Governance Risk Management Compliance The board of directors and senior management of an organization are responsible for Governance. Provides strategic direction Ascertains whether risk is being managed appropriately Ensures that the objectives are achieved Verifies that the organization's resources are being used responsibly It is the process by which the organization manages risks to acceptable levels. These risks may include investment risk, physical risk, and cyber risk. Governance Risk Management Compliance GRC It is the act of adhering to mandated requirements defined by laws and regulations. Governance Risk Management Compliance GRC Roles of Cybersecurity Cybersecurity Roles The success of a cybersecurity role is ultimately the responsibility of the board of directors. Security Management Cybersecurity Practitioners Executive Committee Board of Directors Approaches to Cybersecurity Compliance-based security Risk-based security Ad-hoc approach Cybersecurity: Key Terms Cybersecurity: Key Terms Inherent risk Residual risk Illustration: Basics of Cybersecurity Threat Actors, Attacks, and Mitigation Threat Actor A threat actor or malicious actor is a person or entity that is responsible for an event or incident that impacts or has the potential to impact the safety or security of another entity. Threat Actor Categories Script kiddies Hactivist Competitors Organized crime Insiders Nation states APT Threat Actor categories are: Threats to a System Natural environmental threats Supply system threats Man-made threats Sociopolitical threats Main threats to an organization should be considered. Malware Malware is any software that is intentionally designed to cause damage to a computer, server, client, or computer network. Types of Malware Worms Viruses Trojans Spyware Adware Rootkit Backdoor Logic bombs Ransomware Worms Worms are self-replicating codes designed to penetrate computer systems. Virus Virus is a malicious code that replicates by attaching to an executable code. Trojans Trojans are programs that claim to perform one function but does another, typically malicious. Spyware Spyware is a software aimed to steal personal or organizational information. Adware Adware is a software that displays endless ads and pop-up windows. Rootkit Rootkits are designed to modify the operating systems’ operations to facilitate non-standard functionality. Backdoor Backdoor provides the attacker with unauthorized remote access to a system by exploiting security vulnerabilities. Logic Bombs Logic bombs infect a system and lie dormant until they are triggered by a specific condition. Ransomware Ransomware attempts to extort money from the user by infecting and taking control of a victim's machine. Malware Attacks Kovter WannaCry Zeus or Zbot Ghost Mirai Denial-of-Service Attack The purpose of DoS is to prevent access to the target system. Distributed Denial-of-Service It is a denial-of-service attack employing multiple attacking systems. Distributed Denial-of-Service The goal of DDoS is to prevent access to a specific system. DoS/DDoS Attacks GitHub was hit with 1.35 terabits per second of traffic. GitHub: 1.35 Tbps DoS/DDoS Attacks Cloudflare: 400 Gbps The attack was directed at a single computer with vulnerability. Application Layer Attacks They target computers by causing a fault in the operating system or applications. Application Layer Attacks They refer to a type of malicious behavior designed to target the top layer in the OSI model. Application Layer Attacks Cross-site scripting Buffer overflow Domain hijacking DoS/DDoS SQL injection DNS spoofing Software Codes and Security Programmers are responsible to write safe and high quality codes. Software Codes and Security Source codes are statements written using a computer programming language. Software Codes and Security Code review is a systematic examination or peer review of source code. Find mistakes Improve software quality Software Testing Methods Evaluates the security of software without running it Evaluates the security of software in a runtime environment Static Testing Dynamic Testing Software Testing Methods In March 2018, hackers hit Saks Fifth Avenue and Lord & Taylor, stealing debit and credit cards. 5 million records breached Software Testing Methods In May 2018, the concert and sporting event ticketing website, ticketfly was vandalized, taken down, and disrupted for a week. Security Attacks In August 2018, Russian hackers made millions selling credit card details stolen from almost 245,000 British Airways customers. Social Engineering It is the art of manipulating people, so they give up their confidential information violating the security principle. Social Engineering Attack Categories Whaling Phishing Phishing Spear Phishing There are several attack categories of social engineering. Social Engineering Attack Categories It is a fraudulent attempt to obtain sensitive information. It is targeted to a specific group or an individual. It targets wealthy and prominent individuals. Spear Phishing Phishing Whaling Phishing Social Engineering Attack: Ethereum Classic In 2017, Ethereum Classic website was hacked resulting in the loss of thousands of dollars in cryptocurrency. Social Engineering Attack: Ethereum Classic Impersonated Ethereum owner Gained access to domain registry Redirected the domain to their server Extracted cryptocurrency from the victims Security Cybersecurity Mitigation Methods Information Technology Control An IT control is a procedure or policy that provides a reasonable assurance that: IT used by an organization is operating as intended The organization is in compliance with laws and regulations Data is reliable Countermeasure Computers Networks Operating systems It is an action or method that is applied to prevent, avert, or reduce potential threats to: Servers Information systems Countermeasure It helps to mitigate or reduce the potential risk. Control Categories Administrative controls Technical controls Physical controls Administrative Controls These are procedures and policies used to define employee actions toward sensitive information. Technical Controls These are hardware or software mechanisms used to protect important and confidential assets. Physical Controls These are security measures designed to deny unauthorized access. Physical Controls Deterrent Preventive Corrective Recovery Detective Compensating Defense in Depth or Layered Approach It is the act of using multiple layers of security controls to protect the integrity of information. Defense in Depth or Layered Approach Its intent is to provide increased security through intentional redundancy based on multi-layered security approach. Technical Personnel Procedural Physical Defense in Depth or Layered Approach Identity Management It is an organizational process for identifying, authenticating, and authorizing individuals or groups of people. Identified Authenticated Authorized Identity Management It enables the right users to access the right resources at the right time for the right reasons. IAM Components Authorization Authentication Central user repository User Management The components of IAM are: Identification and Authentication Identify a user or an application in the system Identification Authentication Prove that a user or an application is genuine Identification and Authentication Password Location Biometric Token card Something you know Something you have Where you are Something you are or do Multi-Factor Authentication It is an authentication method where a user is granted access after presenting two or more evidences. Two-Factor Authentication It is a subset of multi-factor authentication, confirming that users are granted access with a combination of two different factors. Multi-Factor Authentication It is an authentication method where a user is granted access after presenting two or more evidences. Authorization It is the process of determining what types of activities, resources, or services a user is permitted. Authorization A user may be authorized for different types of activity once authenticated. Accountability It is the traceability of actions performed on a system to a specific system entity. Accountability User identification and authentication support accountability User ID and password destroy accountability Auditing It is a manual or a systematic measurable technical assessment of a system or application. Reviewing applications and OS access controls Analyzing physical access to the systems Performing security vulnerability scans Interviewing staff Monitoring It describes the process of threat and data breach detection. Defining the behavior types to trigger alerts Taking actions on alerts as needed Patch Management It involves acquiring, testing, and installing multiple patches to an administered computer system. Patch Management Tasks Maintain knowledge of available patches Decide appropriate patches for particular systems Ensure that patches are installed properly Test systems after installation Document all associated procedures Patch Management: Example The outbreak of WannaCry ransomware became large and intense because of a missing security patch. System Hardening It is a collection of tools, techniques, and best practices to reduce vulnerability. Infrastructure Technology applications Systems Firmware System Hardening: Purpose It eliminates security risks and secures a system by reducing its attack surface. System Hardening Activities Hardening activities for a computer system includes: Update security patches and hotfixes on time Monitor security bulletins Close certain ports Use encryption Remove unnecessary programs and user accounts Create strong passwords Install anti-virus and spyware protection system Deny file sharing Change Control It is a systematic approach to manage all changes made to a product or system. Change Control: Purpose Services are not disrupted No unnecessary changes are made All changes are documented Resources are used efficiently Change Control: Purpose Change request Change approval board Implementation Review Possible rollback Formal RFC Asset Management It is the systematic process of developing, operating, maintaining, upgrading, and disposing of assets cost-effectively. Asset Management Lifecycle 1 2 3 4 5 Retirement and disposal Maintain Procurement Deploy and discover Support Data Management Data is the smallest piece of information in any form. Text documents Images Software programs Audio clips Data Management It is an administrative process to ensure the accessibility, reliability, and timeliness of the data for its users. Acquiring data Validating data Storing data Protecting data Processing data States of Data They describe the different modes whereby data is used by a computing equipment. Three Basic States of Data Data at rest Data in transit Data in use Information Lifecycle Archival: Backup, protection, and retention Disposal: Stored data for destruction Acquisition: Indexed system data Use: Challenges in protection Information Lifecycle It is an ongoing process Metadata must be at the right classification level Classification level must be attached to the information lifecycle It helps indicate the level of data protection It helps ensure data is protected Encryption It describes the different modes whereby data is used by a computing equipment. Encryption Encryption Protects information stored on computers Protects data in transit over networks Verifies the authenticity of a transaction Deters and detects alterations of data Cryptography Cryptography is the science of protecting information by encoding it into an unreadable format. Cryptography Factors Influencing Effective Encryption The inability to decrypt an entire cipher text Algorithm strength, secrecy, and difficulty of compromising a key The non-existence of back doors Types of Encryption Symmetric Encryption Asymmetric Encryption Symmetric Encryption • Uses one key to encrypt and decrypt • Uses less processing power • Shares the key with the receiver Symmetric encryption is based on the same key or private key to encrypt plain text and decrypt ciphertext. Symmetric Encryption 64-bit Data Encryption Standard (DES) Advanced Encryption Standard (AES) 128-bit to 256-bit Common private key cryptography systems: Asymmetric Encryption Solves the problem of sharing the key with the receiver Asymmetric Encryption Services of cryptography: Authentication Non-repudiation Confidentiality Validates the sender’s identity Prevents denial of action Controls who reads the data Incident Response It is an organized approach to address and manage the aftermath of a security breach. Incident Response: Goals Manages potential disruption to IT service Minimizes the adverse impact on business operations Reduces damage, recovery time, and costs Has normal service operations within SLAs Security Training It is an organized approach to addressing and managing the aftermath of a security breach or cyber attack. Security Awareness It is the process of exposing people to security issues so that they may be able to recognize them and better respond to them. Key Takeaways Cybersecurity refers to a set of techniques used to protect the integrity of network programs and data from attack, damage, and unauthorized access. Malware is a software that is designed to cause damage to a computer, server, client, or network. The types of malware include worm, spyware, virus, trojan, and logic bomb. Strategic plan, tactical plan, and operational plan are the types of security management plans. Change control is a systematic approach for managing all changes made to a product or system.

Lesson 2-1: Monitoring Tools Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: ● Describe the importance of Network Monitoring Tools ● Explain the function of a Packet Analyzer ● Discuss the uses of a Port Scanner ● Explain SNMP and its role in network monitoring ● Differentiate between Packet Sniffing and Packet Flow Monitoring ● Explain the importance of Temperature, Humidity, and Power Monitoring ● Describe the function of Wireless Survey Tools and Wireless Analyzers Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Things You CAN See There are some things you can see with your eyes on a network, like: • Disconnected cables • The IP address in a configuration window • Link Indicator lights • Smoke, fire, and physical damage Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Things You CAN’T See • Network activity • Outside hackers snooping through your files • Unusual network traffic • Network bottlenecks • Security vulnerabilities Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Monitoring Tools Network monitoring tools give you insight into what is really happening on your network. These can include: • Packet Sniffers (aka Packet or Network Analyzers) • Port Scanners • Interface Monitoring Tools • SNMP Management Tools • Power and Environmental Monitoring Tools • Wireless Survey and Analyzer Tools Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Packet Sniffers Packet Sniffers (aka Packet Analyzers or Network Analyzers) provide insight into packets on the local network. • Sniffers work by capturing all packets transmitted across the network interface • Promiscuous Mode allows the capture of all packets, not just ones sent to or from the local machine (if supported) • Packet Sniffer programs are limited to traffic on the local segment • Packet Sniffer devices can intercept packets in other segments (e.g. between the router and firewall) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Packet Sniffers (contd.) • Captured packets can include just header information or the entire packet • Decoded header info can be useful to identify: • Network problems • Intrusion attempts • Network misuse • Top Talkers (devices that send the most) • Top Listeners (devices that receive the most) Common Packet Sniffer applications include Wireshark, NetMon, and Packet Peeper ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Packet Flow Monitoring • Cisco routers and some independent tools use a function called NetFlow to do Packet Flow Monitoring. • A “Flow” is an aggregated set of packets between two devices and use the same service, protocol, and ports. • Packet Flow data can show the source of network traffic and congestion. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Port Scanners A Port Scanner scans one IP address, or a range of IP addresses, looking for open ports. Some Port Scanners can scan an IP range looking for a specific open port, sometimes called Port Sweeping. Port Scanning is generally done for one of the two reasons: • To scan someone else’s system, trying to find a way into their system • To scan your own system, to make sure there are no openings that might give others access. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Interface Monitoring Other network interface monitoring tools can provide: • Network performance • Device discovery • Interface connections and resets • Packet drops • Link speed and duplex setting Useful network monitoring tools include Solarwinds, ManageEngine, NetMon (Windows), and Network Utility (Mac) ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. SNMP Simple Network Management Protocol (SNMP) • A fundamental part of Internet Protocol (IP), SNMP functions at the Application Layer • Allows parameters on the network device to be read and/or set by Network Management Station (NMS) • Most (but not all) network devices support SNMP • Support may be unidirectional (read only) or bidirectional (read and write) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Information available via SNMP is stored in a tree of data called Management Information Base (MIB) • Each individual variable stored is referred to as an Object Identifier or OID, which looks like “1.4.6.1.3.866.2.4.1.2.1.1.1.3.2757.3” • Some devices have dozens or hundreds of OIDs, some have just a few. • The command to retrieve an OID from the MIB is called GET • To retrieve all OIDs in a MIB tree, a WALK command is used which uses GET and GETNEXT in sequence to retrieve all available SNMP data SNMP (contd.) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. SNMP (contd.) • Trap is an alert generated via SNMP on a managed device, sent to a Network Management Station (NMS), in response to predetermined criteria being met in one or more OIDs. • Typical OIDs: • Link speed • Duplex • Network address • System name • Uptime • Port statuses (for routers/switches) • Page count and ink status (for printers) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Alerts Alerts provide timely information about current network issues, security issues, vulnerabilities, and exploits. Alerts can be generated by SNMP traps, Interface Monitoring applications, or other network management tools. Alerts can be sent via: • Email • SMS Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Syslog • A Syslog server can collect messages from routers and other network devices. • Messages are aggregated, searched, and stored on the Syslog server. • Benefits: • No need to manually check each device • Log files can be stored indefinitely • Data from all network devices can be reviewed together Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. SIEM Security information and event management (SIEM) is a general term for software products and/or services combining security information management (SIM) and security event management (SEM). SIEM tools aggregate data from multiple network devices and applications, to provide: • Data correlation and alerting • Dashboards • Legal compliance and retention support • Forensic support SIEM is sometimes used interchangeably with SIM and SEM. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Environmental and Power Monitoring Three environmental elements can affect network operations and may need to be monitored: • Temperature – warm temperature in any given device may cause the device to fail or perform erratically. • Humidity – high humidity can cause corrosion in equipment, while low humidity can cause static electricity to build up and cause ESD problems • Power – a steady, stable flow of electricity, without dips, surges, and outages, is essential to keep computer equipment running smoothly. Monitoring devices for Temperature, Humidity, and Power can be integrated into any network monitoring system. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Survey Tools / Wireless Analyzers Wireless Analyzers – analyze Wi-Fi signals to determine channels in use, signal strength, bandwidth used, top talkers, and in some cases can also perform packet sniffing functions. Wireless Survey Tools – analyze signal strength and coverage area of wireless transmitters to help determine placement and troubleshoot problem areas. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. What tool would you use to monitor packets through a switch port on the network? 1 Port Scanner Packet Sniffer SNMP Interface Monitoring Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. What tool would you use to monitor packets through a switch port on the network? A packet sniffer or packet analyzer captures packets across a network interface. b. Port Scanner Packet Sniffer SNMP Interface Monitoring 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which protocol can be used to check interface settings on network devices? Summary • Network monitoring tools give you insight into things you can’t see on your network • Packet Sniffers capture all packets transmitted across a network interface • A Port Scanner scans one IP address, or a range of IP addresses, looking for open ports • SNMP allows parameters (OIDs) on a network device to be read and/or set by a Network Management Station • SIEM tools aggregate data from multiple network devices to provide data correlation, dashboards, compliance information, and forensic support • Monitoring variables such as temperature and humidity is called Environmental Monitoring • Wireless Analyzers analyze Wi-Fi signals to determine channels in use, signal strength, bandwidth used, and more Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. Lesson 2-2: Metrics and Reports Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Describe the importance of reports and metrics • Explain the meaning and purpose of a baseline • Define a bottleneck • Discuss the purpose of log management • Explain utilization and its role in removing bottlenecks • Describe attributes that may be reported by interface monitoring Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Working With Reports and Metrics Network servers, monitoring tools, and many network devices can produce logs and reports. Quantifiable data such as capacity, utilization, and bandwidth that are produced by reports or other sources are called metrics. Understanding how to read reports and analyze metrics is an important part of being a network administrator. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Baseline Reporting starts with having a Baseline – a measurement of performance under “normal” conditions. Baselines provide a basis for comparison in future reports. Creating a Baseline is called Baselining. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bottleneck Bottleneck--A point of congestion in a system that occurs when workloads arrive at a given point more quickly than that point can handle them. Addressing the bottleneck is the most efficient way to improve performance in any system. Bottlenecks are usually related to speed or bandwidth. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Log Management Log management refers to dealing with large volumes of computer-generated log messages (also known as audit records, audit trails, event-logs, etc.) Log Management includes • Log collection • Centralized aggregation • Long-term retention • Log rotation (rename, compress, delete) • Log analysis (in real-time and in bulk after storage) • Log search and reporting. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Utilization One of the most important metrics derived from logs and reports is Utilization–how much of a resource is being used. High utilization indicates a resource may be insufficient and is causing a bottleneck. Utilization is often measured for: • Bandwidth (across any segment or total) • Storage • Network device CPU • Network device memory • Wireless channel utilization Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Graphing Utilization and some other metrics are easier to understand in a graph rather than comparing a number to a baseline. Graphs usually show values over time, such as bandwidth or CPU utilization. Graphing tools are often included in network monitoring devices and applications. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Link Status Link status typically refers to a visual indicator that is favorable, neutral, or unfavorable. • Green is favorable/connected • Yellow or Red indicates issues • Off indicates disconnected Link Status can be checked visually on the device or, for many devices, via a dashboard or via SNMP Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Interface Monitoring Most managed network devices include a function to monitor their interface. This is often done via an online dashboard or control panel, which provides insight into the device’s status. Attributes monitored can include: • Link Status • Errors • Utilization • Discards • Packet drops • Interface resets • Speed and duplex Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved.
