Lesson 2-3: Configuration Management Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Discuss configuration management. • Describe the use of backups and archives in configuration management. • Explain how a baseline is used in configuration management. • Discuss issues related to on-boarding and off-boarding mobile devices. • Explain the benefit of Network Access Control (NAC) • Describe the following types of configuration documentation: Network Diagram, Asset Management, IP address utilization, Vendor Documentation, Internal Operating Procedures/Policies Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Configuration Management Network Devices have many settings – speed, duplex, WAN info, LAN info, DNS info, IP schema, port settings, routing and forwarding instructions, etc. Configuration Management refers to managing the configuration of network devices and applications in your network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Archives and Backups Data backups are essential. Configuration backups are also critical, but they are often overlooked. • Routers, firewalls, and other network devices generally provide a function to backup all configuration information to a backup file. • In the event of a hardware failure or replacement, the configuration file can be used to reprogram a replacement device with the original configuration. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Archives and Backups (contd.) Backups refer to an operational set of configuration files that can be used to reprogram equipment in the event of a hardware failure or replacement. Archives refer to multiple backups stored over a long period of time, so that prior configurations can be reviewed if needed. The terms are often used interchangeably. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Baselines We previously discussed baselines (a snapshot of “normal” functions) and baselining as it applies to network reports and metrics. Baselines are also critical for configuration management, especially when troubleshooting. Troubleshooting 101 – if it used to work, and now it doesn’t work, and nothing changed, something broke. Baselines verify the “nothing changed” element. Baseline configurations may be part of network documentation, or saved configuration files, or both. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Mobile Devices • A growing area of IT management relates to mobile devices (smartphones and tablets) and how they can be configured for an organization’s’ network. • This is referred to as Mobile Device Management (MDM). • Some organizations allow users to connect their personal mobile devices to the network – this is called Bring Your Own Device or BYOD. • MDM On-boarding determines how mobile devices are connected to the network, including what access they are granted. • MDM Off-boarding removes network settings and any organization-specific settings when a mobile device will no longer be used on the network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network Access Control (NAC) Network Access Control (NAC) is an extra layer of protection, implemented in some networks, which determines if a device is secure before granting access to the network. Posture Assessment – this is a check that determines if a device meets the criteria to connect to the network. This includes verifying if the device has up-to-date virus protection, OS security updates, disk encryption, and other protections. The Posture Assessment is performed by an agent on the device, which can be persistent (installed, always available) or non- persistent (runs at the time of connection but not permanently installed). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Documentation The key to configuration management is documentation. Up-to-date, easily accessible, and easy-to-read documentation will make it easier to check configurations settings when needed. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Documentation (contd.) Good documentation may include: • Network diagrams (logical/physical) – drawings representing the cabling and device connections for the entire network. • Asset management – a list of all network devices with key specifications and details. • IP address utilization – a list of all assigned IP addresses and/or DHCP pools used by each device. • Vendor documentation – manuals and service information for any key network devices, including serial numbers and service contract details if applicable. • Internal operating procedures/policies/standards Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Managing the configuration of network devices and applications in your network is known as ____________. 1 Backups Configuration Management Archives Network Access Control Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Managing the configuration of network devices and applications in your network is known as ____________. Configuration Management refers to managing the configuration of network devices and applications in your network. b. Backups Configuration Management Archives Network Access Control 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. BYOD Network Administration Multicast MDM Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Configuration Management refers to managing the configuration of network devices and applications in your network. • Backups refer to an operational set of configuration files that can be used to reprogram equipment in the event of a hardware failure or replacement. • Mobile Device On-boarding determines how mobile devices are connected to the network, including what access they are granted. Off-boarding removes network settings when a mobile device will no longer be used on the network. • Network Access Control (NAC) is an extra layer of protection which determines if a device is secure before granting access to the network. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 2: Operations CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 2-4: Network Segmentation Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Define network segmentation. • Discuss how performance optimization, security, compliance, and compatibility can benefit from network segmentation. • Explain why SCADA systems, legacy systems, and public networks should be segmented. • Describe honeypots and honeynets. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network Segmentation Large networks are often separated by switches, routers, or bridges into segments. Each segment is its own collision domain: • CSMA/CD functions only within the local segment. • Traffic identified as being on the local segment is not transmitted outside of the segment. • Broadcast traffic without a specific destination and traffic whose destination is not within the local segment will be transmitted outside the segment. • If a router is used to separate the segment, then broadcast traffic will remain within the segment as well (broadcast domain segmentation). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network Segmentation (contd.) There are three reasons for segmenting a network: 1. Performance Optimization – segmenting local traffic and CSMA/CD requests reduces traffic across the rest of the network (especially in Medianets) and potentially contains problems (e.g. jabber). • Load Balancing – part of Performance, load balancing refers to adjusting equipment to prevent overloading any one component such as a router or switch. Segmenting networks can be a big part of load balancing. 2. Security – restricting data flow to local segments makes it harder for hackers to access other parts of the network. • Compliance – part of Security, when data is subject to specific compliance regulations, particularly finance or privacy related, segmenting that data makes compliance and compliance reporting easier. 3. Compatibility – some network segments may use incompatible technologies. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Networks That Should Be Segmented • SCADA (Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition) – used in industrial settings, SCADA networks control industrial equipment. To prevent interference with machine operation, SCADA networks should be segmented from other general networks. • Legacy Systems – Legacy computer systems are not uncommon in business. These are often outdated and insecure, but still required to manage one or more business-critical applications. Because they lack modern antivirus and security settings, legacy systems should be segmented. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Networks That Should Be Segmented (contd.) • Public/Private networks – Many organizations offer a “guest” network to allow visitors access to the Internet and perhaps less confidential areas of their main network. The public, guest network should be its own segment. • Testing Labs – Testing labs may include secure subnets where developers test new software or IT consultants prepare new equipment or test potentially infected equipment. • Medianets – The high bandwidth demands of audio and video traveling on a medianet will almost always have negative effects on the rest of the network if they are not placed on their own segment. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Honeypots and Honeynets • Honeypots are computers designed to be attractive to intruders. The goal is for intruders to focus their attention on one or more honeypots rather than the organization’s real data. • Honeynets are entire network segments constructed as an attractive target for outside intruders. • Honeypots and Honeynets should obviously be segmented from the rest of the network, with appropriate coverage by Intrusion Detection Systems (IDS). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. How can network segmentation be used to enforce role policies? 1 Creating a separate segment for a guest network. Creating a separate segment for legacy computers. Using a router to create separate segments for HR and finance departments. Using a switch to create multiple collision domains. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. How can network segmentation be used to enforce role policies? All are valid uses of segmentation, but using a router to create separate segments for different departments can limit user access to their local department. c. Creating a separate segment for a guest network. Creating a separate segment for legacy computers. Using a router to create separate segments for HR and finance departments. Using a switch to create multiple collision domains. 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Creating a separate broadcast domain requires a ____________ . 2 Segment Router Collision Domain Switch Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Creating a separate broadcast domain requires a ____________ . Broadcast domains are separated by Routers. b. Segment Router Collision Domain Switch 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Large networks are often separated by switches, routers, or bridges into segments. • Reasons why a network might benefit from segmentation include performance optimization, load balancing, security, compliance, and compatibility. • Specific network types that are usually segmented include SCADA, legacy systems, public networks, testing labs, and medianets. • Honeypots are computers designed to be attractive to intruders. Honeynets are entire network segments constructed as an attractive target for outside intruders. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Patches and Updates’. This concludes ‘Network Segmentation’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 2: Operations CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 2-5: Patches and Updates Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Explain the importance of operating system updates and patches. • Define firmware and firmware updates. • Describe when driver updates are needed. • Explain the difference between major and minor releases. • Describe situations when upgrading or downgrading might be appropriate. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. A Secure Network To be secure, a network can’t remain static. There is strong financial motivation for hackers to find new ways around the protections built into firewalls, routers, servers, and operating systems. Manufacturers regularly release new improved software and security patches to close security holes when they are identified. Patching and updating must be a routine part of all network administration. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Operating System (OS) Updates The most common update is the OS update – applying the updates and patches provided by Microsoft, Apple, or your OS vendor. • Modern operating systems contain between 10 million and 80 million lines of code. • OS updates patch security holes discovered within the code. • Some OS updates also add new features and functionality • OS updates should generally be applied monthly or as directed by the OS vendor Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Firmware Updates Firmware is the onboard instructions on a computer or network device, which control the low level functions and load the Operating System (if applicable). • Firmware updates are issued periodically for computers, routers, firewalls, and managed switches. • Many firmware updates patch security holes discovered in the firmware, or correct known issues. • Network administrators should review all devices on the network for firmware updates periodically. Before any firmware update you should backup any settings in the device, known as a Configuration Backup. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Driver Updates • Drivers are special code that tells the operating system how to communicate with a specific device or hardware component. • Just like firmware and the OS, drivers are periodically updated to correct issues with security, performance, or to fix errors. • The OS will often update its included drivers but may not update third-party drivers. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Vulnerability Patches When vulnerabilities are discovered in an Operating System or firmware, vulnerability patches (aka critical patches/updates, security patches) are often issued very quickly. • Patches that arrive outside the normal patch schedule are called “out-of-band”. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Upgrading vs Downgrading • Upgrading is replacing your current OS or firmware with a newer version. • Generally, upgrading regularly is a good idea. Newer versions may contain new security features and other improvements. • In some cases upgrading can cause compatibility problems with previous apps or hardware devices. • Downgrading is replacing a newer OS or firmware with an older version, and is sometimes necessary for compatibility purposes. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Major vs Minor Releases • A Major Release contains substantial new functionality and bug fixes. • A Minor Release contains bug fixes and minor improvements to existing features. • Most operating systems, drivers, and firmware updates are enumerated with version numbers such as XX.YY.ZZ, where XX is the version, YY is the major release, and ZZ is the minor release. • Major releases and new versions generally include all previously issued minor releases. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. When troubleshooting problems on a network device, which of the following can help to fix the problem? 1 Install any firmware or OS patches or updates Document the problem Check SNMP parameters Escalate the issue to senior management Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. When troubleshooting problems on a network device, which of the following can help to fix the problem? Updating patches and firmware can close security vulnerabilities and fix known device issues. a. Install any firmware or OS patches or updates Document the problem Check SNMP parameters Escalate the issue to senior management 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. A minor release generally includes which of these? 2 bug fixes and small improvements a new version of the software significant improvements updated backups Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. A minor release generally includes which of these? 2 A minor release includes bug fixes and minor improvements. a. bug fixes and small improvements a new version of the software significant improvements updated backups Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Patching and updating must be a routine part of all network administration. • Operating System updates should generally be applied monthly or as directed by the OS vendor. • Firmware is the onboard instructions on a computer or network device, which control the low level functions and load the Operating System (if applicable). • Drivers are special code that tells the Operating System how to communicate with a specific device or hardware component. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘VLANs and Switches’. This concludes ‘Patches and Updates’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 2: Operations CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 2-6: VLANs and Switches Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Distinguish between a Broadcast Domain and a Collision Domain • Explain the function of the MAC Forward/Filter Table • Describe the disadvantage of using routers to break up broadcast domains • Describe the benefit of a Virtual LAN (VLAN) • Explain the difference between static and dynamic VLAN assignment • Identify the differences between managed and unmanaged switches • Describe the following switch features: port bonding, port mirroring, loop avoidance • Explain the use and benefits of Power-over-Ethernet (PoE) Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Refresher – Broadcast Domain and Collision Domain On an old-fashioned hub-based IP network, all traffic is delivered to every device. This is a very inefficient system because: • Every time a node transmits, it may collide (send while another node is also transmitting), causing both nodes to have to resend. • Packets intended for a specific device (on or off the network) are sent to every device. • Broadcast packets, such as DHCP requests, network discovery requests, and Address Resolution Protocol (ARP) requests are sent to every device. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The Benefit of a Switch A Switch is an intelligent device which always performs at least two functions: 1. Each port is its own CSMA/CD Collision Domain. 2. As frames are received on each port, the switch makes a forward/flood/filter decision based on a quick reading of the frame’s header information. Some switches will also perform loop avoidance functions. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. MAC Forward / Filter Table Port MAC Addresses 1 2 3 4 5 6 7 8 Switch is powered on or reset; table is empty Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. MAC Forward / Filter Table Port MAC Addresses 1 00:0a:95:9b:68:16 2 3 4 5 6 7 8 Frame received on port 1 – source MAC address is read from frame header and added to table. Frame is sent to all ports (Flooded) because destination MAC is not in the table. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. MAC Forward / Filter Table Port MAC Addresses 1 00:0a:95:9b:68:16 2 3 4 04:13:a7:01:fe:11 5 6 7 8 Response frame received on port 4 – source MAC address is read from frame header and added to table. Frame is sent to port 1 (Forwarded) because destination MAC is found in the table; no traffic is sent to other ports. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. MAC Forward / Filter Table Port MAC Addresses 1 00:0a:95:9b:68:16 2 A4:32:cc:05:ed:81 3 00:0a:95:9b:69:a0 4 04:13:a7:01:fe:11 5 00:0a:95:9b:69:33 6 01:77:ab:b1:43:19 03:2e:1f:56:2a:3e 05:23:a2:0a:d7:05 7 8 Over time as the table is built, more frames are hopefully Forwarded than Flooded, reducing network traffic. Table entries are reset after a period of time. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Broadcast Traffic Three types of information are sent on each port of a switch: • Frames intended for a device on that port • Frames intended for a device which is not in the forward/filter table of the switch • Broadcast traffic – all switch segments are part of the same broadcast domain Broadcast traffic includes administrative information such as DHCP requests, ARP requests, and network discovery requests. As the network size increases, broadcast traffic becomes a bigger problem. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Segmenting Broadcast Traffic • Routers break up broadcast domains • Disadvantages: • Expensive • Require separate physical networks Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Another Option: VLAN • A Virtual LAN (VLAN) is a virtually separated network, spanning one or more switches • Requires a switch (usually managed) with VLAN support Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. VLAN: Static vs Dynamic • Ports on a switch are assigned to a specific VLAN (access link) or to a trunk (trunk link). • The default or native VLAN is the VLAN ports default if not specifically assigned. • Static assignment is when a port is assigned to a specific VLAN. • Alternatively a port can be assigned by a VLAN Membership Policy Server (VMPS) based on the MAC address of the device connected to the port (dynamic assignment). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. VLAN Trunk • Individual switch ports are designated as “Access” or “Trunk” ports. • Access ports behave exactly like normal switch ports, for their designated VLAN. • Trunk ports aggregate all VLAN data to send to another switch or router using VLAN Trunking Protocol (VTP). • Frames are tagged with VLAN identifier • ISL and 802.1q are popular VLAN tagging protocols. • VLAN tags are removed before packets are sent through access links Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. VLAN Characteristics • VLANS operate entirely separately – no traffic is passed from one VLAN to another through the switch. • To connect traffic between two VLANs a router must be used. • VLANs are usually setup on unique subnets to allow potential routing. • Hosts on a VLAN are unaware they are on a VLAN. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. VLAN Trunks and Aggregation • A trunk carries tagged traffic for multiple VLANs between compatible switches or routers. • To improve bandwidth, port bonding (aka link aggregation or link bundling) can be used to combine two or more port connections between devices. • Link Aggregation Control Protocol (LACP) is commonly used to bundle disparate physical ports into one logical connection. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Port Mirroring • There are situations when it would be beneficial to access the packets being transmitted by a switch port: • When using a packet sniffer to troubleshoot network issues, or • When using an Intrusion Detection System (IDS) to watch for signs of intrusions. • Port Mirroring duplicates all transmissions on a specific switch port to another designated port (Switched Port ANalyzer or SPAN) • Some switches can mirror a local port to a port on another compatible switch (Remote Switched Port ANalyzer or RSPAN) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Managed vs Unmanaged • Unmanaged Switches – work automatically, provide basic switch functions without any configuration or IP address. • Managed Switches – • Can be configured from a local console connection (out- of-band management) or remotely (in-band management). • Must have an IP address and default gateway configured for in-band management using a virtual terminal utility such as Telnet Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Managed Switches • Managed Switches – configuration options • Username and Password to administer the switch • VLAN assignment • Port speed (10/100/1000Mbps) • Duplex (Full or Half) • Port Mirroring and Port Bonding settings • Some switches allow configuration via a centralized AAA Server (authentication, authorization, and accounting) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Power over Ethernet • Power over Ethernet (PoE) can eliminate need for a separate power cord for IP devices. • Great for: • VoIP Phones • Wireless Access Points • Remote Cameras • Two standards: • PoE (802.3af): Up to 15.4W • PoE+ (802.3at): Up to 25.5W Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Power over Ethernet (contd.) • Uses unused wire pairs in Cat5 cabling, and/or transmits power over data pairs using common-mode signaling. • PoE may be supplied from the switch or from a separate PoE injector. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Data Loops • Sometimes multiple connections are created (accidentally or on purpose) between two switches. • Except when they are properly configured in a LACP port-bonding scenario, this can create a “broadcast storm”. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Loop Avoidance • Better switches often use loop avoidance strategies based on Spanning Tree Protocol (STP) • STP port states: • Blocked – no forwarding, drops all packets except Bridge Protocol Data Units (BPDU). “Should I stay blocked?” • Listening -- drops all packets except BPDU. “Should I go to blocked or learning?” • Learning – drops all packets except BPDU, begins to populate the MAC filter/forward table. “Where is everybody?” • Forwarding – normal operation • Disabled -- inoperative • STP uses BPDUs to map the best path to the root switch – alternate paths (loops) are blocked. • Spanning tree (802.1d) requires up to 50 seconds for all ports to reach Forwarding or Blocked states. • Rapid spanning tree (802.1w) simplifies the stages and can complete port election in 15 seconds. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which function on a switch can improve network security? 1 Firewall IDS VLAN Collision Domain Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which function on a switch can improve network security? VLANs separate devices onto logically distinct networks, preventing them from accessing devices on other VLANs. c. Firewall IDS VLAN Collision Domain 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. A switch port which carries traffic from all VLANs to another switch or router is called ______ . 2 An access port A port sniffer A trunk port A broadcast port Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. A switch port which carries traffic from all VLANs to another switch or router is called ______ . Access ports carry traffic for one specific VLAN, trunk ports carry tagged traffic for all VLANs. c. An access port A port sniffer A trunk port A broadcast port 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Switches break up Collision Domains, Routers or VLANs can break up Broadcast Domains. • The MAC Forward/Filter table is created and used by a switch to forward frames to appropriate ports. • A Virtual LAN (VLAN) is a virtually separated network, spanning one or more switches. • Static assignment is when a switch port is assigned to a specific VLAN, dynamic assignment is when VLAN assignment is based on the MAC address of the device connected. • A VLAN trunk carries tagged traffic for multiple VLANs between compatible switches or routers. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Wireless Infrastructure’. This concludes ‘VLANs and Switches’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 2: Operations CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 2-7: Wireless Infrastructure Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Describe the purpose of wireless routers, access points, and bridges • Explain the use of a heat map • Describe how SSIDs are configured for roaming • Distinguish between ad-hoc, infrastructure, and mesh topologies • Define wireless VLAN and wireless controller • Explain the benefits of a wireless bridge • Describe various ways to improve wireless throughput Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Going Wireless • It’s become the norm for organizations to supply wireless networks for their customers and/or staff. • Wireless networks are used for mobile devices, such as: • Notebook computers • Smartphones • Tablets • Security cameras • Media Devices (Roku, Chromecast, etc.) • Gaming Devices (Xbox, PlayStation) • Wireless networks also may be advantageous for desktop computers or other traditionally wired devices in areas where wiring is unavailable. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Routers For many small office/home office (SOHO) networks, the wireless router is the sole piece of network infrastructure with four functions. • Wireless Access Point – receiver/transmitter to connect wireless devices • Switched LAN ports – provide wired network connectivity • Bridge – connects the WLAN to the LAN • Router – connects your LAN to the WAN Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Access Point • Wireless Access Point (WAP or AP) is a wireless transmitter/receiver without the router and switch functions of the wireless router. • Access Points generally include one LAN port for connection to the wired network. • The number of APs or Wireless Routers needed for a given area depends on: • Device density • Environmental considerations (obstacles, interference) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Heat Map • Identifying the coverage area for all Access Points in a network can be done with a Site Survey. • A Site Survey is the planning and designing of a Wi-Fi network. • Initial placement of APs is based on estimated range, considering walls and other obstacles. • A Heat Map showing actual signal strength can be produced using special software utilities or a dedicated wireless meter. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. SSID • Each Wireless Router or AP is set to broadcast one or more Service Set IDentifiers (SSID). • The SSID is the name given to the wireless network connection at that AP. All devices connected to the same SSID are considered part of a Service Set. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Roaming • When two or more APs use the same SSID, wireless devices will choose which AP to connect to based on signal strength. • The wireless device will periodically re-evaluate which AP to connect to. • This process is called Roaming. • No special setup is required. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Advanced WLAN Management • Configuring one WAP is easy. Configuring dozens of Access Points can be complicated! • A WLAN Server (wireless controller) can configure multiple Access Points from one centralized control panel. • The wireless controller and APs communicate using one of the two popular protocols: • Lightweight Access Point Protocol (LWAPP) • Control and Provisioning of Wireless Access Points (CAPWAP) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Load Balancing with VLANs • Wireless APs are a Broadcast Domain • To break up congested APs, wireless clients can be assigned to VLANs to create separate broadcast domains. • Some wireless controllers support VLAN Pooling, where multiple VLANs are used on the same AP and with the same SSID • Benefits: • Multiple broadcast domains, less bandwidth wasted with broadcast traffic. • Can use multiple IP address spaces. • VLANs can be designated (for security), or the wireless controller can auto-assign based on load balancing. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Topologies • Ad-Hoc: A wireless network without access points or routers – wireless nodes communicate directly with each other. • Infrastructure: Standard wireless network where nodes connect to a wireless access point or router, which bridges the wireless network to a wired network. • Mesh: A network topology where each access point or each node relays data for the network as a whole. • Wireless mesh networks often use the WDS system to interconnect wireless access points. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Two-Building Problem Two buildings need to share a network – how can you connect them? Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Two-Building Problem (contd.) Copper? NO – connecting the buildings with Cat5 or similar cabling can cause electrical problems and destroy equipment due to the difference in potential energy between the buildings (aka ground loop) Fiber Optic? YES – but it can be expensive. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Bridge Wireless Bridge: uses two specialized Access Points to connect the two wired networks via Wi-Fi. Wireless Bridges can operate as a true bridge (with distinct subnets on each side) or as a “transparent bridge”, with the same subnet and settings carrying over to both sides. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Antenna Types and Placement Unidirectional • Signal primarily travels in one direction. • Best on the edge of a network or for a wireless bridge. • Signal radiates out in a (mostly) uniform radius from the antenna. • Best in the middle of a network or area. Omnidirectional Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 2.4GHz vs 5GHz • 2.4GHz: • Used in 802.11b, g, n, and ac • Moves through obstacles better than 5GHz • More likely to have interference from other sources including microwaves, Bluetooth, cordless phones • 5GHz: • Used in 802.11a, n, and ac • Faster than 2.5GHz, more bandwidth • 802.11n – can use EITHER 2.4GHz or 5GHz • 802.11ac – uses BOTH 2.4GHz and 5GHz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Faster Wireless • Throughput – the total bandwidth of a connection • Goodput – throughput, less the administrative overhead • Basic improvements: • Signal strength • Improved coverage • Channel selection Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Faster Wireless (contd.) • High Throughput Committee – 802.11n and 802.11ac • 802.11a-ht (5GHz) and 802.11g-ht (2.4GHz) 802.11n (300Mbps) • MIMO – Multiple Input, Multiple Output • Multiplexed signals from multiple (1-4) antennas • Spatial Multiplexing, Space-time Block Coding, Transmit Beamforming • MUMIMO – Multi-user MIMO Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The name given to a wireless network connection is ________ . 1 Access Point Port SSID Channel Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. The name given to a wireless network connection is ________ . SSID is the name given to the wireless network connection on an access point. c. Access Point Port SSID Channel 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. You wish to extend your network into a nearby building. Fiber Optic cabling has been ruled out as being too expensive. What is your next best option? 2 Category 5 cabling run between the buildings VPN Site Survey Wireless Bridge Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. You wish to extend your network into a nearby building. Fiber Optic cabling has been ruled out as being too expensive. What is your next best option? A VPN could connect two networks together, but a wireless bridge can connect the two networks more easily and without the electrical risk of category 5 (or any copper) cabling. d. Category 5 cabling run between the buildings VPN Site Survey Wireless Bridge 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • A Wireless Access Point (WAP or AP) is a wireless transmitter/receiver without the router and switch functions of the wireless router. • A Site Survey is the planning and designing of a Wi-Fi network. • The SSID is the name given to the wireless network connection at that AP. All devices connected to the same SSID are considered part of a Service Set. • Roaming is when wireless devices will choose which AP to connect to based on signal strength. • A WLAN Server (wireless controller) can configure multiple Access Points from one centralized control panel • A Wireless Bridge uses two specialized Access Points to connect the two wired networks via Wi-Fi. It incorporates basic security controls to keep users secure in the network. Case Study: Wireless Attack Noticed a new Wi-Fi access point Tested its security controls Discovered an HTTPS port 443 Virtual Private Network VPN extends the corporate network securely via encrypted packets sent out via virtual connections over the public internet to distant offices, home workers, salespeople, and business partners. Controls Against Electronics Faraday Cage White Noise Control Zones Network Security Controls Network-Based Security Prevents computer network from: Trojan Horses Denial of service Hacking, viruses, and spyware Email spoofing Unauthorized access Network Attack Categories Active attack Passive attack An intruder initiates commands to disrupt the network's normal operation. An intruder intercepts data traveling through the network. Firewall Allows users to access the internet Controls network traffic Stops hackers from accessing network Firewall Features Is a combination of hardware and software Controls the vulnerable point between a corporate network and the internet Unified Threat Management (UTM) UTM combines several key elements of network security to offer a comprehensive security package to buyers. Unified Threat Management (UTM) • Simplicity • Streamlined installation and maintenance • Centralized control • Single point of failure • Single point of compromise • Performance issues Goals Issues Web Application Firewall Filters, monitors, and blocks HTTP traffic Filters the content of specific web applications Prevents attacks from web application security flaws Intrusion Detection System (IDS) Intrusion Detection System otherwise known as IDS is monitored network usage anomaly. ●Operates in the background ●Alerts when intrusions are detected ●Protects external and internal misuse ●Works together with firewalls and routers Intrusion Detection System Components Sensor User Interface Analyzer Admin Console Intrusion Detection System Categories Network-based IDS (NIDS) Host-based IDS (HIDS) An intruder initiates commands to disrupt the network's normal operation. An intruder intercepts data traveling through the network. Intrusion Prevention System (IPS) • Closely related to IDS • Designed to detect and prevent attacks • Must be properly configured and tuned to be effective Network Admission Control It is a concept of controlling access to an environment through strict adherence and implementation of security policy. Network Admission Control Goals Prevent/reduce zero-day attacks Enforce security policy throughout the network Use identities to perform access control Honeypots Enable services and ports Have services emulated A honeypot system is a computer that sits in the screened subnet or the DMZ and attempts to lure attackers. Honeypots Group of honeypots implemented together is called a honeynet. Security Testing Vulnerability Scanning It is a process of examining your systems and network devices for security holes and weaknesses. Vulnerability Scanning Vulnerability scanners are designed to help administrators and address vulnerabilities. Vulnerability Scan Goals • Identify vulnerability • Identify lack of security controls • Identify common misconfigurations Some scanners are capable of remediation checking for misconfigurations. Penetration Testing Emulates the same methods attackers would use Uncovers any weaknesses within the environment Tries to exploit the system The most aggressive form of security testing Simulates an attack from a malicious outsider. Types of Penetration Testing The types depend on the organization, its security objectives, and the management goals. Types of Penetration Testing In black box testing, the tester has no knowledge of the internal design or features of the system. It simulates the external attacker the best. Types of Penetration Testing In white box testing, the tester has complete knowledge of the internal system, it may yield a more complete result, but it may not be representative of an external hacker. It may be a good indicator of an internal type of threat. Types of Penetration Testing In grey box testing, some information about internal working is given to the tester. • Helps guide tester tactics • Mitigates the risks Security Audits Security Audits These are systematic evaluations performed with the purpose of demonstrating the effectiveness of controls to a third party. Security Audits It is performed by independent auditors. Auditors provide unbiased view of the state of security controls. Types of Security Audits • It is performed by an organization’s internal staff. • The reports are intended for internal audience. Disadvantage: Conflict of interest and hidden agenda • It is performed by third-party auditors. • The reports are intended for third-party stakeholders. • NDA is a prerequisite. Disadvantage: Cost Key Takeaways Networks are part of a large, centrally managed, internetworked architecture solutions. Wireless networks are computer networks that are not connected by cables of any kind. Network-based protection or security is a method of preventing your computer network from unauthorized user access. Security testing is a process of examining your systems and network devices for security holes and weaknesses.

Lesson 3-1: Areas of Risk Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Describe the role of Disaster Recovery and Business Continuity in an organization’s risk assessment plan. • Identify an Uninterruptible Power Supply and describe its purpose. • Define a data breach. • Explain the risks associated with a single point of failure and ways to reduce that risk. • Identify the differences between vulnerability scanning and penetration testing. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Risk • Risk is not unexpected. • Disasters can and will happen: • Equipment will fail • Lightning can strike • Power can go out • Fires and floods do happen • Theft and sabotage is possible Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Disaster Recovery / Business Continuity • Disaster Recovery (DR) is a set of policies, procedures and solutions to facilitate recovering from a disaster. • Consider how IT systems, including servers, data, and applications, can be restored after a fire, flood, theft, or equipment failure. • Business Continuity refers to activities and procedures to ensure critical business operations continue during and after a disaster. BDR devices such as the Datto Siris provide special Backup and Disaster Recovery solutions by backing up key servers and virtualizing server operations in case of hardware failure ! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Battery Backups / UPS • Battery Backups or Uninterruptible Power Supplies (UPS) provide supplemental electricity to servers and other equipment during a power outage. • Battery Backups provide five to sixty minutes of power. • UPS software can notify administrators or automatically initiate shutdown processes. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Single Point of Failure • Single Point of Failure – A single device, connection, or service which will significantly impact network operations if it fails. • In Disaster Recovery planning, IT staff should identify: • Critical nodes – network devices or connections which will disrupt operations if they fail • Critical assets – resources such as servers or data storage locations which will disrupt business operations if they are unavailable • Wherever possible redundancy should be used to eliminate single points of failure in critical nodes or critical assets Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Vulnerability Scanning / Penetration Testing • Vulnerability scanner: A computer program designed to assess computers, computer systems, networks, or applications for weaknesses. • Nessus (paid) and Nmap (free) are two of the most popular vulnerability scanners. • Penetration test: An attack on a computer system with the intention of finding security weaknesses, potentially gaining access to it, its functionality, and data. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Responding to a Data Breach • Data breach – unauthorized access to network data, usually from outside the network. • First responders – the first person to identify a data breach or other unauthorized activity. IT staff should be trained in appropriate first responder techniques, including securing the crime scene as well as documenting and preserving evidence. • End user awareness and training – many data breaches occur due to end user errors, such as opening unexpected email attachments. Adhering to appropriate standards and policies related to acceptable behaviors should be part of end user training. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of the following could be a single point of failure? 1 Collision Domain VLAN Switch UPS Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which of the following could be a single point of failure? A switch failure would leave all devices connected to that switch unable to function, therefore a switch is a single point of failure. c. Collision Domain VLAN Switch UPS 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of the following can be a part of a Disaster Recovery plan? 2 UPS Business Continuity Port Mirroring Vulnerability Scanner Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which of the following can be a part of a Disaster Recovery plan? Business Continuity refers to activities and procedures to ensure critical business operations continue during and after a disaster. b. UPS Business Continuity Port Mirroring Vulnerability Scanner 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Disaster Recovery (DR) is a set of policies, procedures, and solutions to facilitate recovering from a disaster. • Business Continuity refers to activities and procedures to ensure critical business operations continue during and after a disaster. • A data breach is unauthorized access to network data, usually from outside the network. • Single Point of Failure is the term used to describe a single device, connection, or service which will significantly impact network operations if it fails. • A Vulnerability Scanner is a computer program designed to assess computers, computer systems, networks, or applications for weaknesses. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Attack Vectors’. This concludes ‘Areas of Risk’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 3: Security CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 3-2: Attack Vectors Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Differentiate between brute force and social engineering attacks. Explain a denial-of-service attack. Describe various attack vectors including IP spoofing, ARP cache poisoning, session hijacking, and VLAN hopping. Explain wireless attack vectors including evil twin, rogue AP, war driving, and WEP/WPA attacks. Discuss the threat caused by malicious insiders. Describe various ways to reduce your attack surface. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Attack Vectors are any paths by which an intruder can gain access to or cause damage to a computer system or network. • Attack Surfaces are any potentially vulnerable areas of a computer system, which can be targeted by an attack. Attack Vectors Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Brute Force • Brute Force attacks use no special tricks or vulnerabilities to work. • Typical brute force attack – using password cracking tool to try thousands of possible username and password combinations to access a server. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Denial of Service • Any attack which seeks to prevent a server (or other device) from responding to its users. • Distributed Denial of Service (DDoS) – an attack where a large number of nodes attempt to communicate with a server at the same time, preventing or delaying the server from responding to normal user requests. • Botnet – a group of computers under the control of a single entity, usually caused by malware, which can be leveraged to implement a DDoS attack or other coordinated attack. • Traffic Spike – often the main indicator of a coordinated attack is a significant spike in the amount of network traffic around a particular server or device. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Denial of Service (contd.) • Reflective attacks – a Denial of Service (DoS) attack that redirects traffic from other servers to overwhelm the target. • Amplification attacks – a reflective DoS attack in which the traffic sent from the reflection source is far greater than the traffic needed to initiate the reflection. • Example: Hacker spoofs the target machine’s IP address and requests DNS or NTP info from one or more “Open Resolver” DNS or NTP servers. • Friendly/Unintentional DoS – when non-malicious traffic overwhelms a server in what appears to be a DoS attack. • Smurfing – a nearly obsolete form of DoS attack involving spoofing an IP address and then sending a PING request to a broadcast address on another network. All devices on the network receive the PING and have to respond, thus flooding the network, but most routers disable this feature on broadcast addresses now. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Physical Attack • Access to a server or network can be prevented by physically damaging the equipment. These attacks can be mitigated by preventing physical access to the equipment. • Permanent Denial of Service (PDoS) – a term used when a server or network is permanently disabled by physical attacks, or by causing permanent damage remotely (e.g. damaging the firmware with a remote flash attack, “phlashing”). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Spoofing • Spoofing = pretending. • IP Spoofing – Packet headers are altered so that packets from one device appear to be coming from another IP. • Used as a way to get through filters and firewalls, or as a way to setup other attacks such as a “Man-in-the-middle” attack. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ARP Cache Poisoning • ARP – Address Resolution Protocol, used to translate IP addresses into MAC addresses. • ARP Cache – a table each device builds and maintains which matches IP addresses to MAC addresses based on ARP packets received (not just ARP packets requested). • ARP Cache Poisoning is a technique by which a local machine sends ARP packets to redirect IP packets intended for another device to itself or to another host. • Only works on the local segment • Also called ARP Spoofing or ARP Poison Routing Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Man-In-The-Middle • A Man-in-the-middle attack occurs when a compromised computer intercepts communication between two hosts by pretending to be the other host. • Can be used to impersonate: • Servers • Critical PCs • Websites • Wireless Access Points • Financial Gateways Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Packet / Protocol Abuse • Imagine a hacker gains control of a key computer and needs to send information outside the network, but the firewall is blocking their TCP packets. • One option: encapsulate TCP packets into DNS protocol packets using a tool such as Iodine. • This is also called Protocol Tunneling. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Other Attacks • Session Hijacking – after two machines authenticate in a session (conversation), the hacker steals the session ID and redirects traffic to replace one of the two original devices in the session. • VLAN Hopping – communicating outside of your designated VLAN by adding a fake VLAN ID tag and communicating over at least two switches. • The first switch passes your packets to the second switch, adding a real VLAN ID. • The second switch removes the real VLAN ID, exposing the fake VLAN ID, which may be routed to the target VLAN. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Social Engineering • Social Engineering refers to using non-technical means to gain access to an otherwise secured network. • Social Engineering techniques may include: • Phone calls • Emails • “Lost” flash drives or other media • Social Engineering is the most difficult threat to defend against. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Attacks • Several attack vectors are unique to wireless networks: • Evil twin – Using a WAP with the same SSID as a legitimate WAP to connect to an organization’s wireless devices for a peer-to-peer attack. • Rogue AP – Any WAP connected to your network but not under your control. • War driving – Scanning for unsecured access points while driving around. • War chalking – Documenting known compromised access points with chalk (or online). • WEP/WPA/WPA2/WPS attacks – attacks to try and break the password on a wireless access point. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bluetooth Attacks • Bluejacking – sending unsolicited messages to a nearby computer or device via Bluetooth. • Bluesnarfing – intercepting Bluetooth connections or taking control of a device via Bluetooth. • Both can be mitigated by turning off “discoverability” in Bluetooth devices. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Malware • Malware (malicious software, including viruses) can be a factor in network attacks. • Malware infections can potentially: • Collect passwords • Look for files or specific data • Allow hackers remote access into the network Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Insider Threat • The best network protections available are useless if a malicious employee with sufficient access wants to cause harm. • Disgruntled users can: • Erase files and data • Physically damage equipment • Install malware or hacking tools Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Other Terms • Compromised System – any computer or device which is under the control of an intruder. • Zero Day Attack: • when an exploit is discovered in an operating system or program and is used by hackers before a fix is available, or • When a new virus or malware is discovered that is not yet detected by anti-malware defenses. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Vulnerabilities – Reducing Your Attack Surface • Unnecessary running services – turn off • Open ports – block at firewall or on local PC • Unpatched/legacy systems – move to separate subnet, disconnect from internet • Unencrypted channels – don’t use • Clear text credentials – make sure connections are encrypted Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Vulnerabilities – Reducing Your Attack Surface (contd.) • Unsecure protocols – discontinue if possible • TELNET • HTTP • SLIP • FTP • TFTP • SNMPv1 and SNMPv2 • TEMPEST/RF emanation – NATO and NSA certification for spying by measuring unintended emanations. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Your web server is being overwhelmed with traffic from multiple sources. It’s most likely due to this type of attack. 1 Man-in-the-middle DDoS Port Scanner Advanced Persistent Threat Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Your web server is being overwhelmed with traffic from multiple sources. It’s most likely due to this type of attack. An attack where a large number of nodes attempt to communicate with a server at the same time is a Distributed Denial of Service (DDoS) attack. b. Man-in-the-middle DDoS Port Scanner Advanced Persistent Threat 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of these best describes a man-in-the-middle attack? 2 When a computer is infected with malware. When IP packets are modified to appear to be from another address When an outside party sets up a wireless access point with the same SSID as an organization’s legitimate access points. When a compromised computer intercepts communication between two hosts by pretending to be the hosts themselves. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. IP Spoofing (b) may be involved in a man-in-the-middle attack, but the attack itself is best described by option (d). d. When a computer is infected with malware. When IP packets are modified to appear to be from another address When an outside party sets up a wireless access point with the same SSID as an organization’s legitimate access points. When a compromised computer intercepts communication between two hosts by pretending to be the hosts themselves. 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Distributed Denial of Service (DDoS) is an attack where a large number of nodes attempt to communicate with a server at the same time, preventing or delaying the server from responding to normal user requests • IP Spoofing is a type of attack where packet headers are altered so that packets from one device appear to be coming from another IP. • A Man-in-the-middle attack occurs when a compromised computer intercepts communication between two hosts by pretending to be the other host. • ARP Cache Poisoning is a technique by which a local machine sends ARP packets to redirect IP packets intended for another device to itself or to another host. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Network Hardening Techniques’. This concludes ‘Attack Vectors’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 3: Security CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 3-3: Network Hardening Techniques Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: Describe the three types of anti-malware protection and their uses. Explain four ways the switches can be configured to improve security. Discuss the importance of security policies. Identify unsecure protocols and unneeded services. Explain how access lists can be used to improve network security. Discuss the three main types of wireless security protocols. Identify various types of user authentication protocols. Describe how hashes are used. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Anti-Malware software • Anti-malware software protects against viruses and other malware and is mandatory in a secure network • Host-based – installed on each local PC or device • Cloud/server-based – a hybrid solution which runs a small client on each host with the processing done at least partially by a cloud-based server. • Network-based – malware protection running on a firewall, proxy server, or cloud server protecting network transactions (e.g. DNS filtering) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Switch Port Security • DHCP snooping – limiting DHCP responses to designated, trusted switch ports. • ARP inspection – verifying IP-to-MAC mapping in packets, preventing ARP cache poisoning attacks • MAC address filtering – whitelist or blacklist devices based on their MAC address • VLAN assignments – dividing hosts into VLANs limits their access to sensitive network areas by segmenting the network Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Security Policy • Security policies communicate to users what they should do to protect the network, which potentially include: • Clean-desk policy • BYOD policy • Data storage and privacy • Security audits • Consent to monitoring • Recording policy Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Disable Unneeded Services • Disable or remove any network services which aren’t needed to reduce your potential attack surface. • IIS • Telnet • FTP • NNTP • Flash • Mail/Exchange Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Secure vs Unsecure Protocols Secure SSH SNMPv3 TLS/SSL SFTP HTTPS IPsec Unsecure TELNET HTTP SLIP FTP TFTP SNMPv1/v2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Firewalls and Access Lists • Firewalls and proxy servers allow filtering based on a list of rules and criteria. Filtering can be based on: • Web/Content – the content of a website (or, less often, a document or file) is analyzed and compared to a list of criteria. This may include filtering known topical sites (porn, violence, games, employment) or may include filtering based on the site contents. • Port – traffic for known or allowed ports (port 80 for http, port 21 for FTP, port 123 for NTP, etc.) can be allowed while other ports are blocked. • IP – individual IP addresses can be blocked or allowed • Many firewalls default to an “Implicit Deny” policy, meaning any traffic which is not expressly allowed by the access list is denied. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Security • WEP – Wired Equivalent Privacy • WPA – Wi-Fi Protected Access • WPA2 *recommended* • Personal – Pre-shared Key (PSK), suitable for home and small business • Enterprise – (802.1x mode), requires a RADIUS/EAP server for authentication • WPS *disable* Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Security (contd.) • TKIP vs AES encryption • TKIP = 128bit encryption, used by WPA • AES (also CCMP) = advanced encryption, used by WPA2 • 802.1x –authentication protocol defining the RADIUS/EAP authentication relationship and requirements • TLS – Transport Layer Security, highly secure authentication mechanism but requires certificates for client and server. • TTLS – Tunneling TLS, also secure but only requires certificate for the server. • MAC filtering Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. User Authentication Authentication is the process of determining whether someone or something is, in fact, who or what it is declared to be. • CHAP – Challenge Handshake Authentication Protocol • Shared Secret (user password) • Authenticator sends challenge • Peer responds with hashed response of the challenge plus shared secret • Authenticator verifies, accepts or drops, periodically rechecks • MSCHAP -- Microsoft’s version • PAP – Password Authentication Protocol; older, insecure alternative to CHAP • EAP – Extensible Authentication Protocol; framework for authentication, included in 802.1x • Kerberos – ticket-based network authentication protocol, requires a trusted third party (server) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. User Authentication (contd.) • Two-factor/Multifactor authentication –using two or more methods for authenticating a user or connection. • Single sign-on – a technique to federate multiple authentication portals so that each will accept authorized users from another, thus preventing the necessity to sign in multiple times. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Hashes A Hash function is a function that can be used to map digital data of arbitrary size to digital data of fixed size. Hashes are used to verify authentication data such as passwords. • MD5 – popular cryptographic hash, which was widely used. By 2012 MD5 was no longer recommended due to known exploits. • SHA – Secure Hash Algorithm, a family of cryptographic hashes designed to be more secure than MD5. SHA-0 and SHA-1 are no longer recommended. SHA-2 is currently the recommended standard with SHA-3 an alternative. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Verifying packets are going to the correct destination can be done by: 1 ARP Inspection Packet Analyzing Content Filtering Using VLANs Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Verifying packets are going to the correct destination can be done by: ARP Inspection verifies that the IP address of a packet matches the MAC address it’s being sent to, and is a function available in higher level switches. a. ARP Inspection Packet Analyzing Content Filtering Using VLANs 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of the following wireless security protocols is the most secure? 2 WEP WPA2 CHAP WPS Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. WPA2 is the most secure of the wireless security protocols widely used today. b. WEP WPA2 CHAP WPS 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Anti-malware software protects against viruses and other malware and is mandatory in a secure network • Four ways to improve security at the switch level include DHCP Snooping, ARP Inspection, MAC Address Filtering, and VLAN Assignments. • Disabling or removing any network services which aren’t needed is a good way to reduce your potential attack surface. • Access Lists can limit traffic through a firewall or proxy by listing websites and content, ports, or IPs which are allowed or blocked. • WEP, WPA, and WPA2 are types of wireless security protocols. • A hash function such as MD5 or SHA is used to verify authentication information. Lesson 3-4: Physical Security Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Discuss the benefits of door access control, cipher lock, and mantrap. • Explain the use of a key fob. • Define biometrics. • Discuss the use of video cameras and security guards. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Let’s Get Physical • The most advanced encryption, authentication, and protection strategies are useless if an intruder can walk in and: • Pick up a backup drive • Plug an infected flash drive into the server • Connect a packet sniffer into the router • Sit down at an unprotected console and change settings. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network Closets • In small offices, or in departments of larger offices, you’ll find network closets – small rooms that house networking equipment. • Security considerations: • Door locks, physical or biometric • Access and sharing Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Door Access Controls Controlling access to network closets and other secure areas can be done with: • Traditional keys • Cipher locks • Electronic keypads/locks • Proximity readers/key fobs • Biometric scanners Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Keypad/Cipher Locks A cipher lock is opened with a 4 or 5 button programmable keypad. It may be mechanical or electronic. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Proximity Readers / Key Fobs • Proximity readers read key cards or key fobs at a short distance. • A key fob is a type of security token: a small hardware device with built-in authentication mechanisms. • Can be used for doors or for authentication on a computer or terminal. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Biometrics Biometrics authentication uses personal biological data to verify identity. • Fingerprint • Retina • Facial recognition • Voice recognition Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Mantraps A mantrap, air lock, sally port or access control vestibule is a physical security access control system that allows a person into one chamber for verification. If verified, they proceed through a second door; if verification fails, they can be held while security is summoned. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Video Monitoring Video monitoring can supplement access control for security and compliance purposes. • Traditional analog CCTV cameras are being replaced by modern, remotely monitored IP cameras. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Security Guard A security guard (or security officer) can provide services unavailable with any technological solution. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. Lesson 3-5: Firewalls Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Define a Firewall and its role in computer networks. • Distinguish between host-based, network-based, hardware, and software firewalls. • Explain the benefit of an application-aware firewall. • Describe the difference between stateful and stateless packet inspection. • Discuss the following terms: ACL, UTM, DMZ, Virtual Wire, and Implicit Deny. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. About Firewalls • The name comes from construction, where a “firewall” is a wall especially designed to either prevent or delay a fire from penetrating into the next space. • Network firewalls are designed to prevent or delay outside intruders from penetrating into our network or resources. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Types of Firewalls • Host-based/software – firewall application designed to keep network intruders from accessing resources on that host. • Network-based/hardware – a physical device designed to keep intruders out of the local network or segment. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. SOHO Firewall • A small office/home office firewall is often integrated in one appliance which may also include: • Router • Wireless Access Point • Switch • File Sharing Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Application Aware Firewalls • Traditional Firewalls block traffic based on ports, IP addresses, or website content filter information. • “Next generation” or “Gen 3” application/context-aware firewalls can also block traffic based on specific applications or micro-applications (layer 7), user behavior, and reputation. • For example, a context-aware firewall can allow access to Facebook while blocking Facebook games. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Firewall Features • Stateless Packet Inspection – packets are reviewed individually and forwarded or dropped based solely on packet information (layer 3). • Fast, easy • Stateful Packet Inspection – packets are reviewed in the context of their TCP or UDP sessions. • Slower, requires maintaining state tables, less susceptible to spoofing and DoS attacks • UTM (Unified Threat Management) – provides additional functions in the same device, potentially including: • Network antivirus • Anti-spam • Intrusion Prevention • Content Filtering • VPN, load balancing, additional services Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Firewall Concepts • ACL – Access Control List, a table of IP addresses, MAC addresses, and/or ports and what they are allowed or not allowed to do. May reside on a firewall, router, or host. • DMZ – Demilitarized Zone, a designated IP or IP range that is specifically NOT protected by the firewall. Traffic to the DMZ is not filtered in any way. • Virtual Wire – a mode on certain firewalls or routers that directly maps an inbound and outbound port together as if they were one circuit. No routing takes place, but firewall filters still function on the virtual wire traffic. • Implicit Deny – the default on most firewalls, any traffic which is not specifically allowed in the firewall rules is automatically blocked. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Placement and Settings • Standard Firewall placement – • Between “trusted network” (internal) and “untrusted network” (external) • Filters inbound and outbound traffic based on rules to block or allow packets (layer 3) • Can also be used internally to limit access to sensitive areas of the internal network Company Network Firewall IDS Internet Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. A computer which is NOT protected by a firewall’s filters may be a part of a _______ . 1 Denial of Service attack Unified Threat Management Demilitarized Zone Application-aware firewall Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. A computer which is NOT protected by a firewall’s filters may be a part of a _______ . A Demilitarized Zone (DMZ) is an IP address or range, which is unprotected by the firewall. c. Denial of Service attack Unified Threat Management Demilitarized Zone Application-aware firewall 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. When a firewall inspects packets in the context of their TCP or UDP session, this is called _________ . 2 Stateful packet inspection Unified Threat Management Application-aware filtering. Implicit Deny Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. When a firewall inspects packets in the context of their TCP or UDP session, this is called _________ . In stateful packet inspection, packets are reviewed in the context of their TCP or UDP sessions. a. Stateful packet inspection Unified Threat Management Application-aware filtering Implicit Deny 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Network firewalls are designed to prevent or delay outside intruders from penetrating into our network or resources. • A host-based firewall is a software application designed to keep network intruders from accessing resources on that host. • A network-based firewall is usually a hardware appliance designed to keep intruders out of the local network or segment. • In stateful packet inspection, packets are reviewed in the context of their TCP or UDP sessions. • A DMZ is an IP or IP range which is not protected by the firewall. • Implicit Deny means that all traffic through a firewall is assumed to be blocked unless it is explicitly allowed by the firewall’s rules. Lesson 3-6: Network Access Control Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Define network access control. • Describe the role of 802.1x and posture assessment in network access control. • Explain the purpose of guest networks and quarantine networks. • Identify the difference between persistent and non-persistent agents. • Describe the function of edge control and access control. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network Access Control • Network Access Control – a system that allows organizations to restrict access to resources on their private network. • Primarily used in large enterprise for • BYOD • Role-based • Defend against Advanced Persistent Threats (APT) • “Who is on my network? Are they accessing data appropriately?” Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 802.1x • 802.1X is an IEEE Standard for authenticating devices attempting to access a LAN or WLAN. • It is part of the IEEE 802.1 group of networking protocols. • 802.1x recognizes three components: • Supplicant – device attempting to connect • Authenticator – Access Point or Router handling the connection • Authentication Server – a server (usually Remote Authentication Dial-In User Service or RADIUS) which verifies the user or device and (optionally) provides access information, such as required VLAN Authenticator Supplicant Authentication Server Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Posture Assessments Posture assessment is the evaluation of system security based on the applications and settings that a particular system is using. Typical posture assessment criteria might include: • Operating System version • Service pack version • Malware definitions updated Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Persistent and Non-Persistent Agents • Posture Assessment is performed by an agent installed on the user’s device. • If the agent is permanently installed (for use in future assessments), it is referred to as a Persistent Agent. • A non-persistent agent runs the assessment then uninstalls itself. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. • Non-compliant machines can be blocked entirely or placed into a limited-access quarantine network. • If post-assessment the device passes, the device can join the regular network. • Some NAC servers can perform remediation services on quarantined devices. Quarantine Network Internet VPN Client / Supplicant Firewall Quarantine / Remediation Network Private Network NAC Server Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Guest Networks • A Guest Network provides limited network access for temporary guests. • Usually separated from an organization’s main network by: • VLAN • Separate Subnet • Separate network • Access Point function Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Edge vs Access Control • Edge Control: Protects the network at its outer boundary, usually with a Firewall. • Access Control: Protects individual resources inside the network using access control lists or other granular settings. Internet Firewall NAC Server Accounting Server w/ ACL Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. In 802.1x the device which is requesting authenticated access to the network is called the: 1 Authenticator Authentication server Network guest Supplicant Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. In 802.1x the device which is requesting authenticated access to the network is called the: The requesting device is the Supplicant, the access point or other device it is connecting to is the Authenticator, and the device verifying their credentials is the Authentication Server. d. Authenticator Authentication Server Network guest Supplicant 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. What is a characteristic that might cause a Posture Assessment to fail? 2 DNS settings Security Updates DHCP Settings Password Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved.
