A Posture Assessment will review security and software settings on the requesting device, which would include whether or not all relevant security updates are installed. • b DNS Settings Security Updates DHCP Settings Password 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Network Access Control refers to a system that allows organizations to restrict access to resources on their private network. • 802.1X is an IEEE Standard for authenticating devices attempting to access a LAN or WLAN and includes three components – a Supplicant, an Authenticator, and an Authentication Server. • Posture assessment is the evaluation of system security based on the applications and settings that a particular system is using. • When Posture Assessment is performed by an agent permanently installed on the user’s device it is referred to as a Persistent Agent. • Edge Control protects the outer boundary of a private network, while Access Control protects individual resources inside the network. Lesson 3-7: Forensic Concepts Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Describe the role of a first responder. • Discuss data breach concepts including securing the area, documenting the scene, chain of custody, and data transport. • Explain the function of eDiscovery tools. • Describe a legal hold. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Forensics • Computer Forensics is the task of identifying, documenting, and recovering digital evidence. • Forensics is critical in the event of a security breach, both to document evidence for legal action and to identify where security measures should be improved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. First Responder • First Responder refers to the first IT professional to recognize the security breach. • Appropriate action by a First Responder can preserve important evidence and minimize damage from the security breach. • Incorrect action by a First Responder can cause more damage and/or destroy important evidence. • Training in proper First Responder procedures is important! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Securing the Area • In a TV police show, police secure the physical area of a crime scene. • In the IT world, the “area” may be digital or physical (or both) and may include disconnecting users, shutting down rogue processes and applications, or even disconnecting a server or host from the network entirely. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Escalation • Sometimes securing the area involves decisions that will adversely impact hundreds or thousands of users, or potentially destroy important evidence. • IT professionals should have a clear chain of command and be able to escalate decisions to a senior manager when needed. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Documenting the Scene • Documenting the Scene can include: • Making copies of current router and server logs as well as any other relevant settings. • Saving screen captures of screens showing evidence of the breach. • Preserving a snapshot of current system activity, including logged-in users • If future testimony is a consideration, documentation should be done by two people. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Evidence Collection • Evidence should be collected in the order of volatility, including: 1. Memory contents 2. Swap files 3. Network processes 4. System processes 5. File system information 6. Raw disk/file information 7. Offline media (backup tapes, USB drives) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Data Transport and Chain of Custody • Chain of Custody refers to documenting who collected and who controlled the evidence at any point in time. If legal action is possible, documenting the chain of custody will make it more likely the evidence will be admissible in court. • Data Transport – when any evidence is being transported, physically or electronically, it must be sufficiently tagged so that it can be reconstructed after transport. Documenting the time data was transported is also helpful in keeping evidence admissible. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Forensic Report • A Forensics Report includes a summary of the evidence, including: • What happened • What evidence supports the situation • How the situation was remediated • How the situation will be prevented in the future • All evidence, including chain of custody and data transport information. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. eDiscovery • eDiscovery is a feature provided in some network applications, which facilitate producing evidence during legal proceedings. • Examples: Google Vault for Google Apps, In-Place eDiscovery for Microsoft Exchange Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Legal Considerations • A legal hold is a process that an organization uses to preserve all forms of relevant information when litigation is reasonably anticipated. • In addition, some industries (finance, medical) may require certain retention periods for key data. • Data Retention Policies document how corporate information should be maintained and destroyed to meet legal or company guidelines. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Your company is in a lawsuit, and the attorneys have requested copies of all e-mails which meet a certain criteria. Which tool would be most helpful in providing this information? 1 eDiscovery Chain of Custody Data Backups Security Policy Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Your company is in a lawsuit, and the attorneys have requested copies of all e-mails which meet a certain criteria. Which tool would be most helpful in providing this information? While data backups might be helpful, using an eDiscovery tool to search the e-mail archives and retrieve data based on the search criteria would be the most helpful. a. eDiscovery Chain of Custody Data Backups Security Policy 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The first IT professional to recognize a data breach is referred to as the _________ . 2 Network Administrator First Responder Point of Entry eDiscovery Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. The first IT professional to recognize a data breach is referred to as the _________ . 2 First Responder refers to the first IT professional to recognize the security breach. b. Network Administrator First Responder Point of Entry eDiscovery Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • First Responder refers to the first IT professional to recognize the security breach. • In IT, securing the area after a data breach may include both physical and digital considerations. • Documenting the scene may include copying system logs, taking screen shots of relevant activity, and documenting current users. • Chain of Custody refers to documenting who collected and who controlled the evidence at any point in time. • eDiscovery is a feature provided in some network applications which facilitates producing evidence during legal proceedings. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Troubleshooting Methodologies’. This concludes ‘Forensic Concepts’.

Introduction to Cyber Security Information Security Governance and Risk Assessment Learning Objectives Explain information security governance Describe risk management Summarize effective information security program By the end of this lesson, you will be able to: Define supply chain Information Security Governance Information Security Governance It is a set of responsibilities and practices exercised by the board and executive management to: Achieve goals Manage risks Meet objectives Verify usage of resources IT Governance Focus Areas IT Governance Risk Management Resource Management Performance Measures Strategic Alignment Value Delivery Business Goals and Objectives Strategic Plan Tactical Plan Operational Plan To meet customer needs by ensuring that business processes and operations are in place Business Drivers Market demands Organizational needs and brand image Technological advancement Customer requests Social needs Legal requirement Business Drivers Enabling Technology It is an invention or innovation that can be applied to drive radical change in the capabilities of a user or culture. Enablers for Governance Enablers are factors that individually and collectively influence whether something will work. Enabler Categories People, Skills, and Competencies Principles, Policies, and Frameworks Processes Services, Infrastructure, and Applications Culture, Ethics, and Behavior Information Security Governance Is the responsibility of the board of directors and executive management and must have a clear organizational strategy for preservation Information Security Governance: Outcomes The outcomes of information security governance are: Clear approval and support for formal security strategies Performance in implementing security policies is monitored Security awareness and training is provided Information security is treated as a critical business issue Professionalism demonstrated to third parties Information security effectiveness is reviewed periodically High level of oversight and control Implementation and maintenance of information security activities Management Support Management Support It is the extent to which the senior management understands the importance of the security function and supports security goals and priorities. Management Support Committing funding and resources Identifying key performance metrics Providing overall guidance Participating in security plans and policies Establish Reporting and Communication Channels Other management Senior management Employees Business process owners The user needs to have routine communication channels to: Performance Management and Smart Metric Performance Management It is the systematic process by which the Department of Commerce involves its employees as individuals and members of a group. Types of Performance management IT balanced scorecard Capability maturity model IT Balanced Scorecard It is a performance metric used in strategic management to identify and improve various internal functions of a business. Capability Maturity Model It is a methodology used to develop and refine an organization's software development process. SMART Metric A smart metric stands for specific, measurable, achievable or acceptable, realistic, and time specific or trackable. Time based Realistic Achievable Measurable Specific Risk Management Risk Management It is the process of identifying, assessing, monitoring, and controlling events arising from risks. Risk Management Risk cannot be removed but it can be minimized to an acceptable level. Risk Management Process Analyze: Assess the risk Action: Develop a risk management plan Monitor: Implement risk management actions Control: Reevaluate the risk Identify: Identify the risk Quantitative Risk Analysis It is a technique used to assess the effect of risk exposure events on overall organizational objectives. Quantitative Risk Analysis Calculates absolute financial values Assists in measuring the magnitude of impact Enables business to prioritize risks Quantitative Risk Analysis Uses different risk scenarios and ranks threats Is based on expert judgment, intuition, and experience Provides initial assessment to identify risks Considers organization culture, reputation, and brand image Ranks risks based on severity Risk Management Methods Risk Mitigation: Implement measures to eliminate vulnerabilities Risk Transfer: Transfer the risks to another entity Risk avoidance: Eliminate activities that involve risks Risk acceptance: Make decisions to live with the risks Risk Management methods are: Key Risk Indicator and Key Performance Indicator Metrics Measurement KPIs KRIs Performance Assessment Risk Assessment Analytics Decision Making Key Performance Indicator is a quantifiable metric that reflects how well an organization is achieving its stated goals and objectives. Key Risk Indicators are metrics used by organizations to provide an early signal of increasing risk exposure in various areas of the enterprise. Key Performance Indicator Measures the performance of security controls Provides a high-level overview of the past performance Key Risk Indicator Is selected for its impact on the senior leaders’ decisions Serves as an early warning indicator Risk IT Framework It is a framework based on a set of guiding principles featuring business processes and management guidelines. Business Process Assurance Supply Chain Supply Chain It is a system of organizations, people, activities, information, and resources involved in moving product to customer. Supply Chain Management (SCM) It is an expansive and complex undertaking that relies on each partner; from suppliers to manufacturers. Supply Chain Risk Management (SCRM) It is the implementation of strategies to manage both everyday and exceptional risks. Supply Chain Risks Compromised software or hardware purchased from suppliers Vulnerabilities in supply chain management or supplier systems Third-party service providers or vendors Poor Information Security practices by lower-tier suppliers Third-party data storage or data aggregators Counterfeit hardware or hardware with embedded malware The supply chain risks are: Supply Chain Countermeasures Presence of robust IT security solutions internally Compliance and governance Certification of international standards Supplier Management Controls It is the process whereby companies monitor and manage interactions with all external parties with which they have a relationship. Personnel Management Personnel Management It refers to planning, organizing, compensation, integration, and maintenance of people for the purpose of contributing to organizational, individual, and societal goals. Personnel Management Skills Responsibility Roles Organizational Culture Case Study: AWS Outage Problem Statement: In May 2017, Amazon faced a big A.W.S. outage that took down a bunch of large internet sites for several hours on a Tuesday afternoon. Case Study: AWS Outage Cause of the problem: In a blog post, the company said that one of its employees was debugging an issue with the billing system and accidentally took more servers offline than intended. That error started a domino effect that took down two other server subsystems and so on. Case Study: AWS Outage This case illustrates the importance of change management and internal governance in organizations. Common IS Program Challenges Inadequate management support Inadequate staffing Inadequate funding Key Takeaways Information security governance is the set of responsibilities and practices exercised by the board and executive management. Risk management is the process of identifying, assessing, monitoring, and controlling events arising from risks. The information security program consists of controls, processes, and practices to increase the resilience of the computing environment. All rights reserved. Lesson 4-1: Troubleshooting Methodologies Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Discuss troubleshooting methodologies. • Explain the bottom-to-top and top-to-bottom OSI troubleshooting models. • Describe how Divide-and-Conquer applies to troubleshooting. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The Troubleshooting Process • Troubleshooting should be a methodical process. • Haphazard guesses are more likely to make a problem worse than better. • When presented with a troubleshooting scenario, use these steps to maximize your chance of resolving the situation in minimal time. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 1. Identify the Problem • Gather information and Question Users • Get as much information as possible from users, from system logs, and from your own observation. • Check the scope of the problem – is it unique to one device, one subnet, one application, or one type of network service? • Duplicate the problem, if possible • Don’t rely on user information alone – users are often mistaken about what exactly is happening, especially with sporadic problems. • Duplicating the problem is the best way to confirm the nature and scope of the problem and to establish a reliable baseline for testing. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 1. Identify the Problem (contd.) • Identify Symptoms • Document symptoms which are clearly related to the problem, for example specific error messages, missing network resources, etc. • Determine if anything has changed • Many (perhaps most) sudden problems occur because something changed. • Was new hardware added, locally or on the network? • Did any software or settings change? • Tracing any changes which occurred when the network problem appeared (recently or before) is often the fastest route to a solution. • Approach multiple problems individually • Multiple symptoms, even when they appear nearly simultaneously, can be confusing or even misleading – focus on one set of symptoms at a time and trace them to their root cause Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 2. Establish a Theory of Probable Cause • Question the obvious! • How long has this problem been happening? • What were you doing when the error first happened? • Is your computer on? • Is your network connected? • Can you access other network resources? • Are other users having the same problem? Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 2. Establish a Theory of Probable Cause (contd.) • Consider multiple troubleshooting approaches to establish a theory of what’s wrong: • Bottom-to-Top OSI Model • Is the physical connection OK? (layer 1) • Do we have a data link? (link indicator) • Do we have an IP address? • Can we browse the Internet or other network resources? • Are any applications working? (HTTP, Mail, ICMP/Ping) • Top-to-Bottom OSI Model 1 - Physical 2 - Data Link 3 - Network 4 - Transport 5 - Session 6 - Presentation 7 -Application Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Troubleshooting Approaches (contd.) • Divide-and-Conquer: How can you split the scope of the problem into two pieces, to determine which piece has the problem? • Test one subnet (disconnect if needed). • Move the faulty device to a different part of the network. • Try connecting to other network resources. • Try alternate software. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 3. Testing Your Theory • Once you have a theory on the cause of the problem, how do you prove it? • Think about what ELSE must happen if your theory is true. • Possible ways to prove your theory: • Replace part • Change setting • Swap computers • Change user accounts/login credentials • Once your theory is confirmed, what is your next step to resolve the problem? • If your theory is not confirmed, re-establish a new theory or escalate the problem Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. 4. Implement and Verify • Establish a plan of action to resolve the problem and identify potential effects. • Include appropriate vendors, contractors, and stakeholders as necessary. • Request and receive any appropriate approvals. • Implement the solution or escalate as necessary • Verify full system functionality and, if applicable, implement preventative measures • Document findings, actions, and outcomes • Inform users and stakeholders of any changes in equipment or recommended operating procedures. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. A user reports a network connectivity problem. Which of the following steps should the technician perform FIRST? 1 Determine the probable cause Implement the solution of the cause Identify the problem Test the theory of the cause Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. A user reports a network connectivity problem. Which of the following steps should the technician perform FIRST? The first step in troubleshooting is to identify the problem. c. Determine the probable cause Implement the solution of the cause Identify the problem Test the theory of the cause 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Splitting the scope of the problem into two parts is called: 2 Subnetting Divide and Conquer Identifying the problem Implement and Verify Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Splitting the scope of the problem into two parts is called: Divide-and-Conquer is a troubleshooting methodology that involves splitting the scope of the problem into two parts. b. Subnetting Divide and Conquer Identifying the problem Implement and Verify 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Troubleshooting should be a methodical process. • The troubleshooting process starts with getting as much information as possible from users, from system logs, and from your own observation. • An important part of troubleshooting is determining if anything has changed recently. • The bottom-to-top OSI troubleshooting model starts with verifying physical layer connections. • The Divide-and-Conquer troubleshooting approach involves splitting the scope of the problem into two pieces, to determine which piece has the problem. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Troubleshooting Tools’. This concludes ‘Troubleshooting Methodologies’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 4: Trouble Shooting CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 4-2: Troubleshooting Tools Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Discuss the use of ipconfig, nbstat, nslookup, and arp command line utilities. • Differentiate between ping and ping6. • Explain the benefits of using pathping over tracert. • Define line testers, multimeters, and toner probes and discuss their use in network troubleshooting. • List various diagnostic websites. • Explain the function of a looking glass site. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Troubleshooting Tools • Your best tools for troubleshooting will always be your own eyes, hands, and brain. • Other tools, both software and hardware, are essential to provide information and verify troubleshooting theories. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Command Line Tools • ipconfig – displays current TCP/IP address, subnet, gateway, and other information • ipconfig /all – displays information for all local network interfaces Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Command Line Tools (contd.) • netstat – displays current network connection statistics and information Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Command Line Tools (contd.) • ifconfig – used on Unix-based systems, including Mac OSX, to display or configure TCP/IP network interface parameters. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Command Line Tools (contd.) • Ping tests to see if a given machine or address is accessible • Ping <address> or Ping <machinename> sends an ICMP packet to the designated address or machine name and returns a response if found. • Ping6 is similar to ping for IPv6 networks • Ping -6 is needed to ping a machine name (not an address) on some systems Note: ping continues indefinitely until you enter Ctrl+C Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Command Line Tools (contd.) • tracert is similar to ping but returns a response from each router or device (“hop”) between the source and destination machines. • “tracert” on Windows machines; “traceroute” on Linux/OSX machines • Also has tracert6 and tracert -6 options similar to Ping. o ping/ping6/ping -6 o tracert/tracert -6/traceroute6/traceroute -6 • pathping combines the functionality of both ping and tracert, displaying statistics about each node between your device and the destination over time. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Command Line Tools (contd.) • nbtstat – used on Windows machines to show information from the NetBIOS cache • nslookup – used to display information from DNS servers (“name server lookup”) • arp – used to display the arp cache on the local machine • “arp –hostname” displays the known IP and MAC address of the host if known • “arp –a” displays all contents of the arp cache Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. MAC Address Lookup • Using a command line tool like “arp” may show you the MAC address of a connected device. • How can you tell what sort of device that is? By using a MAC address lookup table. • Websites that offer free MAC address lookup services include: • Whatsmyip.org • Wireshark.org • Macvendors.com Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Physical Tools • Line testers • Include tools that simply check continuity as well as tools that verify correct pin connections • Also known as cable testers • Certifiers • Include line testing but also certifies the line conditions to meet Category 3, 5, 5e, etc. requirements. • Multimeter • Measures electrical resistance, voltage, and current. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Physical Tools (contd.) • Light meter (aka Optical Power Meter) – measures the power level output from a fiber optic connection. • Toner probe – used to trace wires through a building, a toner probe works by attaching a transmitter (“tone generator”) to the wire on one end and using a probe to detect the transmitted tone from the other end. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Diagnostic Websites • IP Checkers – provide your IP information and some basic connection tests • ipchicken.com, whatsmyip.com • DNS checks – check DNS records for a domain • mxtoolbox.com, dnsstuff.com • Speed test sites – measure the speed of your Internet connection • speedtest.net Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Diagnostic Websites • Looking glass sites – provide limited insight into a company’s router and Internet connections through tools like ping, tracert, and routing statistics. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Analyzers • Wi-Fi analyzer • device (or smartphone app) which provides details about nearby WLANS, including channel usage. • Protocol analyzer (aka packet analyzer/sniffer) • a device which intercepts and logs packet data to detect and analyze network problems Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which command line tool can display your IP address and subnet information? 1 ping tracert pathping ipconfig Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which command line tool can display your IP address and subnet information? ipconfig displays the local device's IP address and subnet information. d. ping tracert pathping ipconfig 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which tool can be used to trace wiring in a building? 2 Light meter Cable certifier Toner Probe Wi-Fi Analyzer Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which tool can be used to trace wiring in a building? A Toner Probe is used to trace wires in a building. c. Light meter Cable certifier Toner Probe Wi-Fi Analyzer 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • IPconfig is a command-line tool which displays the current TCP/IP address, subnet, gateway, and related information. • Ping and Ping6 send an ICMP packet to the designated address or machine name and returns a response if found. • A toner probe is used to trace wires through a building by attaching a transmitter (“tone generator”) to the wire on one end and using a probe to detect the transmitted tone from the other end. • Looking glass sites provide limited insight into a company’s router and Internet connections through tools like ping, tracert, and routing statistics. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Troubleshooting Wireless Issues’. This concludes ‘Troubleshooting Tools’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 4: Trouble Shooting CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 4-3: Troubleshooting Wireless Networks Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Describe three causes of signal loss. • Explain the problem caused by overlapping channels. • Define signal-to-noise ratio and its relationship to power levels. • Discuss the difference between bandwidth saturation and device saturation. • Explain the difference between thin access points and thick or fat access points, and the use of LWAPP in managing thin access points. • Describe the problems caused by having the wrong encryption type or wrong antenna type. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Troubleshooting Wireless • WLANS often benefit more from troubleshooting and optimization than wired LANs. • WLAN speed can be affected more than wired LANs. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Wireless Basics • Throughput – a measure of the speed data travels on the connection. • Frequency – the radio wavelengths used by a given wireless connection. • Channels – predefined blocks of frequencies • In the 2.4GHz band up to 14 channels are defined (11 usable in the US). • In the 5GHz band the available standard 20MHz channels vary by country, but 23 are available in the US. • Some access points can use “fatter” channels of 40, 80, or 120MHz for more throughput. • Distance – how far the wireless device is from the wireless access point (AP). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Signal Loss • Signal loss is a weak or non-existent wireless signal, and may be caused by: • Distance • Environmental factors, especially concrete/brick walls or metal studs • Interference, especially from other devices in the 2.4GHz band • Consider repositioning your AP for better signal coverage, or adding an additional AP to compensate for environmental barriers. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Interference • Signal interference can significantly decrease overall throughput by forcing APs and clients to retransmit corrupted frames. • In the 2.4GHz band (802.11b, g, ac, and sometimes n) interference can come from other electronics which use this spectrum, including Bluetooth, cordless phones, and microwave ovens. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Channel Issues • Overlapping Channels • In the 2.4GHz band there are 11 usable channels, but each channel overlaps 2-4 adjacent channels. • For an optimal signal without interferences, channels should be chosen which do not overlap other nearby APs. • In 802.11n and 802.11ac, fatter channels can be used to increase bandwidth, but these can be more likely to overlap. • Mismatched channels – with certain settings APs and clients can be forced into using different channels (e.g. 3 and 4). While some signaling may work, mismatched channels are unlikely to be usable. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Signal, Noise, and Bounce • Wireless APs transmit at a certain power level. • Increasing the power (if possible) can increase distance and potentially reduce interference. • The Signal-to-Noise Ratio (SNR) is a measurement of the intended signal from a wireless device compared with the normal background noise, measured in decibels (db). • 10-15db is the minimum acceptable • 25-40db is good • 41db+ is excellent • Increasing transmit power can improve SNR. • Higher power signals can also bounce off walls and other surfaces, increasing range but also creating multiple signals (multipath propagation/degradation) and may cause clients to connect to a distant AP rather than a nearby one. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Saturation • Device Saturation is when a given AP or device is overwhelmed with too many connections. • Bandwidth Saturation is when too many devices are trying to use the same frequencies, overwhelming the available bandwidth. • Adding more Access Points, at different bands, can solve saturation effects. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Thin vs. Thick • “Thick” or “Fat” wireless access points handle management, security, authentication, and the connection to the wired switch. • “Thin” access points offload most of the management functions to a separate, shared WLAN Controller via LWAPP (Lightweight Access Point Protocol). • “Thin” access points may be less likely to experience device saturation, BUT overworking the WLAN Controller is still possible. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Other Wireless Issues • Rogue Access Point – an AP within range of your wireless clients which uses the same SSID in an attempt to gain access to those devices, possibly for a man-in-the-middle attack. • Open Networks – using an AP with no encryption set at all. Besides leaving your network more vulnerable, open access points make it easy for intruders to spy on packets sent by any device connected to the open AP. • Wrong SSID – often caused when an AP is replaced and the new SSID is manually set and mistyped. • Wrong Encryption – If an AP is set with the wrong encryption, it could mean clients connect at too low a speed or not at all. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Antennas • Different antennas serve different purposes. • Omnidirectional antennas radiate a signal in all directions, but generally along a horizontal plane. • Directional antennas create a “cone” of signal in a specific direction. • When clients are unable to “see” an Access Point, consider whether the antenna on the client or the AP may be incorrectly configured. • MIMO technologies can make use of multiple device antennas to increase throughput. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Untested Updates • Updating Access Points and wireless devices with newer software and firmware generally improves their performance and security. • However, updates are not perfect and may cause unintended consequences. • Testing updates on sample equipment to verify performance before rolling them out to the entire network is a good idea. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of the following is NOT a possible environmental cause of signal loss? 1 Distance Concrete Interference Overlapping channels Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Overlapping channels can degrade throughput but is not an environmental issue and does not cause signal loss. d. Distance Concrete Interference Overlapping channels 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of these is a problem created when an access point is overwhelmed with too many connections? 2 Bandwidth Saturation Device Saturation Overlapping Channels Thick Access Point Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which of these is a problem created when an access point is overwhelmed with too many connections? Device saturation is when an access point is overwhelmed with too many connections. b. Bandwidth Saturation Device Saturation Overlapping Channels Thick Access Point 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of the following is an AP within range of your wireless clients which uses the same SSID in an attempt to gain access to those devices? 3 Man-in-the-middle Open Network Wrong SSID Rogue AP Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which of the following is an AP within range of your wireless clients which uses the same SSID in an attempt to gain access to those devices? A rogue access point is an AP within range of your wireless clients which uses the same SSID in an attempt to gain access to those devices. d. Man-in-the-middle Open Network Wrong SSID Rogue AP 3 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • WLANS often benefit more from troubleshooting and optimization than wired LANs. • Frequency refers to the radio wavelengths used by a given wireless connection, and Channels are predefined blocks of frequencies. • Signal interference can significantly decrease overall throughput by forcing APs and clients to retransmit corrupted frames. • The Signal-to-Noise Ratio (SNR) is a measurement of the intended signal from a wireless device compared with the normal background noise, measured in decibels (db). • A Rogue Access Point is an AP within range of your wireless clients which uses the same SSID in an attempt to gain access to those devices, possibly for a man-in-the-middle attack. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Troubleshooting Copper Cabling ’. This concludes ‘Troubleshooting Wireless Networks’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 4: Trouble Shooting CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 4-4: Troubleshooting Copper Cabling Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Define shorts, opens, and crosstalk as it applies to network cabling. • Discuss EMI/RFI and its effect on copper cabling. • List the maximum recommended distances for each category of Ethernet cabling. • Explain the likely symptoms of split pairs or Tx/Rx reversed wiring. • Describe some possible causes of a bad GBIC or bad SFP. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Basic Copper Problems • Shorts – a condition when two copper wires are touching each other, creating one combined circuit. • Opens – a condition when there is a break or gap in the wiring, preventing any signal from passing through. • Incorrect Termination – mismatched wire pairs Standard End Crossover End Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Crosstalk • Crosstalk is when a signal transmitted on one circuit or wire pair affects the signal transmitted on another circuit or wire pair. • In Ethernet cables crosstalk often occurs due to EMI generated by one wire pair influencing the signal on another wire pair. • Crosstalk can be minimized by: • Using twisted-pair cables (and maintaining the twist ratio) • Using shielded cables • Separating cables. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. EMI and RFI • EMI/RFI – Electromagnetic Interference or radio- frequency interference, signal distortion caused by electromagnetic induction or electromagnetic radiation from an external source. • To mitigate EMI/RFI signal problems: • Use twisted-pair cabling • Use shielded cabling • Be mindful of cable placement - avoid running cable near EMI/RFI point sources such as lighting fixtures, electrical panels, and any radio transmitters. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Distance Limitations • Always remember copper cabling has a limited recommended distance. • Beyond the recommended distance, signal degradation and attenuation (Db loss) can cause packet loss or render the signal unusable. • For category 3, 5, 5e, and 6a cables the maximum recommended distance is 100m. • For category 6 cables the maximum distance is 55m. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bad Connectors and Wiring • Bad connectors are problematic – they may work most of the time but fail sporadically. • Bad wiring can cause unexpected packet loss and signal degradation. • Testing with a Cable Certifier is a good way to find bad connectors and bad wiring. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Split pairs and Tx/Rx Reverse • What would happen if you swapped wires 1 and 3 on both ends of a EIA/TIA568b wired connector? • It will work, but not correctly. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Split pairs and Tx/Rx Reverse (contd.) • This is known as a Split Pair, where the pins are wired correctly but not in pairs. • Without the EMI/RFI protection of the twisted pairs, signal degradation is very likely. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Split pairs and Tx/Rx Reverse (contd.) • What would happen if the Transmit and Receive wires in a pair are inadvertently swapped? • Depending on the connected device, this may be auto-sensed as a crossover cable and may work correctly. Or it may not work at all. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bad GBIC/SFP • GBIC (Gigabit Interface Converter) and SFP (Small Factor Pluggable, a smaller type of gigabit Ethernet controller) convert gigabit Ethernet from a switch or router into a high speed connection over fiber optic cables or other connections. • Problems with GBIC or SFP modules may be caused by foreign objects in the GBIC slot, by problems with the cables connected to the GBIC, or by a faulty or incompatible GBIC module. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. In copper cabling, an 'Open' is: 1 a condition when two copper wires are touching each other, creating one combined circuit a condition when there is a break or gap in the wiring, preventing any signal from passing through a condition where wire pairs are mismatched when a signal transmitted on one circuit or wire pair affects the signal transmitted on another circuit or wire pair Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • An Open is a condition when there is a break or gap in the wiring, preventing any signal from passing through. • Crosstalk is when a signal transmitted on one circuit or wire pair affects the signal transmitted on another circuit or wire pair, and it can be minimized by using twisted pair cabling, by using shielded cabling, and by keeping cables separated. • EMI/RFI stands for electromagnetic interference or radio-frequency interference, which is signal distortion caused by electromagnetic induction or electromagnetic radiation from an external source. • A split pair in twisted-pair cabling is when the connector wiring matches up but the wire pairs are not in the correct locations. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Troubleshooting Fiber Cabling’. This concludes ‘Troubleshooting Copper Cabling’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 4: Trouble Shooting CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 4-5: Troubleshooting Fiber Cabling Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Explain bend radius limitations and their effect on fiber cabling. • List distance limitations of common types of fiber cabling. • Describe wavelength, fiber type, and connector mismatches. • Discuss the possible causes and effects of a bad SFP/GBIC. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Basic Fiber Problems • Bend Radius Limitations – fiber cabling is more fragile than copper and can break or fail if the wire is twisted or bent beyond its stated bend radius limitation. • Dirty connectors – fiber connections must transmit light without undue refraction or distortion, and so are more susceptible to dirty connectors on cables or switch/router ports. • Distance limitations – although generally much longer than copper, fiber cabling will suffer from signal attenuation (Db loss) if used beyond its recommended maximum distance: • 100baseFX: 2km • 10GbaseSR: 400m • 10GbaseER: 40km • 10GbaseSW: 300m Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Fiber Mismatches • A Fiber type mismatch occurs when two different types of fiber cabling are used on the same segment (e.g. Splicing single-mode and multimode or multimode with different sized cores). • As much as 99% of the signal can be lost in a fiber type mismatch! • A wavelength mismatch most often occurs with single strand fiber cabling, which can accommodate transmitting and receiving at the same time on different wavelengths. To work properly one end must terminate in a 1310/1550 media converter and the other end with a 1550/1310 media converter. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Fiber Mismatches (contd.) • A connector mismatch occurs when trying to connect a fiber cable of one type to switch ports of another type. • Purchasing cables to match your equipment (and installation tools) is critical with fiber! Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Bad GBIC/SFP • GBIC (Gigabit Interface Converter) and SFP (Small Factor Pluggable, a smaller type of gigabit Ethernet controller) convert gigabit Ethernet from a switch or router into a high speed connection over fiber optic cables (or other connections). • Problems with GBIC or SFP modules may be caused by foreign objects in the GBIC slot, by problems with the cables connected to the GBIC, or by a faulty or incompatible GBIC module. • Specific GBIC or SFP modules must match the type of fiber cabling being used. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which fiber type is best for a cabling run of over 10km? 1 100baseFX 10GbaseSR 10GbaseER 10GbaseSW Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Which fiber type is best for a cabling run of over 10km? 10GbaseER (extended range) has a maximum recommended distance of 40km. c. 100baseFX 10GbaseSR 10GbaseER 10GbaseSW 1 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Your fiber cable has a broken optical core. What is the most likely cause? 2 Connector mismatch Dirty connector Exceeded the bend radius limitation Fiber type mismatch Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ The correct answer is a. b. c. d. Your fiber cable has a broken optical core. What is the most likely cause? The bend radius limitation is the maximum you can bend or twist a fiber cable before it breaks. c. Connector mismatch Dirty connector Exceeded the bend radius limitation Fiber type mismatch 2 Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Fiber cabling is more fragile than copper and can break or fail if the wire is twisted or bent beyond its stated bend radius. • A Fiber type mismatch occurs when two different types of fiber cabling are used on the same segment (e.g. Splicing single-mode and multimode or multimode with different sized cores). • A connector mismatch occurs when trying to connect a fiber cable of one type to switch ports or GBIC ports of another type. • Purchasing cables to match your equipment (and installation tools) is critical with fiber. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Troubleshooting Common Network Issues’. This concludes ‘Troubleshooting Fiber Cabling’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 4: Trouble Shooting CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 4-6: Troubleshooting Common Network Issues Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Discuss the likely symptoms of incorrect IP configuration. • Describe the probable effects of misconfigured DHCP or DNS. • Explain the problem of broadcast storms. • Discuss interface errors such as mismatched duplex or speed. • Describe a situation which can cause a problem with end-to-end connectivity. • List network discovery protocols. • Explain what is meant by NIC teaming misconfiguration. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Basic IP Problems • Incorrect IP Configuration – if the IP address, Gateway, subnet mask, or DNS server configuration for a host is incorrect, they may find it impossible to communicate. This is easily checked via the network interface or ipconfig. • Link-Local – if the IP address is a link-local or APIPA address (e.g. 169.254.0.1 or similar), the device is not connected to a DHCP server or the server’s scope is exhausted. • Duplicate IP – two devices on the same subnet with the same IP may happen when one or both uses a static IP or when a DHCP server is reset. One or both devices will be unable to communicate until the situation is resolved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Misconfigured DHCP • Your DHCP server provides IP configuration settings to DHCP- enabled clients on the network. Common DHCP problems include: • DHCP misconfiguration – where the DHCP server is programmed to give out unusable subnet, DHCP, or gateway information. • Rogue DHCP – when a second DHCP server begins handling some DHCP requests on the network, often due to a rogue router. • Scope exhaustion – when the DHCP server has exhausted the available IP addresses in its designated scope. DHCP DHCP Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Misconfigured DNS • DNS issues can easily be tested with PING – if a device can PING to an IP address but cannot PING to a hostname, it indicates the IP network is OK but DNS name resolution is not working. Possible causes: • Manually set DNS server is incorrect. • DHCP-supplied DNS server is incorrect. • DNS server is not resolving properly. • Manually setting DNS to 8.8.8.8 and 8.8.4.4 (Google’s free public DNS servers) can be a good test. • Symptoms of misconfigured DNS: Unable to browse some or all websites, applications perform erratically when trying to access named servers or other resources. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Broadcast Storms vs. Jabber • A broadcast storm is an overwhelming number of useless packets being sent through network infrastructure. • Can be caused by a switching loop (multiple routes between two or more switches, not port aggregation via LACP). • Network traffic will be extremely slow or unreliable until the storm is resolved. • Jabber is a network disturbance caused by a faulty NIC or switch/router port. • Jabber is usually an electrical disturbance, not legitimate network traffic, and is usually stopped at a switch port. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Simultaneous Wired/Wireless Connections • It’s not uncommon for laptop (and some other) users to have both wired and wireless connections to the network. • This does not improve the speed of their connection since only one interface will be used for any particular session. • If the interfaces are configured (statically or dynamically) for different gateways or DNS servers, the user may experience random, sporadic differences in connections or even outages if one is configured improperly. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Interface Errors: Speed, Duplex, and VLAN Misconfiguration • Connections to a switch or router are generally set to auto- sense the speed and duplex of the connecting device by default. • Manually configuring speed, duplex, and other interface settings can improve speed when auto-sense is incorrect, but may also lead to interface incompatibilities now or in the future. • Remember switch ports may be assigned to specific VLANs as well, so connecting devices intended for a different VLAN will cause connection problems or interface errors. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. End-to-End Connectivity • Connections may involve numerous intermediary devices – switches, bridges, routers, etc. • To maintain a given throughput ALL components must meet the minimum criteria. • Example: NIC – Category 5e cable – switch – Category 3 cable – switch – Category 5e cable – router • The Cat3 cable will limit the end-to-end throughput to 10Mbps • MTU black hole – when an intermediate router’s MTU (maximum transmit unit) is too small to accommodate packets sent by a previous router. • Firewall black hole – when a firewall is dropping packets intended for a specific address or network. • Missing IP routes – when a routing path attempts to use routes which do not exist. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Network Discovery Issues • If you find you can ping or access network devices using their IP address, but cannot see or access them by their network name, a network discovery protocol is the most likely culprit. • Network discovery and naming protocols include: • NetBIOS – used by default on Windows computers, also available on other devices, uses a local cache or hosts file or a special broadcast to resolve names. • WINS – Windows Internet Name Service, a server-based database of local machine names • DNS – Domain Name Services, the protocol which resolves domain names on the Internet (and can be used internally as well) • Bonjour – protocol primarily used by Apple computers Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. NIC Teaming Misconfiguration • NIC Teaming is a function to combine two or more Network Interfaces for the purposes of load- balancing or failover. • NIC Teams can be created as: • Active-active: Both NICs are active and being used • Active-passive: One NIC is active, the other is on standby in case the first NIC fails. • The NIC Team is either configured with a multicast address (packets are sent to all involved NICs – if they are joined to the multicast address) or a broadcast address (all NICs, including those not in the team, receive the packet). • NIC Teaming misconfiguration occurs when one or more NICs are not connected to the same network, or are not joined to the multicast address. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Physical Issues • Cable Placement – running copper cables near EMI/RFI sources can degrade performance or cause sporadic communication issues. • Power failure/anomalies – power outages obviously affect all IT equipment, but special concerns with networks include: • Power sequencing issues – problems caused when certain network components’ power on are out of order (e.g. endpoints before DHCP server). • Power anomalies – if power levels fluctuate, it can cause network transmissions to become garbled or unstable. • Hardware failure – of course, hardware failure is a standard part of any IT project, including networks. Replacement components should be maintained to prevent a single point of failure. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Suddenly some computers on a network are unable to communicate because their IP address and gateway information does not match the rest of the network. What is the most likely cause? 1 Scope exhaustion Rogue DHCP Static IP misconfiguration Broadcast Storm Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. What is the most likely cause? 1 Scope exhaustion Rogue DHCP Static IP misconfiguration Broadcast Storm With a rogue DHCP server some clients will acquire DNS from the rogue AP while others acquire from the standard DHCP. b Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. What must be true of the networks in order for the router to function properly? 2 Must be on the same WAN Must be in the same collision domain. Must be in the same broadcast domain Must have distinctly different addressing schemes. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The correct answer is A router connects two networks. What must be true of the networks in order for the router to function properly? 2 Must be on the same WAN Must be in the same collision domain Must be in the same broadcast domain Must have distinctly different addressing schemes. Routers connect different networks -- each must have a different addressing scheme. d Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The correct answer is An overwhelming number of useless packets being sent through network infrastructure is called _____________ . 3 Jabber MTU black hole Power anomalies Broadcast Storm A broadcast storm is an overwhelming number of useless packets being sent through network infrastructure, often caused by a switching loop. d Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Incorrect IP Configuration – if the IP address, Gateway, subnet mask, or DNS server configuration for a host is incorrect, they may find it impossible to communicate. • DHCP misconfiguration is when a DHCP server is programmed to give out unusable subnet, DHCP, or gateway information. • Manually configuring speed, duplex, and other interface settings on a switch or router can improve speed when auto-sense is incorrect, but may also lead to interface incompatibilities now or in the future. • NIC Teaming misconfiguration occurs when one or more teamed NICs are not connected to the same network, or are not joined to the multicast address. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Troubleshooting Common Security Issues’. This concludes ‘Troubleshooting Common Network Issues’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 4: Trouble Shooting CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 4-7: Troubleshooting Common Security Issues Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Discuss the security vulnerabilities related to misconfigured firewalls, ACLs, and applications. • Define a Denial of Service (DoS) attack. • Describe the Ping of Death attack. • Explain the risk associated with default passwords and backdoor access. • Identify the difference between trusted and untrusted users. • Define jamming as it relates to wireless networks. • Discuss the security implications of firmware and OS patches. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Security Problems 101 • Security issues fall into three categories: • Someone has access where they shouldn’t. • Someone doesn’t have access where they should. • Defending the network from malicious attacks. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Malicious Users • Malicious users seek to damage the network or to improperly use the organization’s resources for personal gain. • Untrusted users are those outside the organization with no valid access to any private part of the network. • Trusted users are generally those inside the organization or who have valid credentials to access some portion of the network. • Trusted malicious users are a great risk since they have more opportunities to gain access to the network, such as planting backdoor accounts or connecting a packet sniffer to an unprotected switch. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Firewall Configuration Issues • Firewall misconfiguration manifests in one of the two ways: • Traffic is allowed that should be blocked. • Traffic is blocked that should be allowed (maybe all). • Firewall rules explicitly allow or deny traffic from specific IP addresses and/or ports, and packet content in some cases, so reviewing the rules should show the problem. • Remember that rules are processed in order – lower rules may not apply if a higher rule’s criteria is met. • Remember the “Implicit Deny” rule – adding an explicit deny may help with logging and troubleshooting. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Other Configuration Issues • ACL misconfiguration: similar to a Firewall, the ACL allows or denies traffic based on a set of rules. • ACL rules are usually stateless – they can only be based on IP address or port. • Just like a firewall ACL rules generally include an implicit deny. • Application misconfiguration occurs when an application – especially applications which must be exposed through the firewall – do not have proper restrictions in place and could allow users access to other secure resources. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Edge Issues The edge or border is where your LAN interacts with the WAN. Edge issues can include: • Denial of Service (DoS or DDoS) – an intentional or unintentional disruption of service due to overwhelming traffic to a server or network device. • DDoS attacks can be mitigated with the use of a proxy server and/or help from your WAN vendor. • Ping of Death – a special type of DoS attack using a malformed ping packet which, when reassembled can cause buffer overflows or system crashes on the receiving server. Ping of Death is routinely filtered out by firewalls and ISPs today. • Open/Closed ports – open ports allow packets to flow to or from a device, while closed ports drop traffic to the device. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Edge Issues (contd.) • Unreachable default gateway – if your default gateway (router) is unreachable, traffic can’t flow to or from the WAN. • An ICMP command, route redirect, can be used to redirect traffic from a default gateway to an alternate gateway (presumably under the attacker’s control) to be used as a “man-in-the-middle” style attack. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Authentication Issues (TACACS/RADIUS Misconfiguration) • TACACS+ and RADIUS are forms of Authentication, Authorization, and Accounting (AAA) servers that verify users before allowing them access to certain network resources (APs, VPNs, switches, etc.) • AAA solutions involve three elements – a client (requesting access), a supplicant (the device the client is connecting to), and the server. • AAA misconfiguration can occur when: • Client and server are using different ports • Client and server are not using the correct pre-shared key (PSK) • Supplicant is configured for the wrong RADIUS or TACACS+ server group • User isn’t configured on the AAA server • Some AAA servers also include a default user and password – make sure this is changed so it’s not available to an unauthorized user. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Backdoor Access • Many devices (routers, servers, switches) are configured with default administrator accounts. • These accounts should be disabled or changed to prevent unauthorized use. • In some cases temporary users with access to administrative credentials may plant their own username and password onto a system for their own future unauthorized use (backdoor access). Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. ARP Cache Poisoning • ARP – Address Resolution Protocol, used to translate IP addresses into MAC addresses. • ARP Cache – a table each device builds and maintains which matches IP addresses to MAC addresses based on ARP packets received (not just ARP packets requested). • ARP Cache Poisoning is a technique by which a local machine sends ARP packets to redirect IP packets intended for another device to itself or to another host. • Only works on the local segment • Also called ARP Spoofing or ARP Poison Routing Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Banner Grabbing/OUI • Banners are messages generated by a router, firewall, or other network device in response to an error. • Organizationally Unique Identifiers (OUI) are the first 24 bits of a MAC address and identify the manufacturer of the device. • By using protocols such as telnet or SSH attackers can try to reach key network components. Even if unsuccessful, the information gleaned from the banner or from the OUI can provide the hacker with important information regarding the type of device so they can research and exploit any known weaknesses. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain/Local Group Configuration • On an Active Directory network, Domain Local groups are a type of user group which can assign access to users who are outside of the local domain. • Improperly configuring a domain local group or assigning a trusted user to a domain local group may give them access to network resources beyond what was intended. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Jamming • Jamming is a wireless technique to block access to certain frequencies by flooding the airwaves with a powerful signal. • It can be used in an “evil twin” style attack where the attacker sets up their own AP on a different channel than the organization’s APs, then jams the frequencies of the real APs. • Wireless clients will not be able to “see” the real APs and thus will connect to the rogue AP instead. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Patches and Malware • Firmware and Operating System patches are often used to close vulnerabilities that could allow an intruder access to your equipment. • Malware protection is important for any PC or Server, and malware definitions are often updated daily to include recently discovered strains of known malware and viruses. • Keeping your patches and malware definitions up to date helps to prevent intruders from exploiting your systems. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. A user inside the organization who has valid credentials is a ___________ . 1 Trusted User Untrusted User Malicious User Domain Local Group Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The correct answer is A user inside the organization who has valid credentials is a ___________ . 1 Trusted User Untrusted User Malicious User Domain Local Group A trusted user is a user inside the organization who has valid credentials. a Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. What is the Ping of Death? 2 a command line utility a broadcast storm a side effect of the implicit deny rule a type of DoS attack Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The correct answer is What is the Ping of Death? 2 a command line utility a broadcast storm a side effect of the implicit deny rule a type of DoS attack Ping of Death is a special type of Denial of Service (DoS) attack using a malformed ping packet. d Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • Trusted users are generally those inside the organization or who have valid credentials to access some portion of the network. • Firewall misconfiguration manifests in either traffic being allowed that should be blocked or traffic being blocked that should be allowed (sometimes all). • Ping of Death – a special type of DoS attack using a malformed ping packet which, when reassembled can cause buffer overflows or system crashes on the receiving server. • Jamming is a wireless technique to block access to certain frequencies by flooding the airwaves with a powerful signal. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Troubleshooting Common WAN Issues’. This concludes ‘Troubleshooting Common Security Issues’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 4: Trouble Shooting CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 4-8: Troubleshooting Common WAN Issues Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: • Define Customer Premise Equipment (CPE) and demarc. • Discuss how DNS issues, interference, and the split horizon issue can affect WAN connectivity. • Describe WAN issues specific to satellite connections. • Explain how company security policy can emulate a WAN issue. Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Troubleshooting Responsibility • WAN providers typically guarantee service up to a point known as the demarc. • Troubleshooting from the demarc to and through the internal LAN is the client’s responsibility. • Troubleshooting outside the demarc is the WAN provider’s responsibility. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Customer Premise Equipment (CPE) Demarc Smart Jack / NIU CSU/DSU CPE • CPE is the equipment owned by and maintained by the organization (also called DTE, data terminal equipment). • The WAN provider can run a loopback test up to the Smart Jack/NIU. • In some cases copper line drivers/repeaters are used to extend the demarc connection to another floor or building – in those cases the drivers/repeaters become another element in any troubleshooting. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Loss of Internet Connectivity • The most common WAN issue is probably loss of Internet connectivity. In those cases: • Check the WAN interface for errors. Link status may be accessible from the CSU/DSU panel. • DNS issues manifest when LAN devices can access external IP addresses but not external domain names. If the WAN providers’ DNS servers are not responding correctly, alternate DNS servers can be used for testing. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Loss of Internet Connectivity (contd.) • Misconfiguration between the CPE router and the CSU/DSU can also cause connectivity issues. • Verify speed and duplex. • Check the router WAN configuration settings and error log. • Interference can be an issue with wireless WAN connections. • Repositioning antennas or switching channels (where possible) may solve the issue. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Satellite Issues • Satellite WAN connections can involve additional troubleshooting steps. • Satellite links can be slow or non-existent during severe weather conditions such as storms or high wind. • Debris such as snow or leaves on the satellite dish can impede or block reception. • Satellite dishes need a clear line-of-sight to a compatible satellite. • Even when working properly, satellite WANs have much higher latency than other WAN types. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Fair Access Policy • Some WAN providers (especially satellite-based providers) implement a “Fair Access Policy” which limits or throttles bandwidth after an account has reached a preset download threshold. • Depending on the provider, the limit may be in place for 24 hours or until the next billing cycle. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Frame Relay - Split Horizon • Split Horizon is a technique to prevent routing loops. • Frame Relay WAN connections disable split horizon by default. • This is normal, but can cause problems for some protocols and tests. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Company Security Policy • In some cases a company’s security policy (implemented at a firewall or router) can mimic WAN issues. • For example, the policy may block access from certain applications or to certain sites. • The policy could also choose to throttle (limit) bandwidth on certain applications or ports, or to certain sites, rather than an outright block. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Quiz Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The point where the WAN provider's responsibility ends is called the ________ . 1 CPE Firewall Demarc Router Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The correct answer is The point where the WAN provider's responsibility ends is called the ________ . 1 CPE Firewall Demarc Router The demarc is the point that separates the WAN from the LAN. c Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. Which of the following is a symptom of a Fair Access Policy? 2 two-factor authentication for all users throttled WAN bandwidth load-balancing RADIUS server Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The correct answer is Which of the following is a symptom of a Fair Access Policy? 2 two-factor authentication for all users throttled WAN bandwidth load-balancing RADIUS server A Fair Access Policy from a WAN provider may throttle bandwidth after a preset download limit. b Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Here is a quick recap of what we have learned in this lesson. Summary • WAN providers typically guarantee service up to a point known as the demarc. • CPE is the LAN equipment owned by and maintained by the organization. • Misconfiguration between the CPE router and the CSU/DSU, such as speed or duplex settings, can also cause connectivity issues. • Even when working properly, satellite WANs have much higher latency than other WAN types. • Some WAN providers (especially satellite-based providers) implement a “Fair Access Policy” which limits or throttles bandwidth after an account has reached a preset download threshold. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. The next lesson is ‘Policies and Procedures’. This concludes ‘Troubleshooting Common WAN Issues’.

Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Domain 5: Standards and Best Practices CompTIA Network + Exam Prep (N10-006) Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Lesson 5-1: Policies and Procedures Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. After completing this lesson, you will be able to: ● Describe the role of Policies and Procedures in an organization ● Identify the different types of Security Policies ● Describe the use of ‘Consent to Monitoring’ clauses ● Explain Acceptable Use Policies of an organization ● Describe common standard business documents, including a Service Level Agreement, Memorandum of Understanding, Master Services Agreement, and Statement of Work Objectives Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Every organization needs Policies and Procedures for their users. • Policies communicate to users what behavior is expected and what behavior is not allowed, and create a legal foundation to take action against those users if the Policies are not followed. • Procedures define what steps will be taken in the event of a security breach or other serious issues. • NOT having well-defined Policies and Procedures leave users and administrators to decide for themselves what behavior is appropriate and what should be done to resolve issues, and the results are likely to be unpredictable. Policies and Procedures Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Security Policies Security Policies may include guidelines for: • Physical Security – access to the building, access to servers, and access to key network components. • Data and Document Security – this pertains to where important information is stored (both digitally and physically) and how data stored on mobiles, laptops, flash drives, printouts, and other media should be handled. • Network Security (Network Policies) – this pertains to defining levels of user access for sensitive areas of the network, password retention policies. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Consent to Monitoring A common part of Security Policies is a ‘Consent to Monitoring’ clause, which notifies the user that their activities on the organization’s computer, network, or website may be monitored. Consent to Monitoring clauses are also commonly included in online Terms and Conditions on websites and web applications. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Acceptable Use Policies An Acceptable Use Policy (AUP) is a set of rules governing how an organization’s network, website, and other computer systems should be used. • New employees or members are generally required to sign an Acceptable Use Policy as a condition of using the organization’s systems. • Failure to abide by the AUP can result in disciplinary actions and/or the termination of employment with a company. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Standard Business Documents – Service Level Agreement A Service Level Agreement (SLA) is an agreement defining the scope, quality, and responsibilities related to a service. • In the IT sector, an SLA is commonly used in a vendor/client relationship to detail the responsibilities of the vendor in providing a specific service. For example, the SLA for an Internet service provider might guarantee 99% uptime and a 2 hour outage response. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. Standard Business Documents– Memorandum of Understanding A Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) documents the agreed upon terms between two parties. • Less binding than a formal agreement or contract, an MOU is often the first step in documenting the relationship between two parties. Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. A Master Services Agreement (MSA) is a contract between two parties that specifies the terms of the relationship between the parties. • The MSA often details general areas such as payment terms, warranties, ownership of intellectual property, dispute resolution, and similar general items. • In IT relationships, an MSA is often used to establish the framework for transactions while each project is detailed in a specific Statement of Work. Standard Business Documents– Master Services Agreement Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. A Statement of Work (SOW) details the specific requirements and deliverables for a particular project. • The SOW generally includes pricing, delivery timetables, deliverables and/or activities, as well as general terms and conditions and criteria for acceptable quality standards. Standard Business Documents– Statement of Work Copyright 2015, Simplilearn. All rights reserved. QUIZ a. b. c. d. The clause commonly found in a security policy which informs the user that their activity may be monitored is called ________________ . 1 Acceptable Use Policy Master Services Agreement Consent to Monitoring Consent to Services Copyright 2015, Simplilearn.
